## σαβαχθάνι (id: 004420000000000)

σαβαχθάνι
=========

σαβαχθάνι (G4518) — σαβαχθανι

verb (Aramaic loanword)

35\.56 · Help, Care For · Desert, Forsake

to forsake an Aramaic word meaning: you have forsaken me Languages differ appreciably in expressions meaning ‘to forsake, to abandon.’ For example, the most appropriate equivalent in some instances is ‘to leave alone’ or ‘to leave behind.’ In other instances one may employ a phrase such as ‘to leave without help’ or ‘to leave and refuse to care for.’

[MAT 27:46](https://ref.ly/Matt27:46) · [MRK 15:34](https://ref.ly/Matt15:34)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:46; Mark 15:34


## Σαβαώθ (id: 004421000000000)

Σαβαώθ
======

Σαβαώθ (G4519)

noun\-name, m. \| indeclinable

12\.8{N:001} · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

Almighty, All Powerful, One who is powerful over all (a Greek transliteration of a Hebrew word meaning armies and used with κύριος\[a] Lord, [12\.9](#12.9), as a title for God) pertaining to one who has overwhelming power

[ROM 9:29](https://ref.ly/Acts9:29) · [JAS 5:4](https://ref.ly/Heb5:4)

1 Items [12\.4](#12.4)\-[12\.8](#12.8), ([12\.9](#12.9)) and [12\.12](#12.12) in this domain are titles for θεός\[a] God ([12\.1](#12.1)). As titles, they have precisely the same reference as θεός\[a], but they each contribute distinctive meanings which are legitimate qualifications of the referent in question.

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 9:29; James 5:4


## σαββατισμός (id: 004422000000000)

σαββατισμός
===========

σαββατισμός (G4520)

noun, m. \| \-οῦ \| σάββατον

67\.185 · Time · Definite Units of Time: Year, Month, Week, Day, Hour

a Sabbath rest, a period of rest (derivative of σάββατον\[a], [67\.184](#67.184)) a special religiously significant period for rest and worship

[HEB 4:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm4:9)

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 4:9


## σάββατον (id: 004423000000000)

σάββατον
========

σάββατον (G4521)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| προσάββατον · σαββατισμός

67\.184 · Time · Definite Units of Time: Year, Month, Week, Day, Hour

Sabbath, Saturday the seventh or last day of the week (religiously the most important since it was consecrated to the worship of God)

[MAT 12:1](https://ref.ly/Matt12:1) · [MAT 12:2](https://ref.ly/Matt12:2) · [MAT 12:5](https://ref.ly/Matt12:5) · [MAT 12:5](https://ref.ly/Matt12:5) · [MAT 12:8](https://ref.ly/Matt12:8) · [MAT 17:2](https://ref.ly/John17:2) · [ACT 18:4](https://ref.ly/John18:4) · [COL 2:16](https://ref.ly/Phil2:16)

67\.177 · Time · Definite Units of Time: Year, Month, Week, Day, Hour

week a period of seven days In some languages it may be better to render [LUK 18:12](https://ref.ly/Mark18:12) as simply ‘for every seven days, I fast two days.’ For the expression ‘the first day of the week,’ there may be a number of complications, especially since in present\-day usage Monday is often regarded as ‘the first day of the week.’ For the NT, of course, the Sabbath Day, or ‘Saturday,’ marked the seventh day of the week and the next day would be regarded as ‘the first day of the week,’ namely, Sunday.

[MAT 28:1](https://ref.ly/Matt28:1) · [MRK 16:2](https://ref.ly/Matt16:2) · [MRK 16:9](https://ref.ly/Matt16:9) · [LUK 18:12](https://ref.ly/Mark18:12) · [LUK 24:1](https://ref.ly/Mark24:1) · [JHN 20:1](https://ref.ly/Luke20:1) · [JHN 20:19](https://ref.ly/Luke20:19) · [ACT 20:7](https://ref.ly/John20:7) · [1CO 16:2](https://ref.ly/Rom16:2)

81\.28 · Spacial Dimensions · Specific Measures of Length

half a mile, one kilometer, Sabbath journey a Sabbath day’s journey, somewhat over half a mile and about one kilometer

[ACT 1:12](https://ref.ly/John1:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:1; Matthew 12:2; Matthew 12:5; Matthew 12:8; Matthew 12:10; Matthew 12:11; Matthew 12:12; Matthew 24:20; Matthew 28:1; Mark 1:21; Mark 2:23; Mark 2:24; Mark 2:27; Mark 2:28; Mark 3:2; Mark 3:4; Mark 6:2; Mark 16:1; Luke 4:16; Luke 4:31; Luke 6:1; Luke 6:2; Luke 6:5; Luke 6:6; Luke 6:7; Luke 6:9; Luke 13:10; Luke 13:14; Luke 13:15; Luke 13:16; Luke 14:1; Luke 14:3; Luke 14:5; Luke 23:54; Luke 23:56; John 5:9; John 5:10; John 5:16; John 5:18; John 7:22; John 7:23; John 9:14; John 9:16; John 19:31; Acts 13:14; Acts 13:27; Acts 13:42; Acts 13:44; Acts 15:21; Acts 16:13; Acts 17:2; Acts 18:4; Colossians 2:16; Mark 16:2; Mark 16:9; Luke 18:12; Luke 24:1; John 20:1; John 20:19; Acts 20:7; 1 Corinthians 16:2; Acts 1:12


## σαγήνη (id: 004424000000000)

σαγήνη
======

σαγήνη (G4522)

noun, f. \| \-ης

6\.13 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Fishing

seine net a long seine net used in fishing The σαγήνη was a long net hanging vertically in the water with floats at the upper edge and weights at the lower. It was drawn in by men working in boats or from shore. In [MAT 13:47](https://ref.ly/Matt13:47) the actual form of the net is not so important. What is significant is that the net was sufficiently large to catch a large number of different kinds of fish.

[MAT 13:47](https://ref.ly/Matt13:47)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:47


## Σαδδουκαῖος (id: 004425000000000)

Σαδδουκαῖος
===========

Σαδδουκαῖος (G4523)

noun\-name, m. \| \-ου

11\.48 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Religious

Sadducee a member of a politically influential Jewish party in Jerusalem at the time of Jesus and the apostles. The Sadducees were a smaller group than the Pharisees (see [11\.49](#11.49)), but were often in control of important political and religious positions. Their denial of the resurrection of the dead and their acceptance of only the first five books of the OT are important elements in some of the important differences which arose between the Sadducees and the Pharisees

[MAT 3:7](https://ref.ly/Matt3:7) · [MAT 16:1](https://ref.ly/Matt16:1) · [MAT 16:6](https://ref.ly/Matt16:6) · [MAT 16:11](https://ref.ly/Matt16:11) · [MAT 16:12](https://ref.ly/Matt16:12) · [MAT 22:23](https://ref.ly/Matt22:23) · [MAT 22:34](https://ref.ly/Matt22:34) · [MRK 12:18](https://ref.ly/Matt12:18) · [LUK 20:27](https://ref.ly/Mark20:27) · [ACT 4:1](https://ref.ly/John4:1) · [ACT 5:17](https://ref.ly/John5:17) · [ACT 23:6](https://ref.ly/John23:6) · [ACT 23:7](https://ref.ly/John23:7) · [ACT 23:8](https://ref.ly/John23:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 3:7; Matthew 16:1; Matthew 16:6; Matthew 16:11; Matthew 16:12; Matthew 22:23; Matthew 22:34; Mark 12:18; Luke 20:27; Acts 4:1; Acts 5:17; Acts 23:6; Acts 23:7; Acts 23:8

## σάκκος (id: 004428000000000)

σάκκος
======

σάκκος (G4526)

noun, m. \| \-ου

6\.164 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

sackcloth a heavy material normally used for making sacks, but worn by persons in mourning and as a sign of repentance In most languages sackcloth is described as ‘coarse cloth’ and sometimes as ‘heavy cloth.’

[MAT 11:21](https://ref.ly/Matt11:21) · [LUK 10:13](https://ref.ly/Mark10:13) · [REV 6:12](https://ref.ly/Jude6:12) · [REV 11:3](https://ref.ly/Jude11:3)

## σαλεύω (id: 004433000000000)

σαλεύω
======

σαλεύω (G4531) — σαλεύομαι

verb \| ἅλλομαι

16\.7 · Non\-Linear Movement

to shake to cause something to move back and forth rapidly, often violently In some languages there are quite distinct terms for shaking, depending upon the vigor of the motion and/or the objects which are shaken. Accordingly, one must exercise care in selecting terms which will accurately and adequately represent the nature of the shaking in the various contexts. For example, in [HEB 12:26](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:26) the shaking would presumably involve some kind of reverberation, but in [REV 6:13](https://ref.ly/Jude6:13) the action of the wind suggests whipping something back and forth.  
It is possible to interpret σαλεύω in [MAT 24:29](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29) (αἱ δυνάμεις τῶν οὐρανῶν σαλευθήσονται ‘the hosts of heaven will be shaken’) as meaning literal shaking, but it may be used figuratively in the sense of deposing the hosts of heaven from their positions of power.

[MAT 11:7](https://ref.ly/Matt11:7) · [MAT 24:29](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29) · [MRK 13:25](https://ref.ly/Matt13:25) · [LUK 6:38](https://ref.ly/Mark6:38) · [LUK 6:48](https://ref.ly/Mark6:48) · [LUK 7:24](https://ref.ly/Mark7:24) · [LUK 21:26](https://ref.ly/Mark21:26) · [ACT 4:31](https://ref.ly/John4:31) · [ACT 16:26](https://ref.ly/John16:26) · [HEB 12:26](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:26) · [HEB 12:27](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:27) · [HEB 12:27](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:27)

39\.44 · Hostility, Strife · Riot

to stir up against, to start a riot, to cause an uproar to cause people to riot against

[ACT 17:13](https://ref.ly/John17:13)

25\.242 · (σαλεύομαι) · Attitudes and Emotions · Worry, Anxiety, Distress, Peace

to become unsettled, to be deeply distressed, to be upset (a figurative extension of meaning of σαλεύω ‘to shake,’ [16\.7](#16.7)) to become emotionally unsettled and distraught

[ACT 2:25](https://ref.ly/John2:25) · [2TH 2:2](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 11:7; Matthew 24:29; Mark 13:25; Luke 6:38; Luke 6:48; Luke 7:24; Luke 21:26; Acts 4:31; Acts 16:26; Hebrews 12:26; Hebrews 12:27; Acts 17:13; Acts 2:25; 2 Thessalonians 2:2


## Σαλήμ (id: 004434000000000)

Σαλήμ
=====

Σαλήμ (G4532)

noun\-name, f. \| indeclinable

93\.566 · Names of Persons and Places · Places

Salem a place of which Melchizedek was king; see also [93\.321](#93.321)

[HEB 7:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:1) · [HEB 7:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:2)

93\.321 · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

**Collocation:** βασιλεὺς Σαλήμ

king of Salem the expression βασιλεὺς Σαλήμ ‘king of Salem’ ([HEB 7:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:1) [HEB 7:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:2) may be interpreted as ‘king of peace,’ and as such it may be regarded as an honorific name It is also possible that Σαλήμ refers to a place (see [93\.566](#93.566)).

[HEB 7:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:1) · [HEB 7:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Hebrews 7:1; Hebrews 7:2

## σάλπιγξ (id: 004439000000000)

σάλπιγξ
=======

σάλπιγξ (G4536)

noun, f. \| \-ιγγος \| σαλπίζω

6\.89 · Artifacts · Musical Instruments

trumpet a musical wind instrument; made of metal; frequently used in signaling, especially in connection with war The present\-day equivalent of the σάλπιγξ is the bugle.

[1CO 14:8](https://ref.ly/Rom14:8) · [REV 1:10](https://ref.ly/Jude1:10) · [REV 4:1](https://ref.ly/Jude4:1) · [REV 8:2](https://ref.ly/Jude8:2) · [REV 8:6](https://ref.ly/Jude8:6) · [REV 8:13](https://ref.ly/Jude8:13) · [REV 9:14](https://ref.ly/Jude9:14)

6\.93 · Artifacts · Musical Instruments

trumpet blast, trumpet sound (derivative of σαλπίζω\[a] ‘to play the trumpet,’ [6\.90](#6.90)) the sound made by a trumpet1 With both σαλπίζω\[b] ([6\.92](#6.92)) and σάλπιγξ\[b], it may be necessary to introduce an agent, even though indefinite. For example, ἐν τῇ ἐσχάτω σάλπιγγι may be translated as ‘when someone blows the trumpet for the last time,’ and σαλπίσει may be rendered as ‘when someone sounds the trumpet’ or ‘when someone produces a noise on the trumpet.’ However, any term for ‘noise’ should imply a meaningful sound.

[MAT 24:31](https://ref.ly/Matt24:31) · [1CO 15:52](https://ref.ly/Rom15:52) · [1TH 4:16](https://ref.ly/Col4:16) · [HEB 12:19](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:19)

1 Though it would seem logical to regard σάλπιγξ\[b] as a derivative of σάλπιγξ\[a] ([6\.89](#6.89)) in view of the formal similarity, nevertheless from the standpoint of the semantic components involved, σάλπιγξ\[b] is actually related to the verb σαλπίζω\[a] meaning to play the trumpet ([6\.90](#6.90)) or possibly σαλπίζω\[b] to sound a trumpet ([6\.92](#6.92)). σάλπιγξ\[b] definitely relates to the result of an event, not simply to the instrument employed in such an event.

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 14:8; Revelation 1:10; Revelation 4:1; Revelation 8:2; Revelation 8:6; Revelation 8:13; Revelation 9:14; Matthew 24:31; 1 Corinthians 15:52; 1 Thessalonians 4:16; Hebrews 12:19


## σαλπίζω (id: 004440000000000)

σαλπίζω
=======

σαλπίζω (G4537)

verb \| σάλπιγξ · σαλπιστής

6\.90 · Artifacts · Musical Instruments

to play the trumpet (derivative of σάλπιγξ\[a] trumpet, [6\.89](#6.89)) to produce sound with a trumpet It is possible, of course, in [MAT 6:2](https://ref.ly/Matt6:2) to interpret σαλπίζω as a type of causative and thus to say ‘to cause someone to blow the trumpet’ or ‘to have the trumpet blown.’

[MAT 6:2](https://ref.ly/Matt6:2) · [REV 8:6](https://ref.ly/Jude8:6) · [REV 8:7](https://ref.ly/Jude8:7) · [REV 8:8](https://ref.ly/Jude8:8) · [REV 8:10](https://ref.ly/Jude8:10) · [REV 8:12](https://ref.ly/Jude8:12) · [REV 8:13](https://ref.ly/Jude8:13) · [REV 9:1](https://ref.ly/Jude9:1) · [REV 9:13](https://ref.ly/Jude9:13) · [REV 10:7](https://ref.ly/Jude10:7) · [REV 11:15](https://ref.ly/Jude11:15)

6\.92 · Artifacts · Musical Instruments

to sound a trumpet, a trumpet sounds to produce the sound of a trumpet (without specification of an agent) In a number of languages it may be best to render σαλπίσει in [1CO 15:52](https://ref.ly/Rom15:52) as ‘people will hear the sound of the trumpet’ or ‘the sound of the trumpet will be heard.’

[MAT 6:2](https://ref.ly/Matt6:2) · [1CO 15:52](https://ref.ly/Rom15:52)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 6:2; Revelation 8:6; Revelation 8:7; Revelation 8:8; Revelation 8:10; Revelation 8:12; Revelation 8:13; Revelation 9:1; Revelation 9:13; Revelation 10:7; Revelation 11:15; 1 Corinthians 15:52

Σαμάρεια
========

Σαμάρεια (G4540)

noun\-name, f. \| \-ας

## σαπρός (id: 004453000000000)

σαπρός
======

σαπρός (G4550)

adjc. \| \-ά, \-όν \| σήπω

65\.28 · Value · Good, Bad

bad, diseased and possibly seedling pertaining to being of poor or bad quality and hence of little or no value (particularly in reference to plants, either in the sense of seriously diseased or of seedling stock, that is, not budded or grafted) Some scholars have suggested that σαπρός in [MAT 7:18](https://ref.ly/Matt7:18) really refers to a seedling, that is to say, a tree which has grown up completely from seed rather than being budded or grafted. Seedling trees often produce tasteless or even bitter fruit. By its very nature, such a tree cannot produce good fruit and is, therefore, considered to be of no value.

[MAT 7:17](https://ref.ly/Matt7:17) · [MAT 7:18](https://ref.ly/Matt7:18) · [MAT 12:33](https://ref.ly/Matt12:33) · [MAT 12:33](https://ref.ly/Matt12:33) · [MAT 13:48](https://ref.ly/Matt13:48) · [LUK 6:43](https://ref.ly/Mark6:43) · [LUK 6:43](https://ref.ly/Mark6:43)

20\.14 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Harm, Wound

harmful, unwholesome pertaining to that which is harmful in view of its being unwholesome and corrupting In [EPH 4:29](https://ref.ly/Gal4:29) σαπρός is in contrast with that which is ἀγαθός ‘good’ for building up what is necessary. In such a context ἀγαθός may be interpreted as that which is helpful, and by contrast σαπρός may be understood to mean ‘harmful.’

[EPH 4:29](https://ref.ly/Gal4:29)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 7:17; Matthew 7:18; Matthew 12:33; Matthew 13:48; Luke 6:43; Ephesians 4:29

## σαργάνη (id: 004456000000000)

σαργάνη
=======

σαργάνη (G4553)

noun, f. \| \-ης

6\.148 · Artifacts · Containers

large basket a large container made of woven material, usually grass or reeds; used for carrying a variety of things, including food and produce, and for moving soil from one place to another1 In the one context in which σαργάνη occurs ([2CO 11:33](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:33)), the basket was evidently rather large, since it was used to let Paul down from an opening in the wall of Damascus. It may very well have been made of braided ropes. In [2CO 11:33](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:33) the basket is called σαργάνη, while in [ACT 9:25](https://ref.ly/John9:25) the same basket is referred to as σπυρίς ({D:6\.149\).

[2CO 11:33](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:33)

1 Neither from NT contexts nor from extrabiblical usage can one determine precisely the differences in meaning between these three terms for baskets: σαργάνη ([6\.148](#6.148)), σπυρίς ([6\.149](#6.149)), and κόφινος ([6\.150](#6.150)).

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 11:33

## σαρκικός (id: 004461000000000)

σαρκικός
========

σαρκικός (G4559)

adjc. \| \-ή, \-όν \| σάρξ

26\.8 · Psychological Faculties

human, natural pertaining to what is human or characteristic of human nature

[2CO 1:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:12)

79\.1 · Features of Objects · Physical \[Material], Spiritual

material, physical pertaining to being material or physical, with the possible implication of inferior It is possible that σαρκικός in [ROM 15:27](https://ref.ly/Acts15:27) refers to blessings for the body, but the context would seem to imply blessings of greater significance than those designed only for a person’s body.

[ROM 15:27](https://ref.ly/Acts15:27) · [1CO 9:11](https://ref.ly/Rom9:11) · [2CO 10:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:4)

79\.4 · Features of Objects · Natural \[Human], Spiritual

natural, human pertaining to the natural, physical characteristics of persons and often including their characteristic behavior1

[1CO 3:3](https://ref.ly/Rom3:3)2 · [1CO 3:3](https://ref.ly/Rom3:3)2

41\.42 · Behavior and Related States · Particular Patterns of Behavior

worldly, base (derivative of σάρξ\[f] ‘human nature,’ [26\.7](#26.7)) pertaining to behavior which is typical of human nature, but with special focus upon more base physical desires In some languages the expression τῶν σαρκικῶν ἐπιθυμιῶν in [1PE 2:11](https://ref.ly/Jas2:11) may be rendered as ‘the desires which one’s body has’ or ‘what the body wants.’

[1PE 2:11](https://ref.ly/Jas2:11)

1 In a number of contexts it is difficult to determine whether the focus of σάρκινος\[c] and σαρκικός\[c] is upon the natural, physical characteristics or upon the tendency to behave in a particular way. In any event, resulting behavior is always implied. 2 1CO 3:3 · 1CO 3:3 The close proximity of σάρκινος and σαρκικός in the context of [1CO 3:1](https://ref.ly/Rom3:1)\-[1CO 3:3](https://ref.ly/Rom3:3) would seem to indicate that there is little, if any, difference in meaning.

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 1:12; Romans 15:27; 1 Corinthians 9:11; 2 Corinthians 10:4; 1 Corinthians 3:3; 1 Peter 2:11


## σάρκινος (id: 004462000000000)

9\.13 · People · Human Beings

[HEB 7:16](https://ref.ly/Phlm7:16)

26\.8 · Psychological Faculties

1 In a number of contexts it is difficult to determine whether the focus of σάρκινος\[c] and σαρκικός\[c] is upon the natural, physical characteristics or upon the tendency to behave in a particular way. In any event, resulting behavior is always implied.

## σάρξ (id: 004463000000000)

σάρξ
====

σάρξ (G4561)

noun, f. \| σαρκός \| σαρκικός · σάρκινος

8\.63 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

flesh the flesh of both animals and human beings Some languages make an important distinction between the flesh of a living person and the flesh of someone who has been killed or who has died. It would be this latter sense which should be reflected in [REV 19:18](https://ref.ly/Jude19:18). In [ROM 2:28](https://ref.ly/Acts2:28) the reference to ‘circumcision in the flesh’ (ἐν σαρκὶ περιτομή) would, however, require the first sense, namely, the flesh of a living person.

[LUK 24:39](https://ref.ly/Mark24:39) · [JHN 6:51](https://ref.ly/Luke6:51) · [JHN 6:52](https://ref.ly/Luke6:52) · [JHN 6:53](https://ref.ly/Luke6:53) · [JHN 6:54](https://ref.ly/Luke6:54) · [JHN 6:55](https://ref.ly/Luke6:55) · [JHN 6:56](https://ref.ly/Luke6:56) · [ACT 2:26](https://ref.ly/John2:26) · [ACT 2:31](https://ref.ly/John2:31) · [ROM 2:28](https://ref.ly/Acts2:28) · [1CO 5:5](https://ref.ly/Rom5:5) · [1CO 10:18](https://ref.ly/Rom10:18) · [1CO 15:39](https://ref.ly/Rom15:39) · [1CO 15:39](https://ref.ly/Rom15:39) · [1CO 15:39](https://ref.ly/Rom15:39) · [1CO 15:39](https://ref.ly/Rom15:39) · [GAL 6:13](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:13) · [EPH 2:11](https://ref.ly/Gal2:11) · [COL 1:22](https://ref.ly/Phil1:22) · [HEB 2:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:14) · [HEB 9:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:13) · [HEB 10:20](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:20) · [JAS 5:3](https://ref.ly/Heb5:3) · [REV 17:16](https://ref.ly/Jude17:16) · [REV 19:18](https://ref.ly/Jude19:18) · [REV 19:18](https://ref.ly/Jude19:18) · [REV 19:18](https://ref.ly/Jude19:18) · [REV 19:18](https://ref.ly/Jude19:18) · [REV 19:18](https://ref.ly/Jude19:18) · [REV 19:21](https://ref.ly/Jude19:21)

8\.4 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Body

body, physical body a living body1 Though the reference of σάρξ in [1TI 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:16) is to the physical body, it may be necessary in some instances to translate this as ‘a human being’ or ‘a person,’ that is to say, ‘Christ appeared as a human being’ or ‘Christ became a person.’ Otherwise, the reader might assume that Christ took on the body of someone else or merely indwelt some miraculous human form rather than actually became a human being

[MAT 19:5](https://ref.ly/Matt19:5) · [MAT 19:6](https://ref.ly/Matt19:6) · [MRK 10:8](https://ref.ly/Matt10:8) · [MRK 10:8](https://ref.ly/Matt10:8) · [JHN 6:51](https://ref.ly/Luke6:51) · [1CO 6:16](https://ref.ly/Rom6:16) · [2CO 4:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:11) · [2CO 7:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:1) · [2CO 7:5](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:5) · [2CO 10:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:3) · [GAL 2:20](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:20) · [GAL 4:13](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:13) · [GAL 4:14](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:14) · [EPH 2:14](https://ref.ly/Gal2:14) · [EPH 5:29](https://ref.ly/Gal5:29) · [EPH 5:31](https://ref.ly/Gal5:31) · [PHP 1:22](https://ref.ly/Eph1:22) · [PHP 1:24](https://ref.ly/Eph1:24) · [COL 1:24](https://ref.ly/Phil1:24) · [COL 2:1](https://ref.ly/Phil2:1) · [COL 2:5](https://ref.ly/Phil2:5) · [1TI 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:16) · [HEB 9:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:10) · [HEB 10:20](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:20) · [HEB 12:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:9) · [1PE 3:18](https://ref.ly/Jas3:18) · [1PE 3:21](https://ref.ly/Jas3:21) · [1PE 4:1](https://ref.ly/Jas4:1) · [1PE 4:1](https://ref.ly/Jas4:1) · [1PE 4:6](https://ref.ly/Jas4:6) · [2PE 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:10) · [2PE 2:18](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:18) · [1JN 4:2](https://ref.ly/2Pet4:2) · [JUD 1:7](https://ref.ly/3John1:7) · [JUD 1:8](https://ref.ly/3John1:8) · [JUD 1:23](https://ref.ly/3John1:23)

9\.11 · People · Human Beings

people, human being (a figurative extension of meaning of σάρξ\[a] ‘flesh,’ [8\.63](#8.63)) humans as physical beings

[MAT 24:22](https://ref.ly/Matt24:22) · [MRK 13:20](https://ref.ly/Matt13:20) · [LUK 3:6](https://ref.ly/Mark3:6) · [JHN 1:14](https://ref.ly/Luke1:14) · [JHN 17:2](https://ref.ly/Luke17:2) · [ACT 2:17](https://ref.ly/John2:17) · [ROM 3:20](https://ref.ly/Acts3:20) · [1CO 1:29](https://ref.ly/Rom1:29) · [GAL 2:16](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:16) · [1PE 1:24](https://ref.ly/Jas1:24)

9\.12 · People · Human Beings

physical nature, human (a figurative extension of meaning of σάρξ\[a] ‘flesh,’ [8\.63](#8.63)) human nature, with emphasis upon the physical aspects In a number of languages it would seem strange, if not totally redundant, to speak of ‘physical fathers’ or ‘human fathers’ ([HEB 12:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:9)), since the term ‘fathers’ would suffice, and any addition would be misleading. In some instances, however, one might use an expression such as ‘our own fathers,’ so as to provide an implied contrast with the heavenly Father. Where it is necessary to qualify the term ‘fathers,’ one may use an expression such as ‘fathers which caused us to be conceived.’

[EPH 6:5](https://ref.ly/Gal6:5) · [PHP 3:3](https://ref.ly/Eph3:3) · [PHP 3:4](https://ref.ly/Eph3:4) · [PHP 3:4](https://ref.ly/Eph3:4) · [HEB 12:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:9) · [2JN 1:7](https://ref.ly/1John1:7)

10\.1 · Kinship Terms · Groups and Members of Groups of Persons Regarded as Related by Blood but without Special Reference to Successive Generations

race, ethnic group, nation a relatively large group of persons regarded as being biologically related2 It may be difficult in some languages to clearly distinguish between culture and race as in [MRK 7:26](https://ref.ly/Matt7:26). Sometimes this difference can be indicated by saying ‘the woman lived like a Greek, but she was a Syrophoenician’ or ‘... her parents were from Syrophoenicia.’ In translating ‘people of my own race’ in [ROM 11:14](https://ref.ly/Acts11:14), it may be necessary to say ‘all my fellow Jews’ or ‘all those people of whom I am a part’ or ‘those people who are my roots’ or ‘... my trunk,’ based on the analogy of a tree trunk and branches.

[ROM 11:14](https://ref.ly/Acts11:14) · [EPH 2:11](https://ref.ly/Gal2:11)

26\.7 · Psychological Faculties

human nature, human aspects, natural, human the psychological aspect of human nature which contrasts with the spiritual nature; in other words, that aspect of human nature which is characterized by or reflects typical human reasoning and desires in contrast with those aspects of human thought and behavior which relate to God and the spiritual life Some scholars understand the meaning of σάρξ\[f] as being a person’s lower nature rather than simply human nature, but the distinction between lower nature and higher nature seems to be primarily one arising out of typical Greek thought rather than out of the Semitic background which seems to be so pervasive in the use of the term σάρξ in NT contexts such as [1CO 1:26](https://ref.ly/Rom1:26). There are, of course, contexts in which σάρξ does refer to that psychological factor in man which serves as a willing instrument of sin and is subject to sin.

[MAT 26:41](https://ref.ly/Matt26:41) · [MRK 14:38](https://ref.ly/Matt14:38) · [JHN 6:63](https://ref.ly/Luke6:63) · [JHN 8:15](https://ref.ly/Luke8:15) · [ROM 6:19](https://ref.ly/Acts6:19) · [ROM 7:5](https://ref.ly/Acts7:5) · [ROM 7:18](https://ref.ly/Acts7:18) · [ROM 7:25](https://ref.ly/Acts7:25) · [ROM 8:3](https://ref.ly/Acts8:3) · [ROM 8:3](https://ref.ly/Acts8:3) · [ROM 8:4](https://ref.ly/Acts8:4) · [ROM 8:5](https://ref.ly/Acts8:5) · [ROM 8:5](https://ref.ly/Acts8:5) · [ROM 8:6](https://ref.ly/Acts8:6) · [ROM 8:7](https://ref.ly/Acts8:7) · [ROM 8:8](https://ref.ly/Acts8:8) · [ROM 8:9](https://ref.ly/Acts8:9) · [ROM 8:12](https://ref.ly/Acts8:12) · [ROM 8:12](https://ref.ly/Acts8:12) · [ROM 8:13](https://ref.ly/Acts8:13) · [ROM 13:14](https://ref.ly/Acts13:14) · [1CO 1:26](https://ref.ly/Rom1:26) · [2CO 1:17](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:17) · [2CO 5:16](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:16) · [2CO 5:16](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:16) · [2CO 10:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:2) · [2CO 10:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:3) · [2CO 11:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:18) · [GAL 3:3](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:3) · [GAL 5:13](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:13) · [GAL 5:16](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:16) · [GAL 5:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:17) · [GAL 5:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:17) · [GAL 5:19](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:19) · [GAL 5:24](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:24) · [GAL 6:8](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:8) · [GAL 6:8](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:8) · [GAL 6:12](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:12) · [EPH 2:3](https://ref.ly/Gal2:3) · [EPH 2:3](https://ref.ly/Gal2:3) · [COL 2:11](https://ref.ly/Phil2:11) · [COL 2:13](https://ref.ly/Phil2:13) · [COL 2:18](https://ref.ly/Phil2:18) · [COL 2:23](https://ref.ly/Phil2:23) · [PHM 1:16](https://ref.ly/Titus1:16) · [1JN 2:16](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:16)

trouble, woe, suffering, serious inconvenience, thorn in the flesh (an idiom, literally: thorn in the flesh) something which causes serious trouble and difficulty There are a number of different interpretations of σκόλοψ τῇ σαρκί in [2CO 12:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:7) (see discussion at [20\.27](#20.27)).

1 It is possible that σάρξ\[b] differs in meaning from σῶμα\[a] ([8\.1](#8.1)) in focussing somewhat more upon the physical nature. 2 πατριά\[a] and φυλή\[b] nation, people ([11\.56](#11.56)) focus attention upon a particular people as a socially functioning unit, while the feature of biological descent is largely secondary. But in the case of γένος\[b] and σάρξ\[e], the feature of biological descent is focal, while group functioning is largely secondary. 3 In this subdomain (Human Beings) a number of expressions referring to people are based upon metonymies involving terms for parts or aspects of persons. Such metonymic figures of speech are involved in σὰρξ καὶ αἷμα ([9\.14](#9.14)), γόνυ\[b] ([9\.16](#9.16)), χείρ\[b] ([9\.17](#9.17)), γλῶσσα\[g] ([9\.18](#9.18)), ὄνομα\[b] ([9\.19](#9.19)), and ψυχή\[c] ([9\.20](#9.20)).

## Σατανᾶς (id: 004467000000000)

Σατανᾶς
=======

Σατανᾶς (G4567)

noun\-name, m. \| \-ᾶ

12\.34 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

Devil, Satan (a borrowing from Hebrew and Aramaic: a title for the Devil, literally: adversary) the principal supernatural evil being1 In a number of languages there is a well known proper name for the Devil as the chief of all demons. In other instances, however, he is given a descriptive name, for example, ‘the ruler of the evil spirits,’ ‘the chief of the demons,’ ‘the truly bad one,’ ‘the left\-handed one’ (as the one who is opposed to all which is right or correct), ‘the no\-good one,’ ‘the avaricious one.’ In some instances a term for the Devil may be highly idiomatic as, for example, ‘the barking one,’ a reference to the Devil’s presumed activity in animal guise.  
Some translators have employed for ‘Devil’ the proper name Satan, but this is often not a satisfactory solution. In one language in West Africa, for example, the term Satan had already been borrowed but was understood in the sense of the culture hero of the people and not as a designation for the chief of demons.  
See also [REV 20:2](https://ref.ly/Jude20:2).

[MAT 4:10](https://ref.ly/Matt4:10) · [MAT 12:26](https://ref.ly/Matt12:26) · [MAT 12:26](https://ref.ly/Matt12:26) · [MAT 16:23](https://ref.ly/Matt16:23) · [MRK 1:13](https://ref.ly/Matt1:13) · [MRK 3:23](https://ref.ly/Matt3:23) · [MRK 3:23](https://ref.ly/Matt3:23) · [MRK 3:26](https://ref.ly/Matt3:26) · [MRK 4:15](https://ref.ly/Matt4:15) · [MRK 8:33](https://ref.ly/Matt8:33) · [LUK 10:18](https://ref.ly/Mark10:18) · [LUK 11:18](https://ref.ly/Mark11:18) · [LUK 13:16](https://ref.ly/Mark13:16) · [LUK 22:3](https://ref.ly/Mark22:3) · [LUK 22:31](https://ref.ly/Mark22:31) · [JHN 13:27](https://ref.ly/Luke13:27) · [ACT 5:3](https://ref.ly/John5:3) · [ACT 26:18](https://ref.ly/John26:18) · [ROM 16:20](https://ref.ly/Acts16:20) · [1CO 5:5](https://ref.ly/Rom5:5) · [1CO 7:5](https://ref.ly/Rom7:5) · [2CO 2:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:11) · [2CO 11:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:14) · [2CO 12:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:7) · [1TH 2:18](https://ref.ly/Col2:18) · [2TH 2:9](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:9) · [1TI 1:20](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:20) · [1TI 5:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:15) · [REV 2:9](https://ref.ly/Jude2:9) · [REV 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jude2:13) · [REV 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jude2:13) · [REV 2:24](https://ref.ly/Jude2:24) · [REV 3:9](https://ref.ly/Jude3:9) · [REV 12:9](https://ref.ly/Jude12:9) · [REV 20:2](https://ref.ly/Jude20:2) · [REV 20:7](https://ref.ly/Jude20:7)

93\.330 · Names of Persons and Places · Persons

Satan (a borrowing from Hebrew and Aramaic meaning literally: adversary) the usual proper name of the Devil; see also [12\.34](#12.34)

[MAT 4:10](https://ref.ly/Matt4:10) · [MAT 12:26](https://ref.ly/Matt12:26) · [MAT 12:26](https://ref.ly/Matt12:26) · [MAT 16:23](https://ref.ly/Matt16:23) · [MRK 1:13](https://ref.ly/Matt1:13) · [MRK 3:23](https://ref.ly/Matt3:23) · [MRK 3:23](https://ref.ly/Matt3:23) · [MRK 3:26](https://ref.ly/Matt3:26) · [MRK 4:15](https://ref.ly/Matt4:15) · [MRK 8:33](https://ref.ly/Matt8:33) · [LUK 10:18](https://ref.ly/Mark10:18) · [LUK 11:18](https://ref.ly/Mark11:18) · [LUK 13:16](https://ref.ly/Mark13:16) · [LUK 22:3](https://ref.ly/Mark22:3) · [LUK 22:31](https://ref.ly/Mark22:31) · [JHN 13:27](https://ref.ly/Luke13:27) · [ACT 5:3](https://ref.ly/John5:3) · [ACT 26:18](https://ref.ly/John26:18) · [ROM 16:20](https://ref.ly/Acts16:20) · [1CO 5:5](https://ref.ly/Rom5:5) · [1CO 7:5](https://ref.ly/Rom7:5) · [2CO 2:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor2:11) · [2CO 11:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:14) · [2CO 12:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:7) · [1TH 2:18](https://ref.ly/Col2:18) · [2TH 2:9](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:9) · [1TI 1:20](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:20) · [1TI 5:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess5:15) · [REV 2:9](https://ref.ly/Jude2:9) · [REV 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jude2:13) · [REV 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jude2:13) · [REV 2:24](https://ref.ly/Jude2:24) · [REV 3:9](https://ref.ly/Jude3:9) · [REV 12:9](https://ref.ly/Jude12:9) · [REV 20:2](https://ref.ly/Jude20:2) · [REV 20:7](https://ref.ly/Jude20:7)

1 The terms διάβολος and Σατανᾶς appear to function both as titles and as proper names. This results from the fact that the referent in each instance is unique. In the text of the Greek NT Σατανᾶς was traditionally written with an initial capital letter, while διάβολος was normally written with a lower case initial letter, except for the occurrences of Διάβολος in [REV 12:9](https://ref.ly/Jude12:9) and [REV 20:2](https://ref.ly/Jude20:2).

## σάτον (id: 004468000000000)

σάτον
=====

σάτον (G4568)

noun, n. \| \-ου

81\.23 · Spacial Dimensions · Specific Measures of Volume

saton, measure, batch the Hebrew measure for grain, about a peck and a half or somewhat less than one\-half bushel (a bushel consists of four pecks) or approximately twelve liters in the metric system In [MAT 13:33](https://ref.ly/Matt13:33) the precise amount of flour is not important. What is important is to provide some type of measurement which will indicate a considerable quantity.

## σβέννυμι (id: 004470000000000)

σβέννυμι
========

σβέννυμι (G4570) — σβέννυμαι

verb \| fut. σβέσω · aor. ἔσβεσα · inf. σβέσαι \| ἄσβεστος

14\.70 · Physical Events and States · Burning

to extinguish a fire, to put out a fire to cause a fire to be extinguished ‘To put out fierce fires’ may be expressed as ‘to cause fierce fires no longer to burn’ or ‘to make large fires stop burning.’ In order to speak of ‘fierce fires’ it may be necessary in some languages to speak of ‘large, hot fires.’

[MAT 12:20](https://ref.ly/Matt12:20) · [MAT 25:8](https://ref.ly/Matt25:8) · [MRK 9:48](https://ref.ly/Matt9:48) · [EPH 6:16](https://ref.ly/Gal6:16) · [HEB 11:34](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:34)

68\.52 · Aspect · Cease, Stop

to stop, to quench (a figurative extension of meaning of σβέννυμι\[a] ‘to extinguish a fire,’ [14\.70](#14.70)) to cause a fervent activity to cease Though the particular activity of the Spirit is not overtly indicated in the context of [1TH 5:19](https://ref.ly/Col5:19), the book as a whole contains sufficient reference to the activity of the Spirit so as to indicate what is involved.

[1TH 5:19](https://ref.ly/Col5:19)

14\.69 · (σβέννυμαι) · Physical Events and States · Burning

to stop burning to cease burning, either because of lack of material to be burned or because the fire has been forcibly extinguished The expression ‘our lamps are going out’ may be rendered as ‘our lamps will soon not be burning’ or ‘our lamps will burn only a little bit more.’ It may, however, be misleading to speak of ‘lamps burning’ (see discussion in [14\.65](#14.65)), and accordingly, it may be much better to translate ‘our lamps will show light only a little bit more’ or ‘the oil in our lamps will burn only a little bit more.’

[MAT 25:8](https://ref.ly/Matt25:8)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:20; Matthew 25:8; Mark 9:48; Ephesians 6:16; Hebrews 11:34; 1 Thessalonians 5:19

## σεβάζομαι (id: 004472000000000)

σεβάζομαι
=========

σεβάζομαι (G4573)

verb \| σέβομαι

53\.53 · Religious Activities · Worship, Reverence

to worship, to venerate to express in attitude and ritual one’s allegiance to and regard for deity In a number of languages worship is expressed in an idiomatic manner, for example, ‘to bow down before,’ ‘to lower one’s head before,’ ‘to raise one’s arms to,’ ‘to sing to,’ ‘to honor.’ It is important in selecting an expression for worship to employ a term or phrase which will include various aspects of worship.

[ROM 1:25](https://ref.ly/Acts1:25)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 1:25


## σέβασμα (id: 004473000000000)

σέβασμα
=======

## σέβω (id: 004475000000000)

σέβω
====

σέβω (G4576) — σέβομαι

verb \| ἀσέβεια · ἀσεβέω · ἀσεβής · εὐσέβεια · εὐσεβέω · εὐσεβής · εὐσεβῶς · θεοσέβεια · θεοσεβής · σεβάζομαι · σέβασμα · σεβαστός · σεμνός · σεμνότης

53\.53 · (σέβομαι) · Religious Activities · Worship, Reverence

to worship, to venerate to express in attitude and ritual one’s allegiance to and regard for deity In a number of languages worship is expressed in an idiomatic manner, for example, ‘to bow down before,’ ‘to lower one’s head before,’ ‘to raise one’s arms to,’ ‘to sing to,’ ‘to honor.’ It is important in selecting an expression for worship to employ a term or phrase which will include various aspects of worship.

[MAT 15:9](https://ref.ly/Matt15:9) · [MRK 7:7](https://ref.ly/Matt7:7) · [ACT 13:43](https://ref.ly/John13:43) · [ACT 13:50](https://ref.ly/John13:50) · [ACT 16:14](https://ref.ly/John16:14) · [ACT 17:4](https://ref.ly/John17:4) · [ACT 17:17](https://ref.ly/John17:17) · [ACT 18:7](https://ref.ly/John18:7) · [ACT 18:13](https://ref.ly/John18:13) · [ACT 19:27](https://ref.ly/John19:27)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 15:9; Mark 7:7; Acts 13:43; Acts 13:50; Acts 16:14; Acts 17:4; Acts 17:17; Acts 18:7; Acts 18:13; Acts 19:27

## σειρά (id: 004477000000000)

σειρά
=====

σειρά (G4577) — σιρά

noun, f. \| \-ᾶς

6\.15 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Binding and Fastening

chain (made of metal) or rope (made of fiber) a pliable instrument of binding In a number of languages a term for chain is simply metal rope. In other languages it may be described as linked rope in contrast with twisted rope, that is, a rope made out of some kind of fiber.  
The phrase σειραῖς ζόφου ([2PE 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:4)) is admittedly a strange expression, and in some manuscripts this gave rise to a slight change in orthography (σιροῖς; see [1\.59](#1.59)) with the resulting meaning being ‘in pits of darkness.’ If, however, one adopts the text ἀλλὰ σειραῖς ζόφου ταρταρώσας, it may be possible to interpret the entire expression as ‘but he chained them in the darkness of hell.’

[2PE 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:4)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Peter 2:4


## σεισμός (id: 004478000000000)

σεισμός
=======

σεισμός (G4578)

noun, m. \| \-οῦ \| σείω

14\.87 · Physical Events and States · Movement of the Earth

earthquake a sudden and severe movement of the earth Since earthquakes are universal in occurrence, there is normally no difficulty involved in finding some way of speaking about them. However, in a number of languages idiomatic expressions are used, for example, ‘the devil rolled over’ or ‘mother earth belched.’  
In [ACT 16:26](https://ref.ly/John16:26) the earthquake is regarded as the cause of the prison foundations shaking, and it may be better to restructure the relationships expressed in [ACT 16:26](https://ref.ly/John16:26) as ‘the prison shook because of the earthquake.’

[MAT 24:7](https://ref.ly/Matt24:7) · [MAT 27:54](https://ref.ly/Matt27:54) · [MAT 28:2](https://ref.ly/Matt28:2) · [MRK 13:8](https://ref.ly/Matt13:8) · [LUK 21:11](https://ref.ly/Mark21:11) · [ACT 16:26](https://ref.ly/John16:26) · [REV 6:12](https://ref.ly/Jude6:12) · [REV 8:5](https://ref.ly/Jude8:5) · [REV 11:13](https://ref.ly/Jude11:13) · [REV 11:13](https://ref.ly/Jude11:13) · [REV 11:19](https://ref.ly/Jude11:19) · [REV 16:18](https://ref.ly/Jude16:18) · [REV 16:18](https://ref.ly/Jude16:18)

14\.22 · Physical Events and States · Events Involving Liquids and Dry Masses

storm on the sea a violent action of the surface of a body of water as the result of high waves caused by a strong wind Though the term σεισμός\[b] obviously implies the strong action of the wind, the focus is upon the violent motion caused by the waves. It might, therefore, be more appropriate to translate [MAT 8:24](https://ref.ly/Matt8:24) as ‘there were huge waves on the sea’ or ‘... on the lake.’ Such a translation would then be appropriate for the following clause.

[MAT 8:24](https://ref.ly/Matt8:24)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 24:7; Matthew 27:54; Matthew 28:2; Mark 13:8; Luke 21:11; Acts 16:26; Revelation 6:12; Revelation 8:5; Revelation 11:13; Revelation 11:19; Revelation 16:18; Matthew 8:24


## σείω (id: 004479000000000)

σείω
====

σείω (G4579) — σείομαι

verb \| ἀνασείω · διασείω · κατασείω · σεισμός

16\.7 · Non\-Linear Movement

to shake to cause something to move back and forth rapidly, often violently In some languages there are quite distinct terms for shaking, depending upon the vigor of the motion and/or the objects which are shaken. Accordingly, one must exercise care in selecting terms which will accurately and adequately represent the nature of the shaking in the various contexts. For example, in [HEB 12:26](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:26) the shaking would presumably involve some kind of reverberation, but in [REV 6:13](https://ref.ly/Jude6:13) the action of the wind suggests whipping something back and forth.

[MAT 27:51](https://ref.ly/Matt27:51) · [HEB 12:26](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:26) · [REV 6:13](https://ref.ly/Jude6:13)

25\.233 · Attitudes and Emotions · Worry, Anxiety, Distress, Peace

to stir up, to cause an uproar, to cause great anxiety (a figurative extension of meaning of σείω\[a] ‘to shake,’ [16\.7](#16.7)) to cause extreme anxiety and apprehension, implying accompanying movement

[MAT 21:10](https://ref.ly/Matt21:10)

16\.6 · (σείομαι) · Non\-Linear Movement

to tremble, trembling, to quiver, to shake to shake or tremble, often with the implication of fear and/or consternation In a number of languages there are two distinct terms for trembling, one relating to illness (as in the case of epileptic seizures or the chills and fever associated with malaria) and the other associated with fear.

[MAT 28:4](https://ref.ly/Matt28:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:51; Hebrews 12:26; Revelation 6:13; Matthew 21:10; Matthew 28:4

## σελήνη (id: 004482000000000)

σελήνη
======

σελήνη (G4582)

noun, f. \| \-ης \| σεληνιάζομαι

1\.29 · Geographical Objects and Features · Heavenly Bodies

moon a celestial body smaller than the sun that gives light to earth in the nighttime; the moon’s appearance changes over the course of each month as the angle we can see the moon’s half\-illuminated surface changes As in the case of ἥλιος the sun ([1\.28](#1.28)), there are relatively few difficulties involved in obtaining a satisfactory word for σελήνη ‘the moon,’ though there may also be a tendency to add some kind of honorific or title, for example, ‘mother moon.’ At the same time, certain difficulties may occur in some passages. For example, in [LUK 21:25](https://ref.ly/Mark21:25) it may be misleading to speak of signs occurring ‘in the moon,’ for this might mean ‘inside the moon.’ TEV has resolved the problem somewhat by translating “there will be strange things happening to the sun, the moon, and the stars.” One may also translate ‘the sun, the moon, and the stars will cause signs in the heavens’ or ‘... portents in the sky.’

[MAT 24:29](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29) · [MRK 13:24](https://ref.ly/Matt13:24) · [LUK 21:25](https://ref.ly/Mark21:25) · [ACT 2:20](https://ref.ly/John2:20) · [1CO 15:41](https://ref.ly/Rom15:41) · [REV 6:12](https://ref.ly/Jude6:12) · [REV 8:12](https://ref.ly/Jude8:12) · [REV 12:1](https://ref.ly/Jude12:1) · [REV 21:23](https://ref.ly/Jude21:23)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 24:29; Mark 13:24; Luke 21:25; Acts 2:20; 1 Corinthians 15:41; Revelation 6:12; Revelation 8:12; Revelation 12:1; Revelation 21:23

## σημεῖον (id: 004493000000000)

σημεῖον
=======

σημεῖον (G4592)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| σημαίνω

33\.477 · Communication · Non\-Verbal Communication

sign an event which is regarded as having some special meaning In translating σημεῖον in [MAT 24:3](https://ref.ly/Matt24:3), it may be necessary in some languages to say ‘tell us what will happen that will show that you are coming’ or ‘tell us what we will see that will make us know that you are coming.’  
σημεῖον as an event with special meaning was inevitably an unusual or even miraculous type of occurrence, and in a number of contexts σημεῖον may be rendered as ‘miracle.’ Certainly that is the referent of the term σημεῖον in [JHN 2:23](https://ref.ly/Luke2:23) (πολλοὶ ἐπίστευσαν εἰς τὸ ὄνομα αὐτοῦθεωροῦντες αὐτοῦ τὰ σημεῖα ἅ ἐποίει ‘many believed in him as they saw the signs he did’). For the Gospel of John, however, a σημεῖον is not simply a miraculous event but something which points to a reality with even greater significance. A strictly literal translation of σημεῖον as ‘sign’ might mean nothing more than a road sign or a sign on a building, and therefore in some languages σημεῖον in a context such as [JHN 2:23](https://ref.ly/Luke2:23) may be rendered as ‘a miracle with great meaning.’

[MAT 12:38](https://ref.ly/Matt12:38) · [MAT 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39) · [MAT 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39) · [MAT 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39) · [MAT 16:1](https://ref.ly/Matt16:1) · ## σήμερον (id: 004495000000000)

σήμερον
=======

σήμερον (G4594)

advb. \| ἡμέρα

67\.205 · Time · Units of Time with Reference to Other Units or Points of Time: Yesterday, Today, Next Day

today the same day as the day of a discourse

## σήπω (id: 004496000000000)

σήπω
====

σήπω (G4595)

verb \| pf. σέσηπα \| σαπρός

23\.205 · Physiological Processes and States · Rot, Decay

to rot, to decay, decay to rot or decay, in reference to organic matter There may be problems involved in a literal rendering of [JAS 5:2](https://ref.ly/Heb5:2) because it may seem strange to speak of ‘riches rotting,’ since a term for ‘riches’ is likely to refer primarily to money. It may therefore be necessary to translate ‘the things that make you rich’ or ‘all the things you have as a rich person.’

[JAS 5:2](https://ref.ly/Heb5:2)

* **Associated Passages:** James 5:2


## σής (id: 004497000000000)

σής
===

σής (G4597)

noun, m. \| σητός \| σητόβρωτος

4\.49 · Animals · Insects

moth smallish brown or gray moth that lays eggs in clothing or other cloth; eggs hatch into very small caterpillars, which feed on the fibers; Tineidae family, probably Tineola biselliella; symbols of decay, ruin, and slow destruction In the NT the Greek term σής is used only in reference to the larvae of moths, and therefore it is frequently necessary to employ a term in the receptor language for the larvae rather than for the flying insect. This means that frequently an appropriate equivalent is ‘the worms of moths,’ but often one can employ an expression which means simply ‘cloth worms’ or ‘cloth eaters.’  
In [MAT 6:19](https://ref.ly/Matt6:19) [MAT 6:20](https://ref.ly/Matt6:20) [LUK 12:33](https://ref.ly/Mark12:33) the effect of the larvae of moths is combined with rust as agents for the destruction of valuable objects. It is rare, however, that one can speak of the destruction caused by moths in the same way as one can describe the effects of rust or tarnish. It may therefore be necessary to talk about ‘moths eating cloth,’ while ‘tarnish ruins precious metal.’

[MAT 6:19](https://ref.ly/Matt6:19) · [MAT 6:20](https://ref.ly/Matt6:20) · [LUK 12:33](https://ref.ly/Mark12:33)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 6:19; Matthew 6:20; Luke 12:33


## σητόβρωτος (id: 004498000000000)

σητόβρωτος
==========

σητόβρωτος (G4598)

adjc. \| \-ον \| σής \+ βιβρώσκω

20\.20 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Harm, Wound

moth\-eaten, ruined by moths pertaining to that which has been damaged by the larvae of moths This expression in [JAS 5:2](https://ref.ly/Heb5:2) may often be rendered as ‘your garments have been eaten by worms’ or ‘your garments are full of holes.’

[JAS 5:2](https://ref.ly/Heb5:2)

* **Associated Passages:** James 5:2

σθενόω

verb \| ἀσθένεια · ἀσθενέω · ἀσθένημα · ἀσθενής

74\.14 · Able, Capable

to make more able, to strengthen to cause someone to be or to become more able or capable, with the implication of a contrast with weakness The terms στηρίζω (see [74\.19](#74.19)) and σθενόω in [1PE 5:10](https://ref.ly/Jas5:10) are very similar in meaning and serve primarily to intensify the meaning of making persons more able to engage in or to undergo certain experiences.

[1PE 5:10](https://ref.ly/Jas5:10)

## σίκερα (id: 004508000000000)

σίκερα
======

σίκερα (G4608)

noun, n. (Aramaic loanword)

6\.200 · Artifacts · Plant Products

beer an intoxicating drink made from grain Though σίκερα may have a generic meaning and thus refer to any type of intoxicating drink, in the NT it occurs only in [LUK 1:15](https://ref.ly/Mark1:15), where it contrasts with wine and refers to intoxicating beverages made from grain. Distilled alcoholic beverages, such as whiskey, gin, and vodka, were not known in the ancient world.

[LUK 1:15](https://ref.ly/Mark1:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:15

## σίναπι (id: 004515000000000)

σίναπι
======

σίναπι (G4615)

noun, n. \| \-εως

3\.20 · Plants · Plants That Are Not Trees

mustard plant mustard plant, a large herb noted for its very small seeds and in some instances growing to a height of three meters (about ten feet) Note that in [MAT 13:31](https://ref.ly/Matt13:31) (and in the parallel passage [LUK 13:19](https://ref.ly/Mark13:19)) σίναπι is actually spoken of as a δένδρον tree, evidently a type of rhetorical hyperbole.  
Though the mustard plant may not be known in certain areas of the world, the use of mustard as a condiment is widely known, and therefore it is often possible to speak of ‘a plant that produces mustard’ or ‘the plant used in making mustard.’ In order, however, to make the parable meaningful, it may be necessary to have some explanation of this plant in a footnote or glossary.

[MAT 13:31](https://ref.ly/Matt13:31) · [MAT 17:20](https://ref.ly/Matt17:20) · [MRK 4:31](https://ref.ly/Matt4:31) · [LUK 13:19](https://ref.ly/Mark13:19) · [LUK 17:6](https://ref.ly/Mark17:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:31; Matthew 17:20; Mark 4:31; Luke 13:19; Luke 17:6


## σινδών (id: 004516000000000)

σινδών
======

σινδών (G4616)

noun, f. \| \-όνος

6\.155 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

linen cloth linen cloth of good quality In a number of languages there is no term for ‘linen,’ and though a word for ‘linen’ may be borrowed, what is important in the NT contexts in which σινδών occurs is primarily the quality of the cloth, not the material of which it was made. Accordingly, many translators have used an expression such as ‘fine cloth’ or ‘good cloth.’

[MAT 27:59](https://ref.ly/Matt27:59) · [MRK 14:51](https://ref.ly/Matt14:51) · [MRK 14:52](https://ref.ly/Matt14:52) · [MRK 15:46](https://ref.ly/Matt15:46) · [MRK 15:46](https://ref.ly/Matt15:46) · [LUK 23:53](https://ref.ly/Mark23:53)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:59; Mark 14:51; Mark 14:52; Mark 15:46; Luke 23:53


## σινιάζω (id: 004517000000000)

σινιάζω
=======

σινιάζω (G4617)

verb

46\.18 · Household Activities

to sift to sift by shaking in a sieve The expression ὑμᾶς τοῦ σινιάσαι ὡς τὸν σῖτον in [LUK 22:31](https://ref.ly/Mark22:31) is clearly a type of figurative usage and in many languages must be translated as ‘to test you’ or ‘to test you so as to separate the good from the bad.’ In some languages, however, it may be more satisfactory to shift the figure from sifting to winnowing and hence translate ‘to winnow you like a farmer who separates the wheat from the chaff.’

[LUK 22:31](https://ref.ly/Mark22:31)1

1 LUK 22:31 In [LUK 22:31](https://ref.ly/Mark22:31) the expression ὑμᾶς τοῦ σινιάσαι ὡς τὸν σῖτον ‘to sift you like wheat’ is semantically complex, for σινιάσαι ὡς τὸν σῖτον ‘to sift like wheat’ must be taken in a literal sense, but when used with the object ὑμᾶς ‘you’ (plural), obviously it is not wheat which is involved, but persons, and therefore the meaning must relate to some type of testing of actions and/or motivations. It is impossible to determine whether the expression σινιάσαι ὡς τὸν σῖτον had actually become an established idiom.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 22:31


## σιρικός (id: 004518000000000)

σιρικός
=======

σιρικός (G4596a) — σιρικόν

adjc. \| \-ή, \-όν

6\.168 · Artifacts · Cloth, Leather, and Objects Made of Such Materials

silk cloth fabric made of threads from the lustrous tough elastic fiber produced by silkworms for their cocoons; highly valued

[REV 18:12](https://ref.ly/Jude18:12)1

1 REV 18:12 From the context of [REV 18:12](https://ref.ly/Jude18:12) it is impossible to determine whether the referents of βύσσινον ([6\.167](#6.167)), σιρικόν ([6\.168](#6.168)), and πορφύρα ([6\.169](#6.169)) are cloth or garments made of linen, silk, and purple cloth respectively.

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 18:12


## σιρός (id: 004519000000000)

σιρός
=====

σιρός — σειρός

noun, f. \| \-οῦ

1\.59 · Geographical Objects and Features · Depressions and Holes

pit, deep hole This word is found as a variant reading only: ἀλλὰ σιροῖς ζόφου ταρταρώσας παρέδωκεν εἰς κρίσιν τηρουμένους ‘but cast them into hell and committed them to the pits of intense gloom to be kept until the judgment’ [2PE 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:4) (apparatus; the text of [2PE 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:4) reads σειρά ‘chain,’ [6\.15](#6.15)). In this one occurrence of σιρός in the NT, the pit in question is a place of imprisonment until the time of judgment. The expression ‘the pits of intense gloom’ may be translated as ‘pits where it is extremely dark.’  
Though most scholars have interpreted σιρός as being equivalent to ἄβυσσος ([1\.20](#1.20)), others see a distinction. But there is a danger in attempting to make too many fine distinctions between the meanings of such biblical terms. There is little evidence that biblical writers used such expressions with the same degree of differentiation which some persons would like to find.

[2PE 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:4)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Peter 2:4


## σιτευτός (id: 004520000000000)

σιτευτός
========

adjc. \| \-ή, \-όν \| σῖτος

44\.2 · Animal Husbandry, Fishing

fat, fattened, grain\-fattened pertaining to being well fed on grain and hence fattened In [LUK 15:27](https://ref.ly/Mark15:27) σιτευτός may, however, mean ‘valuable’ or ‘prize.’ This would simply be an extended meaning of σιτευτός in view of the resulting condition or value of a grain\-fed animal. valuable, prize pertaining to being valuable or prized on the basis of its being well fed and fat (occurring in reference to a calf) For another interpretation of σιτευτός in [LUK 15:27](https://ref.ly/Mark15:27), see [44\.2](#44.2).

## σιτίον (id: 004521000000000)

σιτίον
======

σιτίον (G4621a)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| σῖτος

3\.42 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

grain, food (a diminutive form of σῖτος ‘grain,’ [3\.41](#3.41), but not diminutive in meaning) any grain, but with the evident implication of its relevance as food (See also [5\.2](#5.2).) On the basis of this one NT occurrence it is impossible to know whether the meaning of σιτία is ‘grain’ or ‘food,’ since in the phrase σιτία καὶ ποτά ‘food and drink’ (an expression occurring in a number of extrabiblical contexts), the term σιτίον contrasts solid with liquid nourishment.

[ACT 7:12](https://ref.ly/John7:12)

5\.2 · Foods and Condiments · Food

food, grain (diminutive of σῖτος\[a] ‘wheat, grain,’ [3\.41](#3.41), but without diminutive meaning and occurring primarily in the plural) food consisting principally of grain products It is, of course, possible in [ACT 7:12](https://ref.ly/John7:12) to understand the plural form as ‘grain’ (see [3\.42](#3.42)), but the reference is probably to food made from grain, a common meaning of this term in Classical Greek.

[ACT 7:12](https://ref.ly/John7:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 7:12

## σιτομέτριον (id: 004523000000000)

σιτομέτριον

## σῖτος (id: 004524000000000)

σῖτος
=====

σῖτος (G4621)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| ἀσιτία · ἄσιτος · ἐπισιτισμός · σιτίον · σιτιστός · σιτομέτριον

3\.41 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

grain, wheat any kind of edible grain, though generally referring to wheat

[MAT 3:12](https://ref.ly/Matt3:12) · [MAT 13:30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:30) · [MRK 4:28](https://ref.ly/Matt4:28) · [LUK 3:17](https://ref.ly/Mark3:17) · [LUK 12:18](https://ref.ly/Mark12:18) · [LUK 16:7](https://ref.ly/Mark16:7) · [LUK 22:31](https://ref.ly/Mark22:31) · [ACT 27:38](https://ref.ly/John27:38) · [1CO 15:37](https://ref.ly/Rom15:37) · [REV 6:6](https://ref.ly/Jude6:6) · [REV 18:13](https://ref.ly/Jude18:13)

3\.31 · Plants · Plants That Are Not Trees

wheat the plant of wheat Elsewhere in the NT σῖτος, when used alone, refers to wheat as grain, but even in [JHN 12:24](https://ref.ly/Luke12:24) τοῦ σίτου may be interpreted as a so\-called ‘appositional genitive,’ that is, ‘seed which is wheat’ or ‘wheat seed.’  
While in some parts of the world wheat as a grain or as a plant is not known, in almost all instances people are acquainted with wheat flour, and therefore it is often possible to translate ‘wheat’ as ‘flour plant’ or ‘plant the grain of which is used to make flour.’ In some languages, however, the only possible equivalent is ‘rice\-like plant’ in which ‘rice\-like’ means essentially ‘grass\-like,’ while at the same time indicating edible grain.

[MAT 13:25](https://ref.ly/Matt13:25) · [MAT 13:29](https://ref.ly/Matt13:29) · [JHN 12:24](https://ref.ly/Luke12:24)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 3:12; Matthew 13:30; Mark 4:28; Luke 3:17; Luke 12:18; Luke 16:7; Luke 22:31; Acts 27:38; 1 Corinthians 15:37; Revelation 6:6; Revelation 18:13; Matthew 13:25; Matthew 13:29; John 12:24

33\.118 · Communication · Keep Silent

## σκάνδαλον (id: 004528000000000)

σκάνδαλον
=========

σκάνδαλον (G4625)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| σκανδαλίζω

6\.25 · Artifacts · Traps, Snares

trap a trap, probably of the type which has a stick which when touched by an animal causes the trap to shut In [ROM 11:9](https://ref.ly/Acts11:9) παγίς ([6\.23](#6.23)), θήρα ([6\.24](#6.24)), and σκάνδαλον would all seem to be completely parallel in structure and meaning. As a result, in a number of languages the three terms are reduced often to two, for example, ‘snare’ and ‘trap.’ If there are three different kinds of traps, then, of course, three terms can be used. In some cases, however, it may be preferable to use verbs to express the catching and trapping, and thus one may translate γενηθήτω ἡ τράπεζα αὐτῶν εἰς παγίδα καὶ εἰς θήραν καὶ εἰς σκάνδαλον as in TEV, “may they be caught and trapped at their feasts; may they fall.”

[ROM 11:9](https://ref.ly/Acts11:9)1

88\.306 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sin, Wrongdoing, Guilt

that which causes someone to sin, one who causes someone to sin (a figurative extension of meaning of σκάνδαλον\[a] ‘trap,’ [6\.25](#6.25)) that which or one who causes someone to sin

[MAT 13:41](https://ref.ly/Matt13:41) · [MAT 18:7](https://ref.ly/Matt18:7) · [MAT 18:7](https://ref.ly/Matt18:7) · [MAT 18:7](https://ref.ly/Matt18:7) · [LUK 17:1](https://ref.ly/Mark17:1) · [ROM 9:33](https://ref.ly/Acts9:33) · [ROM 14:13](https://ref.ly/Acts14:13) · [1PE 2:8](https://ref.ly/Jas2:8) · [1JN 2:10](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:10) · [REV 2:14](https://ref.ly/Jude2:14)

25\.181 · Attitudes and Emotions · Offend, Be Offended

what causes offense, offense that which causes offense and thus arouses opposition

[MAT 16:23](https://ref.ly/Matt16:23) · [ROM 16:17](https://ref.ly/Acts16:17) · [1CO 1:23](https://ref.ly/Rom1:23) · [GAL 5:11](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:11)

1 ROM 11:9 In [ROM 11:9](https://ref.ly/Acts11:9) παγίς ([6\.23](#6.23)), θήρα ([6\.24](#6.24)), and σκάνδαλον ([6\.25](#6.25)) are all treated as having literal meanings, whereas the passage as a whole is figurative.

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 11:9; Matthew 13:41; Matthew 18:7; Luke 17:1; Romans 9:33; Romans 14:13; 1 Peter 2:8; 1 John 2:10; Revelation 2:14; Matthew 16:23; Romans 16:17; 1 Corinthians 1:23; Galatians 5:11

6\.2 · Artifacts · Artifacts \[General Meaning]

## σκεῦος (id: 004536000000000)

σκεῦος
======

σκεῦος (G4632)

noun, n. \| \-ους \| ἀπαρασκεύαστος · ἐπισκευάζομαι · κατασκευάζω · παρασκευάζω · παρασκευή · σκευή

6\.1 · Artifacts · Artifacts \[General Meaning]

object, thing any kind of instrument, tool, weapon, equipment, container, or property The manner in which σκεῦος\[a] is translated depends in many instances upon the specific context. It may, of course, be rendered by a highly generic expression such as English ‘thing,’ but wherever the context refers to some particular type of object, it is preferable to employ a specific referent. In [ACT 27:17](https://ref.ly/John27:17), for example, the reference of σκεῦος is generally understood to be the mainsail.

[MAT 12:29](https://ref.ly/Matt12:29) · [MRK 11:16](https://ref.ly/Matt11:16) · [ACT 10:11](https://ref.ly/John10:11) · [ACT 10:16](https://ref.ly/John10:16) · [ACT 27:17](https://ref.ly/John27:17) · [HEB 9:21](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:21)

6\.118 · Artifacts · Containers

vessel, container a highly generic term for any kind of jar, bowl, basket, or vase In [ACT 10:11](https://ref.ly/John10:11) and [ACT 10:16](https://ref.ly/John10:16) σκεῦος\[b] refers to a sheet (as a container) which was let down from heaven in Peter’s vision.  
In a number of languages there is no relatively high generic term which may be used to refer to any type of vessel or container, and therefore one must employ more specific terms depending upon the context, even as in the case of most English translations in [ACT 10:11](https://ref.ly/John10:11), [REV 2:27](https://ref.ly/Jude2:27), and [LUK 8:16](https://ref.ly/Mark8:16).

[LUK 8:16](https://ref.ly/Mark8:16) · [JHN 19:29](https://ref.ly/Luke19:29) · [ACT 10:11](https://ref.ly/John10:11) · [ACT 10:16](https://ref.ly/John10:16) · [ACT 11:5](https://ref.ly/John11:5) · [ROM 9:21](https://ref.ly/Acts9:21) · [2CO 4:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:7) · [2TI 2:20](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:20) · [2TI 2:21](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:21) · [HEB 9:21](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:21) · [REV 2:27](https://ref.ly/Jude2:27) · [REV 18:12](https://ref.ly/Jude18:12) · [REV 18:12](https://ref.ly/Jude18:12)

57\.20 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Have, Possess, Property, Owner

goods, belongings, household furnishings objects which are possessed

[MRK 3:27](https://ref.ly/Matt3:27) · [LUK 17:31](https://ref.ly/Mark17:31)

9\.21 · People · Human Beings

person (a figurative extension of meaning of σκεῦος\[a] ‘instrument, thing,’ [6\.1](#6.1)) a person in relation to a particular function or role

[ACT 9:15](https://ref.ly/John9:15) · [ROM 9:22](https://ref.ly/Acts9:22) · [ROM 9:23](https://ref.ly/Acts9:23)

8\.6 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Body

body (a figurative extension of meaning of σκεῦος\[a] ‘object, thing, instrument,’ [6\.1](#6.1), or of σκεῦος\[b] ‘vessel,’ [6\.118](#6.118)) the human body It is also possible to interpret σκεῦος in [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) as meaning ‘wife,’ and for a discussion of this meaning and some of the problems involved in translation, see [10\.55](#10.55). A further alternative meaning, and one closely related to the meaning of ‘body’ is ‘sexual life,’ so that this expression in [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) might be rendered as ‘each of you must gain mastery over his sexual life’ or, in the form τὸ ἑαυτοῦ σκεῦος κτᾶσθαι ἐν ἁγιασμῷ καὶ τιμῇ, ‘your sexual life should be holy and honorable’ (see [23\.63](#23.63)).

[1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) · [1PE 3:7](https://ref.ly/Jas3:7)

10\.55 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Based upon Marriage

wife (a figurative extension of meaning of σκεῦος\[b] ‘vessel,’ [6\.118](#6.118)) a woman married to a man, with focus upon the sexual relation The interpretation of σκεῦος in [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) has given rise to serious divisions of opinion as noted in [8\.6](#8.6), where σκεῦος is interpreted as designating a person’s own body. The interpretation of σκεῦος as ‘wife’ is based upon a number of considerations. In the first place, the verb κτᾶσθαι ‘to get, to acquire’ ([57\.58](#57.58)) does not normally go with ‘body,’ while it fits well with the meaning of ‘wife.’ On the other hand, σκεῦος meaning ‘wife’ is nowhere else attested in Greek but is assumed in [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) to refer to a wife primarily on the strength of the particular interpretation of the context, in which πορνεία ‘immorality’ ([88\.271](#88.271)) in verse 3 and and ἐν πάθει ἐπιθυμίας ‘with a lustful desire’ ([25\.30](#25.30)) in verse 5 are assumed to point to the meaning of σκεῦος as ‘wife.’ In ancient Jewish literature a wife was euphemistically called a ‘vessel’ in contexts relating to sexual relations, and ‘vessel’ is a very common meaning of σκεῦος in Greek. If, therefore, one assumes a Semitic background for this Greek text, the statement in [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) would refer to the need for sexual life to be both holy and honorable (see [23\.63](#23.63)).

[1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4)

23\.63 · Physiological Processes and States · Sexual Relations

**Collocation:** σκεῦος κτάομαι

sexual life (an idiom, literally: to possess a vessel) a euphemistic manner of referring to sexual relations It is also possible to understand σκεῦος in [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) as one’s wife (see [10\.55](#10.55)). σκεῦος in [1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4) may also be understood as one’s body, and therefore the phrase τὸ ἑαυτοῦ σκεῦος κτᾶσθαι may be rendered as ‘to control his own body’ (see [8\.6](#8.6)).

[1TH 4:4](https://ref.ly/Col4:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:29; Mark 11:16; Acts 10:11; Acts 10:16; Acts 27:17; Hebrews 9:21; Luke 8:16; John 19:29; Acts 11:5; Romans 9:21; 2 Corinthians 4:7; 2 Timothy 2:20; 2 Timothy 2:21; Revelation 2:27; Revelation 18:12; Mark 3:27; Luke 17:31; Acts 9:15; Romans 9:22; Romans 9:23; 1 Thessalonians 4:4; 1 Peter 3:7


## σκηνή (id: 004537000000000)

σκηνή
=====

σκηνή (G4633)

noun, f. \| \-ῆς \| σκηνόω

7\.9 · Constructions · Buildings

tent a portable dwelling of cloth and/or skins, held up by poles and fastened by cords to stakes In a number of languages ‘tent’ is simply ‘a house made of cloth.’ One should avoid terms which would imply a military tent or a temporary shelter used only on vacations or holidays. In OT times such tents were permanent dwellings of nomadic groups and were moved from place to place as livestock were transferred from one pasture area to another.

[MAT 17:4](https://ref.ly/Matt17:4) · [MRK 9:5](https://ref.ly/Matt9:5) · [LUK 9:33](https://ref.ly/Mark9:33) · [LUK 16:9](https://ref.ly/Mark16:9) · [ACT 7:43](https://ref.ly/John7:43) · [HEB 11:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:9)

7\.17 · Constructions · Buildings

tent, tabernacle tent the relatively large tent used as a central place of worship by the Jews prior to the building of the Temple In a number of languages σκηνή\[b] may be rendered as ‘the largest tent in which God lived’ or ‘the large tent for worshiping God’ or ‘the holy tent.’ In selecting a proper designation for σκηνή\[b], it is important to indicate that the function of σκηνή\[b] was essentially the same as that of the Temple; it was only a different type of construction and not a difference of use or of religious relevance.  
Since σκηνή\[b] refers to one unique object, it is essentially equivalent to a title.

[ACT 7:44](https://ref.ly/John7:44) · [ACT 15:16](https://ref.ly/John15:16) · [HEB 8:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:2) · [HEB 8:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:5) · [HEB 9:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:2) · [HEB 9:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:3) · [HEB 9:6](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:6) · [HEB 9:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:8) · [HEB 9:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:11) · [HEB 9:21](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:21) · [HEB 13:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:10) · [REV 13:6](https://ref.ly/Jude13:6) · [REV 15:5](https://ref.ly/Jude15:5) · [REV 21:3](https://ref.ly/Jude21:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 17:4; Mark 9:5; Luke 9:33; Luke 16:9; Acts 7:43; Hebrews 11:9; Acts 7:44; Acts 15:16; Hebrews 8:2; Hebrews 8:5; Hebrews 9:2; Hebrews 9:3; Hebrews 9:6; Hebrews 9:8; Hebrews 9:11; Hebrews 9:21; Hebrews 13:10; Revelation 13:6; Revelation 15:5; Revelation 21:3

## σκῆνος (id: 004540000000000)

σκῆνος
======

σκῆνος (G4636)

noun, n. \| \-ους \| σκηνόω

8\.5 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Body

body (figurative extension of meaning of σκῆνος ‘tent,’ not occurring in the NT) temporary habitation in the human body Only rarely can one preserve in translation the figurative meanings suggested by the terms σκῆνος and σκήνωμα. What is significant in such contexts is the temporary nature of the dwelling, and therefore the relatively brief time which the body is to serve the person who dwells in it. In some cases it may be relevant, therefore, to have a footnote to point out the temporal aspects of this figurative usage of σκῆνος and σκήνωμα\[c] .

[2CO 5:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:1) · [2CO 5:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:4)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 5:1; 2 Corinthians 5:4


## σκηνόω (id: 004541000000000)

σκηνόω
======

σκηνόω (G4637)

verb \| ἐπισκηνόω · κατασκηνόω · κατασκήνωσις · σκηνή · σκηνοπηγία · σκηνοποιός · σκῆνος · σκήνωμα

85\.75 · Existence in Space · Dwell, Reside

to take up residence, to come to reside, to come to dwell to come to dwell in a place defined psychologically or spiritually (with the possible implication in some contexts of a temporary arrangement) In all of these contexts, σκηνόω and ἐπισκηνόω are essentially figurative in meaning, for they deal with spiritual existence and residence rather than human residence or dwelling. In translating one should, in so far as possible, try to preserve this important figurative relationship, since it expresses one of the most significant ways in which spiritual and human existence can be combined. In some languages, however, it may be necessary to employ an expression which means simply ‘to be in’ or ‘to continue with,’ since expressions for ‘living’ or ‘dwelling’ may be based upon terms which are too specific in meaning, for example, ‘to eat from the same pot’ or ‘to enter by the same door.’

[JHN 1:14](https://ref.ly/Luke1:14) · [REV 7:15](https://ref.ly/Jude7:15) · [REV 12:12](https://ref.ly/Jude12:12) · [REV 13:6](https://ref.ly/Jude13:6) · [REV 21:3](https://ref.ly/Jude21:3)

* **Associated Passages:** John 1:14; Revelation 7:15; Revelation 12:12; Revelation 13:6; Revelation 21:3


## σκήνωμα (id: 004542000000000)

σκήνωμα
=======

σκήνωμα (G4638)

noun, n. \| \-τος \| σκηνόω

7\.8 · Constructions · Buildings

dwelling a dwelling, with the implication of temporary duration In [ACT 7:46](https://ref.ly/John7:46) there is a complex textual problem in which the critical text has τῷ οἴκῳ Ἰακώβ ‘the house of Jacob’ (but in the figurative sense of ‘people’), but the Byzantine text reads τῷ θεῷ Ἰακώβ ‘the God of Jacob.’ It is only with this latter form of the text that σκήνωμα would mean an actual construction or dwelling. If one adopts the form of the critical text, then σκήνωμα would point to ‘a place to dwell,’ in other words, an area or region (see [85\.77](#85.77)).

[ACT 7:46](https://ref.ly/John7:46)

85\.77 · Existence in Space · Dwell, Reside

dwelling place, temporary dwelling place (derivative of σκηνόω ‘to take up residence,’ [85\.75](#85.75)) a place where one may dwell, with the possible implication in certain contexts of something which is of temporary duration An alternative reading of the expression σκήνωμα τῷ οἴκῳ Ἰακώβ ‘dwelling place for the people of Jacob’ in [ACT 7:46](https://ref.ly/John7:46) has θεῷ for οἴκῳ (see [7\.8](#7.8)) and the consequent translation ‘a house for the God of Jacob.’  
For another interpretation of σκήνωμα in [2PE 1:14](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:14), see [8\.5](#8.5).

[ACT 7:46](https://ref.ly/John7:46) · [2PE 1:14](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:14)

8\.5 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Body

body (figurative extension of meaning of σκήνωμα\[a] ‘temporary dwelling,’ [7\.8](#7.8)) temporary habitation in the human body Only rarely can one preserve in translation the figurative meanings suggested by the terms σκῆνος and σκήνωμα. What is significant in such contexts is the temporary nature of the dwelling, and therefore the relatively brief time which the body is to serve the person who dwells in it. In some cases it may be relevant, therefore, to have a footnote to point out the temporal aspects of this figurative usage of σκῆνος and σκήνωμα\[c] .  
It is also possible to interpret σκήνωμα in [2PE 1:14](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:14) as meaning a temporary habitation, though referring, of course, to the human body (see [85\.77](#85.77)).

[2PE 1:13](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:13) · [2PE 1:14](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:14)

23\.91 · Physiological Processes and States · Live, Die

**Collocation:** εἶναι ἐν σκηνώματι

to be alive (an idiom, literally: to be in a dwelling, see [7\.8](#7.8)) to be alive, with special emphasis upon physical existence on earth Most languages have rather generic expressions for ‘life’ or ‘to live,’ but sometimes there are idiomatic expressions which may readily fit the types of contexts illustrated by [2CO 5:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:6) and [2PE 1:13](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:13), for example, ‘to have strength,’ ‘to have one’s eyes,’ and ‘to walk about on the earth.’

[2PE 1:13](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 7:46; 2 Peter 1:14; 2 Peter 1:13


## σκιά (id: 004543000000000)

σκιά
====

σκιά (G4639)

noun, f. \| \-ᾶς \| ἀποσκίασμα · ἐπισκιάζω · κατασκιάζω

14\.60 · Physical Events and States · Darkness

shade shade, as a shelter from light and the heat associated with light A term for ‘shade’ as an area sheltered from the direct rays of the sun usually differs from a term for ‘shadow,’ which is cast by a particular object blocking rays of light (see [14\.61](#14.61)).

[MRK 4:32](https://ref.ly/Matt4:32)

14\.61 · Physical Events and States · Darkness

shadow the shape or shade cast by an object which blocks rays of light In [LUK 1:79](https://ref.ly/Mark1:79) (τοῖς ἐν σκότει καὶ σκιᾷ θανάτου καθημένοις ‘those living in the darkness and shadow of death’), σκιά may be interpreted as being used figuratively of a shadow cast by impending death, that is to say, death is personified in such a way as to suggest that it casts a shadow because of its nearness. One may, therefore, translate τοῖς ἐν σκότει καὶ σκιᾷ θανάτου καθημένοις as ‘those who live in the darkness of impending death,’ in which case σκιά becomes essentially equivalent to an expression of time.  
In a number of languages a term for ‘shadow’ has a number of very important meanings. In some instances it is regarded as a part of personality which goes on to the next world, since a dead person no longer ‘casts a shadow.’ The shadow may also be regarded as a kind of counterpart of the personality, a type of alter ego. In cases of severe illness one may say ‘his shadow has walked away,’ and in many parts of the world the shadow of a person is an important element in the practice of black magic, for to damage a shadow may be regarded as a means of causing harm to a person.

[MAT 4:16](https://ref.ly/Matt4:16) · [LUK 1:79](https://ref.ly/Mark1:79) · [ACT 5:15](https://ref.ly/John5:15) · [HEB 10:1](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:1)

58\.65 · Nature, Class, Example · Archetype, Corresponding Type \[Antitype]

foreshadow, faint prototype, shadow a faint archetype which foreshadows a later reality

[COL 2:17](https://ref.ly/Phil2:17) · [HEB 8:5](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:5)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 4:32; Matthew 4:16; Luke 1:79; Acts 5:15; Hebrews 10:1; Colossians 2:17; Hebrews 8:5


## σκιρτάω (id: 004544000000000)

σκιρτάω
=======

σκιρτάω (G4640)

verb

15\.243 · Linear Movement · Jump, Leap

to jump for joy, to leap for joy to leap or jump, as a possible expression of joy and happiness For a difference of semantic focus see [25\.134](#25.134)).  
In [LUK 1:41](https://ref.ly/Mark1:41) σκιρτάω may be regarded as an instance of figurative usage: ἐσκίρτησεν τὸ βρέφος ἐν τῇ κοιλίᾳ αὐτῆς ‘the baby leaped for joy in her womb.’  
Though it may seem quite natural to speak of ‘leaping for joy,’ in some cultures this would not be a meaningful combination of words, for leaping might suggest anger, ritual exorcism (driving out demons), or preparation for war. It may, therefore, be necessary in some languages to translate ‘jump for joy’ merely as ‘be exceedingly glad.’ It may be particularly awkward to speak of a fetus jumping in the womb, for obviously it would simply be a rapid movement of the limbs and not actual change of location. Therefore, it may be better to translate in some instances ‘moved quickly to show joy’ or ‘... as a sign of happiness.’

[LUK 1:41](https://ref.ly/Mark1:41) · [LUK 1:44](https://ref.ly/Mark1:44) · [LUK 6:23](https://ref.ly/Mark6:23)

25\.134 · Attitudes and Emotions · Happy, Glad, Joyful

to be extremely joyful, to dance for joy (a figurative extension of meaning of σκιρτάω\[a] ‘to jump for joy,’ [15\.243](#15.243)) to be extremely happy, possibly implying in some contexts actually leaping or dancing for joy χάρητε ἐν ἐκείνω τῇ ἡμέρᾳ καὶ σκιρτήσατε ‘be glad when that happens and dance for joy’ [LUK 6:23](https://ref.ly/Mark6:23), but see also [15\.243](#15.243) for a different semantic focus. The phrase ‘for joy’ clearly expresses ‘reason,’ and therefore it may be useful to translate ‘dance for joy’ as ‘dance because I am so joyful’ or ‘... so happy.’

[LUK 6:23](https://ref.ly/Mark6:23)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:41; Luke 1:44; Luke 6:23


## σκληροκαρδία (id: 004545000000000)

σκληροκαρδία
============

σκληροκαρδία (G4641)

noun, f. \| \-ας \| σκληρύνω \+ καρδία

88\.224 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Stubbornness

stubborn, completely unyielding pertaining to being obdurate and obstinate1 In the contexts illustrated by σκληροτράχηλος, ἀπερίτμητος καρδίᾳ καὶ τοῖς ὠσίν, and σκληροκαρδία, the focus of the stubbornness and obstinacy is the unwillingness to be taught or to understand.

[MAT 19:8](https://ref.ly/Matt19:8) · [MRK 10:5](https://ref.ly/Matt10:5) · [MRK 16:14](https://ref.ly/Matt16:14)
