## σκοπέω (id: 004552000000000)

σκοπέω
======

σκοπέω (G4648)

verb \| ἀλλοτριεπίσκοπος · ἐπισκέπτομαι · ἐπισκοπέω · ἐπισκοπή · ἐπίσκοπος · κατασκοπέω · κατάσκοπος · σκοπός

24\.32 · Sensory Events and States · See

to watch, to notice carefully to continue to regard closely It is also possible to understand σκοπέω in [ROM 16:17](https://ref.ly/Acts16:17) as being predominantly a mental process of paying close attention in order to be prepared to respond appropriately (see [27\.58](#27.58)).

[ROM 16:17](https://ref.ly/Acts16:17) · [PHP 3:17](https://ref.ly/Eph3:17)

27\.58 · Learn · Be Ready To Learn, Pay Attention

to beware of, to watch out for, to pay attention to (figurative extension of meaning of σκοπέω\[a] ‘to notice carefully,’ [24\.32](#24.32)) to be ready to learn about future dangers or needs, with the implication of preparedness to respond appropriately

[LUK 11:35](https://ref.ly/Mark11:35) · [ROM 16:17](https://ref.ly/Acts16:17) · [GAL 6:1](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:1)

27\.36 · Learn · Try To Learn

to be aware of, to be concerned about, to consider to exert effort in continually acquiring information regarding some matter, with the implication of concern as to how to respond appropriately

[PHP 2:4](https://ref.ly/Eph2:4)

30\.20 · Think · To Think, Thought

to ponder, to let one’s mind dwell on, to keep thinking about, to fix one’s attention on to keep on giving serious consideration to something

[2CO 4:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 16:17; Philippians 3:17; Luke 11:35; Galatians 6:1; Philippians 2:4; 2 Corinthians 4:18


## σκοπός (id: 004553000000000)

σκοπός
======

σκοπός (G4649)

noun, m. \| \-οῦ \| σκοπέω

84\.28 · Spacial Extensions · Extension To a Goal

goal that toward which movement or activity is directed The context of σκοπός in [PHP 3:14](https://ref.ly/Eph3:14) is highly figurative, and in some languages it may be better rendered as ‘what I seek to achieve’ or ‘what I wish to accomplish.’ For σκοπός in the idiom κατὰ σκοπὸν διώκω, see [89\.56](#89.56).

[PHP 3:14](https://ref.ly/Eph3:14)

* **Associated Passages:** Philippians 3:14


## σκορπίζω (id: 004554000000000)

σκορπίζω
========

σκορπίζω (G4650)

verb \| διασκορπίζω

15\.135 · Linear Movement · Disperse, Scatter

to scatter, to cause to disperse to cause a group or a gathering to disperse or scatter

[MAT 12:30](https://ref.ly/Matt12:30) · [LUK 11:23](https://ref.ly/Mark11:23) · [JHN 10:12](https://ref.ly/Luke10:12) · [JHN 16:32](https://ref.ly/Luke16:32)

57\.95 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

to give generously, to distribute generously (a figurative extension of meaning of σκορπίζω\[a] ‘to scatter,’ [15\.135](#15.135)) to give or distribute generously or in abundance In a number of languages ‘to give generously’ may simply be rendered as ‘to give much often,’ but one may sometimes employ such figurative expressions as ‘to give from a full heart’ or ‘to give without holding back anything.‘

[2CO 9:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:9)1

1 2CO 9:9 In view of the fact that σκορπίζω in [2CO 9:9](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:9) is a quotation based on the rendering of the Hebrew text of [PSA 112:9](https://ref.ly/Ps112:9), it is possible that σκορπίζω is only used figuratively in this context.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 12:30; Luke 11:23; John 10:12; John 16:32; 2 Corinthians 9:9


## σκορπίος (id: 004555000000000)

σκορπίος
========

σκορπίος (G4651)

noun, m. \| \-ου

4\.56 · Animals · Reptiles and Other 'Creeping Things'

scorpion terrestrial arachnid (eight\-legged) with pincers and a poisonous sting at the end of its jointed tail, which it can hold curved over the back; grows to about 13 cm long; known for the pain and danger of its sting, and associated with harsh, inhospitable living conditions In the two NT occurrences of σκορπίος ([REV 9:5](https://ref.ly/Jude9:5)), the emphasis is upon the stinging capacity of the scorpion, and if in a particular area of the world scorpions are not known, it is possible to use a descriptive phrase such as ‘a fierce, stinging, little creature.’

[LUK 10:19](https://ref.ly/Mark10:19) · [LUK 11:12](https://ref.ly/Mark11:12) · [REV 9:3](https://ref.ly/Jude9:3) · [REV 9:5](https://ref.ly/Jude9:5) · [REV 9:10](https://ref.ly/Jude9:10)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 10:19; Luke 11:12; Revelation 9:3; Revelation 9:5; Revelation 9:10

adjc. \| \-ή, \-όν

14\.54 · Physical Events and States · Darkness

dark, in darkness pertaining to being in a state of darkness In some languages ‘dark’ may be most satisfactorily expressed as ‘without light.’

## σκοτία (id: 004557000000000)

σκοτία
======

σκοτία (G4653)

noun, f. \| \-ας \| σκοτίζομαι

14\.53 · Physical Events and States · Darkness

**Collocation:** ἐν τῇ σκοτίᾳ

darkness a condition resulting from the partial or complete absence of light (see [14\.36](#14.36)) In a number of languages it is impossible to speak of ‘darkness’ as being an agent in the sense of [LUK 23:44](https://ref.ly/Mark23:44) ‘darkness covered the whole country.’ Accordingly, one must say ‘throughout the whole country it was dark’ or ‘it darkened over the whole country.’ In some languages darkness may be characterized as being a quality of the night, for example, ‘it was like night.’

[MAT 10:27](https://ref.ly/Matt10:27) · [LUK 12:3](https://ref.ly/Mark12:3) · [JHN 6:17](https://ref.ly/Luke6:17) · [JHN 12:35](https://ref.ly/Luke12:35) · [JHN 20:1](https://ref.ly/Luke20:1) · [1JN 1:5](https://ref.ly/2Pet1:5)

88\.125 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Bad, Evil, Harmful, Damaging

evil world, realm of evil, darkness (figurative extension of meaning σκοτία\[a] ‘darkness,’ [14\.53](#14.53)) the realm of sin and evil

[JHN 1:5](https://ref.ly/Luke1:5) · [JHN 1:5](https://ref.ly/Luke1:5) · [JHN 8:12](https://ref.ly/Luke8:12) · [JHN 12:35](https://ref.ly/Luke12:35) · [JHN 12:46](https://ref.ly/Luke12:46) · [1JN 1:5](https://ref.ly/2Pet1:5) · [1JN 2:8](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:8) · [1JN 2:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:9) · [1JN 2:11](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:11) · [1JN 2:11](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:11) · [1JN 2:11](https://ref.ly/2Pet2:11)

28\.71 · Know · Not Able To Be Known, Secret

in secret, in private, secretly, privately pertaining to not being able to be known by the public but known by some in\-group or by those immediately involved

[MAT 10:27](https://ref.ly/Matt10:27) · [LUK 12:3](https://ref.ly/Mark12:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 10:27; Luke 12:3; John 6:17; John 12:35; John 20:1; 1 John 1:5; John 1:5; John 8:12; John 12:46; 1 John 2:8; 1 John 2:9; 1 John 2:11


## σκοτίζω (id: 004558000000000)

σκοτίζω
=======

σκοτίζω (G4654) — σκοτίζομαι

verb \| σκοτεινός · σκοτία · σκοτόομαι · σκότος

14\.55 · (σκοτίζομαι\[a]) · Physical Events and States · Darkness

to become dark (derivative of σκοτία\[a] ‘darkness,’ [14\.53](#14.53)) to change from a condition of being light to one of being dark In [REV 9:2](https://ref.ly/Jude9:2) it may not be difficult to speak of ‘the air becoming dark,’ since this would mean the space above the earth, but it may be difficult to speak of ‘the sun becoming dark.’ In the latter instance, for both [REV 9:2](https://ref.ly/Jude9:2) and [MAT 24:29](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29), one may say ‘the sun will no longer shine’ or ‘the sun will not give its light.’  
In place of ‘the air became dark,’ it is also possible to speak of ‘the sky will become dark.’

[MAT 24:29](https://ref.ly/Matt24:29) · [MRK 13:24](https://ref.ly/Matt13:24) · [REV 8:12](https://ref.ly/Jude8:12)

32\.44 · (σκοτίζομαι\[b]) · Understand · Lack of Capacity for Understanding

to be incapable of perceiving, to not be able to understand (figurative extension of meaning of σκοτίζω\[a] ‘to become dark,’ [14\.55](#14.55)) to become unable to perceive and thus unable to understand It is rare that one can combine the concept of ‘becoming dark’ with incapacity to understand or comprehend. Sometimes a parallel figure of speech may be employed by using an expression such as ‘to not be able to see.’ For example, in [ROM 1:21](https://ref.ly/Acts1:21) it is sometimes possible to translate ‘their foolish minds became unable to see the truth,’ and in [EPH 4:18](https://ref.ly/Gal4:18) it is sometimes possible to translate ‘they were not able to see with their minds.’

[ROM 1:21](https://ref.ly/Acts1:21) · [ROM 11:10](https://ref.ly/Acts11:10)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 24:29; Mark 13:24; Revelation 8:12; Romans 1:21; Romans 11:10


## σκότος (id: 004559000000000)

σκότος
======

σκότος (G4655)

noun, n. \| \-ους \| σκοτίζομαι

14\.53 · Physical Events and States · Darkness

darkness a condition resulting from the partial or complete absence of light (see [14\.36](#14.36)) In a number of languages it is impossible to speak of ‘darkness’ as being an agent in the sense of [LUK 23:44](https://ref.ly/Mark23:44) ‘darkness covered the whole country.’ Accordingly, one must say ‘throughout the whole country it was dark’ or ‘it darkened over the whole country.’ In some languages darkness may be characterized as being a quality of the night, for example, ‘it was like night.’

[MAT 27:45](https://ref.ly/Matt27:45) · [MRK 15:33](https://ref.ly/Matt15:33) · [LUK 1:79](https://ref.ly/Mark1:79) · [LUK 11:35](https://ref.ly/Mark11:35) · [LUK 22:53](https://ref.ly/Mark22:53) · [LUK 23:44](https://ref.ly/Mark23:44) · [ACT 2:20](https://ref.ly/John2:20) · [ACT 13:11](https://ref.ly/John13:11) · [1CO 4:5](https://ref.ly/Rom4:5) · [2CO 4:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:6) · [1TH 5:4](https://ref.ly/Col5:4) · [1TH 5:5](https://ref.ly/Col5:5) · [1JN 1:6](https://ref.ly/2Pet1:6)

88\.125 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Bad, Evil, Harmful, Damaging

evil world, realm of evil, darkness (figurative extension of meaning of σκότος\[a] ‘darkness,’ [14\.53](#14.53)) the realm of sin and evil It is possible that in [COL 1:13](https://ref.ly/Phil1:13) σκότος\[b] is a figurative reference to the Devil or Satan, since ἐκ τῆς ἐξουσίας τοῦ σκότους is in a parallel relationship with τὴν βασιλείαν τοῦ υἱοῦ τῆς ἀγάπης αὐτοῦ.

[MAT 6:23](https://ref.ly/Matt6:23) · [MAT 6:23](https://ref.ly/Matt6:23) · [JHN 3:19](https://ref.ly/Luke3:19) · [ACT 26:18](https://ref.ly/John26:18) · [ROM 2:19](https://ref.ly/Acts2:19) · [ROM 13:12](https://ref.ly/Acts13:12) · [1CO 4:5](https://ref.ly/Rom4:5) · [2CO 6:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:14) · [EPH 5:8](https://ref.ly/Gal5:8) · [EPH 5:11](https://ref.ly/Gal5:11) · [EPH 6:12](https://ref.ly/Gal6:12) · [COL 1:13](https://ref.ly/Phil1:13) · [1TH 5:4](https://ref.ly/Col5:4) · [1PE 2:9](https://ref.ly/Jas2:9) · [2PE 2:17](https://ref.ly/1Pet2:17) · [1JN 1:6](https://ref.ly/2Pet1:6)

1\.24 · Geographical Objects and Features · Regions Below the Surface of the Earth

**Collocation:** ὁ ζόφος τοῦ σκότους

gloomy hell, black darkness (an idiom, literally: the gloom of darkness) the dark, gloomy nature of hell as a place of punishment

[JUD 1:13](https://ref.ly/3John1:13)

1\.23 · Geographical Objects and Features · Regions Below the Surface of the Earth

**Collocation:** τὸ σκότος τὸ ἐξώτερον

outer darkness, darkness outside (an idiom, literally: the outer darkness) a place or region which is both dark and removed (presumably from the abode of the righteous) and serving as the abode of evil spirits and devils In a number of languages this expression in [MAT 8:12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:12) must be rendered as ‘they will be thrown outside where it is dark.’

[MAT 8:12](https://ref.ly/Matt8:12) · [MAT 22:13](https://ref.ly/Matt22:13) · [MAT 25:30](https://ref.ly/Matt25:30)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:45; Mark 15:33; Luke 1:79; Luke 11:35; Luke 22:53; Luke 23:44; Acts 2:20; Acts 13:11; 1 Corinthians 4:5; 2 Corinthians 4:6; 1 Thessalonians 5:4; 1 Thessalonians 5:5; 1 John 1:6; Matthew 6:23; John 3:19; Acts 26:18; Romans 2:19; Romans 13:12; 2 Corinthians 6:14; Ephesians 5:8; Ephesians 5:11; Ephesians 6:12; Colossians 1:13; 1 Peter 2:9; 2 Peter 2:17; Jude 1:13; Matthew 8:12; Matthew 22:13; Matthew 25:30

## σκώληξ (id: 004567000000000)

σκώληξ
======

σκώληξ (G4663)

noun, m. \| \-ηκος \| σκωληκόβρωτος

4\.57 · Animals · Reptiles and Other 'Creeping Things'

maggot, worm small, soft, legless, tube\-shaped creatures that have no bones or shells. They typically feed on overripe fruit, rotting meat, and similar things; most are larvae that hatch from the eggs laid by flies or some beetles; symbols of uncleanness, decay, and death In [MRK 9:48](https://ref.ly/Matt9:48) the reference is clearly to the type of maggots which feed on refuse.  
In a number of languages a very important distinction is made between three different types of worms: (1\) maggots, (2\) worms that live in the ground, so\-called ‘earthworms,’ and (3\) intestinal worms. It is essential that an appropriate term be employed in order to avoid meaninglessness or misunderstanding.

[MRK 9:48](https://ref.ly/Matt9:48)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 9:48

## σμύρνα (id: 004571000000000)

σμύρνα
======

noun, f. \| \-ης

6\.208 · Artifacts · Perfumes and Incense

myrrh the aromatic resin of certain bushes Myrrh was used as one of the ingredients involved in the process of embalming a corpse. Most translators borrow a term for myrrh and then use some kind of marginal note to explain that myrrh was a valuable aromatic substance often used in preserving a corpse. See [6\.204](#6.204).

## σμυρνίζω (id: 004573000000000)

σμυρνίζω
========

σμυρνίζω (G4669)

verb \| σμύρνα

6\.204 · Artifacts · Medicines

**Collocation:** ἐσμυρνισμένος οἶνος

myrrhed wine wine drugged with myrrh and used as a stupefying potion1 In general, ἐσμυρνισμένος οἶνος must be rendered by means of a phrase or a clause, for example, ‘wine which has been mixed with a drug called myrrh’ or ‘wine mixed with a drug to reduce pain.’ It is, of course, also possible to use an abbreviated phrase such as ‘myrrhed wine’ and then to place the explanation of its function in a marginal note.

[MRK 15:23](https://ref.ly/Matt15:23)

1 The term ἐσμυρνισμένος οἶνος can be seen as semantically endocentric (σμυρνίζω, ‘mixed with myrrh’ and οἶνος, ‘wine’). However, due to its specific role in the passage of [MRK 15:23](https://ref.ly/Matt15:23), it was included in this semantic field.

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 15:23

[MAT 11:19](https://ref.ly/Matt11:19) · [MAT 13:54](https://ref.ly/Matt13:54) · [MRK 6:2](https://ref.ly/Matt6:2) · [LUK 11:31](https://ref.ly/Mark11:31) · [LUK 21:15](https://ref.ly/Mark21:15) · [ACT 6:3](https://ref.ly/John6:3) · [ACT 6:10](https://ref.ly/John6:10) · [ACT 7:10](https://ref.ly/John7:10) · [ROM 11:33](https://ref.ly/Acts11:33) · [1CO 1:21](https://ref.ly/Rom1:21) · [1CO 1:21](https://ref.ly/Rom1:21) · [1CO 1:22](https://ref.ly/Rom1:22) · [1CO 1:24](https://ref.ly/Rom1:24) · [1CO 1:30](https://ref.ly/Rom1:30) · [1CO 2:7](https://ref.ly/Rom2:7) · [1CO 12:8](https://ref.ly/Rom12:8) · [2CO 1:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:12) · [EPH 1:8](https://ref.ly/Gal1:8) · [EPH 1:17](https://ref.ly/Gal1:17) · [EPH 3:10](https://ref.ly/Gal3:10) · [COL 1:9](https://ref.ly/Phil1:9) · [COL 1:28](https://ref.ly/Phil1:28) · [COL 2:23](https://ref.ly/Phil2:23) · [COL 3:16](https://ref.ly/Phil3:16) · [COL 4:5](https://ref.ly/Phil4:5) · [JAS 1:5](https://ref.ly/Heb1:5) · [JAS 3:13](https://ref.ly/Heb3:13) · [REV 7:12](https://ref.ly/Jude7:12) · [REV 13:18](https://ref.ly/Jude13:18) · [REV 17:9](https://ref.ly/Jude17:9)

wisdom, insight, understanding the content of what is known by those regarded as wise

[MAT 12:42](https://ref.ly/Matt12:42) · [LUK 2:40](https://ref.ly/Mark2:40) · [LUK 2:52](https://ref.ly/Mark2:52) · [ACT 7:22](https://ref.ly/John7:22) · [1CO 2:5](https://ref.ly/Rom2:5) · [1CO 2:6](https://ref.ly/Rom2:6) · [1CO 2:6](https://ref.ly/Rom2:6) · [1CO 2:13](https://ref.ly/Rom2:13) · [1CO 3:19](https://ref.ly/Rom3:19) · [EPH 1:17](https://ref.ly/Gal1:17) · [COL 2:3](https://ref.ly/Phil2:3) · [JAS 3:15](https://ref.ly/Heb3:15) · [JAS 3:17](https://ref.ly/Heb3:17) · [2PE 3:15](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:15) · [REV 5:12](https://ref.ly/Jude5:12)

28\.8 · Know · Know

specialized knowledge, skill knowledge which makes possible skillful activity or performance It is also possible to interpret σοφία in [1CO 1:17](https://ref.ly/Rom1:17) as wisdom which makes possible correct understanding (see [32\.32](#32.32)).

[1CO 1:17](https://ref.ly/Rom1:17) · [1CO 1:19](https://ref.ly/Rom1:19) · [1CO 1:20](https://ref.ly/Rom1:20) · [1CO 2:1](https://ref.ly/Rom2:1) · [1CO 2:4](https://ref.ly/Rom2:4)

32\.41 · Understand · Capacity for Understanding

Wisdom a document or book containing wise sayings (as in the phrase ἡ σοφία τοῦ θεοῦ ‘the Wisdom of God,’ [LUK 11:49](https://ref.ly/Mark11:49), a possible reference to the OT or to apocryphal wisdom literature, possibly even a book which has been lost) If one understands ἡ σοφία τοῦ θεοῦ as being a reference to a book, one could translate the statement in [LUK 11:49](https://ref.ly/Mark11:49) as ‘for this reason, the book entitled The Wisdom of God has the words: ...’ On the other hand, the phrase ἡ σοφία τοῦ θεοῦ in [LUK 11:49](https://ref.ly/Mark11:49) may mean merely ‘God’s wisdom’ ([32\.32](#32.32)), and therefore this expression in [LUK 11:49](https://ref.ly/Mark11:49) could be rendered as ‘God in his wisdom said’ or ‘God, who is wise, said.’

[LUK 7:35](https://ref.ly/Mark7:35) · [LUK 11:49](https://ref.ly/Mark11:49)

adjc. \| \-ή, όν \| σοφίζω

adjc. \| \-οῦ \| σοφίζω

32\.35 · Understand · Capacity for Understanding

one who is wise, wise man a person of professional or semi\-professional status who is regarded as particularly capable in understanding the philosophical aspects of knowledge and experience

## σπείρω (id: 004589000000000)

σπείρω
======

σπείρω (G4687)

verb \| aor.pass.ptc. σπαρείς · pf.pass. ἔσπαρμαι \| διασπείρω · διασπορά · ἐπισπείρω · σπέρμα · σπερμολόγος · σπορά · σπόριμα · σπόρος

43\.6 · Agriculture

to sow to scatter seed over tilled ground1 In many languages there is a problem of translating σπείρω literally as ‘to scatter seed,’ since this is interpreted as an exceedingly wasteful manner of sowing, but unless one translates more or less literally and then provides some explanatory footnote, the parable loses much of its significance for many cultures.

[MAT 6:26](https://ref.ly/Matt6:26) · [MAT 13:3](https://ref.ly/Matt13:3) · [MAT 13:3](https://ref.ly/Matt13:3) · [MAT 13:4](https://ref.ly/Matt13:4) · [MAT 13:18](https://ref.ly/Matt13:18) · [MAT 13:19](https://ref.ly/Matt13:19) · [MAT 13:19](https://ref.ly/Matt13:19) · [MAT 13:20](https://ref.ly/Matt13:20) · [MAT 13:22](https://ref.ly/Matt13:22) · [MAT 13:23](https://ref.ly/Matt13:23) · [MAT 13:24](https://ref.ly/Matt13:24) · [MAT 13:27](https://ref.ly/Matt13:27) · [MAT 13:31](https://ref.ly/Matt13:31) · [MAT 13:37](https://ref.ly/Matt13:37) · [MAT 13:39](https://ref.ly/Matt13:39) · [MAT 25:24](https://ref.ly/Matt25:24) · [MAT 25:26](https://ref.ly/Matt25:26) · [MRK 4:3](https://ref.ly/Matt4:3) · [MRK 4:3](https://ref.ly/Matt4:3) · [MRK 4:4](https://ref.ly/Matt4:4) · [MRK 4:14](https://ref.ly/Matt4:14) · [MRK 4:14](https://ref.ly/Matt4:14) · [MRK 4:15](https://ref.ly/Matt4:15) · [MRK 4:15](https://ref.ly/Matt4:15) · [MRK 4:16](https://ref.ly/Matt4:16) · [MRK 4:18](https://ref.ly/Matt4:18) · [MRK 4:20](https://ref.ly/Matt4:20) · [MRK 4:31](https://ref.ly/Matt4:31) · [MRK 4:32](https://ref.ly/Matt4:32) · [LUK 8:5](https://ref.ly/Mark8:5) · [LUK 8:5](https://ref.ly/Mark8:5) · [LUK 8:5](https://ref.ly/Mark8:5) · [LUK 12:24](https://ref.ly/Mark12:24) · [LUK 19:21](https://ref.ly/Mark19:21) · [LUK 19:22](https://ref.ly/Mark19:22) · [JHN 4:36](https://ref.ly/Luke4:36) · [JHN 4:37](https://ref.ly/Luke4:37) · [1CO 9:11](https://ref.ly/Rom9:11) · [1CO 15:36](https://ref.ly/Rom15:36) · [1CO 15:37](https://ref.ly/Rom15:37) · [1CO 15:37](https://ref.ly/Rom15:37) · [1CO 15:42](https://ref.ly/Rom15:42) · [1CO 15:43](https://ref.ly/Rom15:43) · [1CO 15:43](https://ref.ly/Rom15:43) · [1CO 15:44](https://ref.ly/Rom15:44) · [2CO 9:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:6) · [2CO 9:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:6) · [2CO 9:10](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:10) · [GAL 6:7](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:7) · [GAL 6:8](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:8) · [GAL 6:8](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:8) · [JAS 3:18](https://ref.ly/Heb3:18)

1 In [MRK 4:26](https://ref.ly/Matt4:26) the phrase σπόρον βάλλω (literally ‘to throw seed’) has the same meaning as σπείρω.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 6:26; Matthew 13:3; Matthew 13:4; Matthew 13:18; Matthew 13:19; Matthew 13:20; Matthew 13:22; Matthew 13:23; Matthew 13:24; Matthew 13:27; Matthew 13:31; Matthew 13:37; Matthew 13:39; Matthew 25:24; Matthew 25:26; Mark 4:3; Mark 4:4; Mark 4:14; Mark 4:15; Mark 4:16; Mark 4:18; Mark 4:20; Mark 4:31; Mark 4:32; Luke 8:5; Luke 12:24; Luke 19:21; Luke 19:22; John 4:36; John 4:37; 1 Corinthians 9:11; 1 Corinthians 15:36; 1 Corinthians 15:37; 1 Corinthians 15:42; 1 Corinthians 15:43; 1 Corinthians 15:44; 2 Corinthians 9:6; 2 Corinthians 9:10; Galatians 6:7; Galatians 6:8; James 3:18


## σπεκουλάτωρ (id: 004590000000000)

σπεκουλάτωρ
===========

σπεκουλάτωρ (G4688)

noun, m. \| \-ορος

33\.196 · Communication · Inform, Announce

courier, messenger a soldier who acts as a courier to carry confidential information In [MRK 6:27](https://ref.ly/Matt6:27) σπεκουλάτωρ may also have the meaning of ‘executioner’ (see [20\.70](#20.70)).

[MRK 6:27](https://ref.ly/Matt6:27)

20\.70 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Kill

executioner one who carries out official executions on the basis of orders from military or government officials It is also possible to interpret σπεκουλάτωρ (a borrowing from Latin) as meaning ‘courier,’ possibly a soldier who had special duties to carry messages of a confidential nature (see [33\.196](#33.196)).

[MRK 6:27](https://ref.ly/Matt6:27)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 6:27


## σπένδω (id: 004591000000000)

σπένδω
======

σπένδω (G4689) — σπένδομαι

verb \| ἄσπονδος

53\.27 · Religious Activities · Offering, Sacrifice

to pour a libation, to pour out an offering to pour out an offering as an act of worship or ritual observance In some languages it may be almost meaningless to speak of ‘a person being poured out,’ and therefore it may be more appropriate to translate this expression in [PHP 2:17](https://ref.ly/Eph2:17) as ‘but if my blood is to be poured out upon the sacrifice.’ In [PHP 2:17](https://ref.ly/Eph2:17) and in [2TI 4:6](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:6) (the other occurrence of σπένδω in the NT), the contexts are highly figurative.

[PHP 2:17](https://ref.ly/Eph2:17) · [2TI 4:6](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Philippians 2:17; 2 Timothy 4:6


## σπέρμα (id: 004592000000000)

σπέρμα
======

σπέρμα (G4690)

noun, n. \| \-τος \| σπείρω

3\.35 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

seed the kernel part of fruit, usually grain A number of languages make distinctions between two quite different types of seed: (1\) those produced by grasses (that is to say, grains) and (2\) those produced by other types of plants, for example, beans, squash, apples, etc. In all passages employing the Greek terms in this subdomain (κόκκος, σπέρμα, σπόρος), it is best to use some expression referring to ‘grain.’

[MAT 13:24](https://ref.ly/Matt13:24) · [MAT 13:27](https://ref.ly/Matt13:27) · [MAT 13:32](https://ref.ly/Matt13:32) · [MAT 13:37](https://ref.ly/Matt13:37) · [MAT 13:38](https://ref.ly/Matt13:38) · [MRK 4:31](https://ref.ly/Matt4:31) · [1CO 15:38](https://ref.ly/Rom15:38)

10\.29 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Involving Successive Generations

posterity, descendants, offspring (a figurative extension of meaning of σπέρμα\[a] ‘seed,’ [3\.35](#3.35)) posterity, with emphasis upon the ancestors role in founding the lineage See discussion at [10\.28](#10.28).

[MAT 22:25](https://ref.ly/Matt22:25) · [MRK 12:19](https://ref.ly/Matt12:19) · [MRK 12:20](https://ref.ly/Matt12:20) · [MRK 12:21](https://ref.ly/Matt12:21) · [MRK 12:22](https://ref.ly/Matt12:22) · [LUK 1:55](https://ref.ly/Mark1:55) · [JHN 7:42](https://ref.ly/Luke7:42) · [JHN 8:33](https://ref.ly/Luke8:33) · [JHN 8:37](https://ref.ly/Luke8:37) · [ACT 3:25](https://ref.ly/John3:25) · [ACT 7:5](https://ref.ly/John7:5) · [ACT 7:6](https://ref.ly/John7:6) · [ACT 13:23](https://ref.ly/John13:23) · [ROM 1:3](https://ref.ly/Acts1:3) · [ROM 4:13](https://ref.ly/Acts4:13) · [ROM 4:16](https://ref.ly/Acts4:16) · [ROM 4:18](https://ref.ly/Acts4:18) · [ROM 9:7](https://ref.ly/Acts9:7) · [ROM 9:7](https://ref.ly/Acts9:7) · [ROM 9:8](https://ref.ly/Acts9:8) · [ROM 9:29](https://ref.ly/Acts9:29) · [ROM 11:1](https://ref.ly/Acts11:1) · [2CO 11:22](https://ref.ly/1Cor11:22) · [GAL 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:16) · [GAL 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:16) · [GAL 3:16](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:16) · [GAL 3:19](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:19) · [GAL 3:29](https://ref.ly/2Cor3:29) · [2TI 2:8](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:8) · [HEB 2:16](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:16) · [HEB 11:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:11) · [HEB 11:18](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:18) · [REV 12:17](https://ref.ly/Jude12:17)

58\.13 · Nature, Class, Example · Nature, Character

nature, something of the nature of a derivative and imparted nature If in some languages it is not possible to speak literally of ‘God’s nature,’ it may still be possible to render the second clause in [1JN 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:9) as ‘because something of what God is like is in him’ or ‘because he has in himself something of what God is like.’

[1JN 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:9)

23\.59 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

**Collocation:** ἀνίστημι σπέρμα · ἐξανίστημι σπέρμα

to beget, to procreate, to become the father of (idioms, literally: to raise up seed) the male role in begetting children In contexts such as [MAT 22:24](https://ref.ly/Matt22:24), [MRK 12:19](https://ref.ly/Matt12:19), and [LUK 20:28](https://ref.ly/Mark20:28) it may be important to add a note concerning levirate responsibilities, that is to say, the requirement for a younger brother to beget children by a deceased older brother’s wife and the reckoning of such an offspring as being the descendant of the older deceased brother.

[MAT 22:24](https://ref.ly/Matt22:24) · [LUK 20:28](https://ref.ly/Mark20:28)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:24; Matthew 13:27; Matthew 13:32; Matthew 13:37; Matthew 13:38; Mark 4:31; 1 Corinthians 15:38; Matthew 22:25; Mark 12:19; Mark 12:20; Mark 12:21; Mark 12:22; Luke 1:55; John 7:42; John 8:33; John 8:37; Acts 3:25; Acts 7:5; Acts 7:6; Acts 13:23; Romans 1:3; Romans 4:13; Romans 4:16; Romans 4:18; Romans 9:7; Romans 9:8; Romans 9:29; Romans 11:1; 2 Corinthians 11:22; Galatians 3:16; Galatians 3:19; Galatians 3:29; 2 Timothy 2:8; Hebrews 2:16; Hebrews 11:11; Hebrews 11:18; Revelation 12:17; 1 John 3:9; Matthew 22:24; Luke 20:28


## σπερμολόγος (id: 004593000000000)

σπερμολόγος
===========

σπερμολόγος (G4691)

adjc. \| \-ου \| σπείρω \+ λέγω

27\.19 · Learn · Learn

ignorant show\-off, charlatan (a figurative extension of meaning of a term based on the practice of birds in picking up seeds) one who acquires bits and pieces of relatively extraneous information and proceeds to pass them on with pretense and show The term σπερμολόγος is semantically complex in that it combines two quite distinct phases of activity: (1\) the acquiring of information and (2\) the passing on of such information. Because of the complex semantic structure of σπερμολόγος, it may be best in some languages to render it as ‘one who learns lots of trivial things and wants to tell everyone about his knowledge,’ but in most languages there is a perfectly appropriate idiom for ‘a pseudo\-intellectual who insists on spouting off.’ For a different focus on the meaning of σπερμολόγος in [ACT 17:18](https://ref.ly/John17:18), see [33\.381](#33.381).

[ACT 17:18](https://ref.ly/John17:18)

33\.381 · Communication · Foolish Talk

foolish babbler (a figurative expression, literally: one who picks up seed; originally a reference to birds picking up seed, but figuratively applied to a person who is an information scavenger) one who is not able to say anything worthwhile in view of his miscellaneous collection of tidbits of information For another interpretation of σπερμολόγος in [ACT 17:18](https://ref.ly/John17:18), see [27\.19](#27.19).

[ACT 17:18](https://ref.ly/John17:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 17:18


## σπεύδω (id: 004594000000000)

σπεύδω
======

σπεύδω (G4692)

verb \| σπουδάζω · σπουδαῖος · σπουδαίως · σπουδή

68\.79 · Aspect · Rapidity, Suddenness

to hasten to, to hurry to, to do quickly to do something hurriedly, with the implication of associated energy1 For another interpretation of σπεύδω in [ACT 20:16](https://ref.ly/John20:16), see [25\.74](#25.74).

[LUK 2:16](https://ref.ly/Mark2:16) · [LUK 19:5](https://ref.ly/Mark19:5) · [LUK 19:6](https://ref.ly/Mark19:6) · [ACT 20:16](https://ref.ly/John20:16) · [ACT 22:18](https://ref.ly/John22:18)

68\.80 · Aspect · Rapidity, Suddenness

to cause to happen soon, to hurry up to cause something to happen soon It is also possible to render this meaning of σπεύδω in [2PE 3:12](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:12) as ‘doing your best to cause ...’

[2PE 3:12](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:12)

25\.74 · Attitudes and Emotions · Be Eager, Be Earnest, In a Devoted Manner

to be eager, eagerness, devotion to be eager to do something, with the implication of readiness to expend energy and effort For another interpretation of σπεύδω in [ACT 20:16](https://ref.ly/John20:16), see [68\.79](#68.79).

[ACT 20:16](https://ref.ly/John20:16)

1 The meanings in this series ([68\.79](#68.79)) may very well be classified under Domain 67 Time, implying either that the period of time before beginning the event is a brief one or that the event itself takes place in a brief period of time. There is, however, a factor of energy involved in these terms, and therefore it seems legitimate to consider this additional factor as justifying the classification of these meanings as aspectual.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 2:16; Luke 19:5; Luke 19:6; Acts 20:16; Acts 22:18; 2 Peter 3:12


## σπήλαιον (id: 004595000000000)

σπήλαιον
========

σπήλαιον (G4693)

noun, n. \| \-ου

1\.57 · Geographical Objects and Features · Depressions and Holes

cave, den, hideout a cave or den generally large enough for at least temporary occupation by persons (since such places were often used for habitation or refuge by those who were refugees or thieves, σπήλαιον has in certain contexts the connotation of a ‘hideout’) In [REV 6:15](https://ref.ly/Jude6:15) the reference of σπήλαιον is literal, since people actually hid themselves in such caves. In [MAT 21:13](https://ref.ly/Matt21:13), however, the reference is to the Temple, which has been made a kind of ‘cave’ or ‘den,’ and since the connotation of the term suggests a ‘hideout,’ this is obviously a reflection upon the activities and motivations of those who had commercialized the Temple in Jerusalem.

[MAT 21:13](https://ref.ly/Matt21:13) · [MRK 11:17](https://ref.ly/Matt11:17) · [LUK 19:46](https://ref.ly/Mark19:46) · [JHN 11:38](https://ref.ly/Luke11:38) · [HEB 11:38](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:38) · [REV 6:15](https://ref.ly/Jude6:15)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 21:13; Mark 11:17; Luke 19:46; John 11:38; Hebrews 11:38; Revelation 6:15


## σπιλάς (id: 004596000000000)

noun, f. \| \-άδος \| σπιλόω

21\.5 · Danger, Risk, Safe, Save · Danger

unseen danger, hidden danger (a figurative extension of meaning of σπιλάς ‘a rock or reef washed by the sea,’ not occurring in the NT) an unrecognized source of danger or peril σπιλάς in [JUD 1:12](https://ref.ly/3John1:12) may also be understood as meaning ‘spot’ or ‘stain’ (see [79\.57](#79.57)).

[JUD 1:12](https://ref.ly/3John1:12)

79\.57 · Features of Objects · Spotted, Spotless

spot, stain that which constitutes an unwanted spot or stain upon something It is also possible that in [JUD 1:12](https://ref.ly/3John1:12) σπιλάς means an ‘unseen danger,’ in that it may refer to a rock which is mostly or completely covered by the sea (see [21\.5](#21.5)).

[JUD 1:12](https://ref.ly/3John1:12)

## σπλάγχνον (id: 004600000000000)

σπλάγχνον
=========

σπλάγχνον (G4698)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| σπλαγχνίζομαι

8\.58 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

intestines the inner parts of the body, especially the intestines

[ACT 1:18](https://ref.ly/John1:18)

26\.11 · Psychological Faculties

heart, feelings, desires (figurative extension of meaning of σπλάγχνον\[a] ‘intestines,’ [8\.58](#8.58)) the psychological faculty of desire, intent, and feeling1 Though some persons have attempted to distinguish between σπλάγχνον\[b], κοιλία\[c], and νεφρός, it is extremely doubtful whether this is really possible or practical. The semantic focus in the use of these terms is clearly the deeper and more intimate feelings and emotions. In some languages one can use a term which literally means ‘belly’ or ‘bowels,’ but more often than not, these emotions are associated with some particular organ of the body such as heart, spleen, liver, etc. Rather, however, than attempting to employ a figurative expression which may or may not be fully equivalent, it is often preferable to refer to the emotional content by using terms such as ‘feelings,’ ‘intents,’ ‘desires,’ or ‘compassion,’ depending upon the context.

[2CO 7:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:15) · [COL 3:12](https://ref.ly/Phil3:12) · [PHM 1:7](https://ref.ly/Titus1:7) · [PHM 1:20](https://ref.ly/Titus1:20)

25\.49 · Attitudes and Emotions · Love, Affection, Compassion

great affection for, love, compassion experiencing great affection and compassion for someone In [PHP 1:8](https://ref.ly/Eph1:8) the phrase ἐν σπλάγχνοις Χριστοῦ Ἰησοῦ is ambiguous. It may mean ‘because of the compassion which Christ Jesus himself has for you’ or ‘... for me.’ On the other hand, it may also be interpreted as characterizing the kind of love which Paul has for the believers, for example, ‘how I long for all of you, even with the kind of love Christ Jesus himself has for you.’

[LUK 1:78](https://ref.ly/Mark1:78) · [2CO 7:15](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:15) · [PHP 1:8](https://ref.ly/Eph1:8) · [PHP 2:1](https://ref.ly/Eph2:1) · [1JN 3:17](https://ref.ly/2Pet3:17)

25\.50 · Attitudes and Emotions · Love, Affection, Compassion

object of affection one for whom there is deep affection or compassion

[PHM 1:12](https://ref.ly/Titus1:12)

25\.54 · Attitudes and Emotions · Love, Affection, Compassion

**Collocation:** στενοχωρέομαι ἐν τοῖς σπλάγχνοις

to not respond with affection to someone, to close one’s heart to (an idiom, literally: to be restricted in the bowels) to restrict one’s affection for someone In [2CO 6:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:12) it is also possible to understand στενοχωρέομαι as meaning ‘to live with severe restrictions’ (see [37\.18](#37.18)), and σπλάγχνα may be interpreted as a psychological faculty of intent and feeling (see [26\.11](#26.11)).

[2CO 6:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:12)

1 It would be possible to treat σπλάγχνα\[b], κοιλία\[c], and νεφρός in this figurative sense in Domain 25 Attitudes and Emotions, but these meanings have been assigned to this domain of Psychological Faculties since the meanings involve aspects of personality which function as agents or presumed locations of psychological dispositions.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 1:18; 2 Corinthians 7:15; Colossians 3:12; Philemon 1:7; Philemon 1:20; Luke 1:78; Philippians 1:8; Philippians 2:1; 1 John 3:17; Philemon 1:12; 2 Corinthians 6:12


## σπόγγος (id: 004601000000000)

σπόγγος
=======

σπόγγος (G4699)

noun, m. \| \-ου

6\.133 · Artifacts · Containers

sponge a porous material used to absorb liquid In the only type of NT context in which σπόγγος occurs ([MAT 27:48](https://ref.ly/Matt27:48); [MRK 15:36](https://ref.ly/Matt15:36); [JHN 19:29](https://ref.ly/Luke19:29)), it serves as a container for cheap wine offered to Jesus on the cross.

## σποδός (id: 004602000000000)

σποδός
======

σποδός (G4700)

noun, f. \| \-οῦ

14\.73 · Physical Events and States · Burning

ashes the residue from a burned substance1 It may be important in rendering σποδὸς δαμάλεως to indicate that the ashes are the result of the animal having been burned as a sacrifice, for example, ‘the ashes of a heifer burned as a sacrifice.’ Otherwise, the relationship between ‘ashes’ and ‘heifer’ may be difficult, if not impossible, for readers to understand.

[MAT 11:21](https://ref.ly/Matt11:21) · [LUK 10:13](https://ref.ly/Mark10:13) · [HEB 9:13](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:13)

1 It would be possible to classify σποδός as a natural substance (see Domain 2\), since it is the result of a natural process and occurs in circumstances not involving artifacts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 11:21; Luke 10:13; Hebrews 9:13


## σπορά (id: 004603000000000)

σπορά
=====

σπορά (G4701)

noun, f. \| \-ᾶς \| σπείρω

10\.23 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations Involving Successive Generations

parentage (a figurative extension of meaning of σπορά ‘sowing of seed,’ not occurring in the NT) the instrumental means of birth

[1PE 1:23](https://ref.ly/Jas1:23)1

1 1PE 1:23 It is also possible to understand σπορά in [1PE 1:23](https://ref.ly/Jas1:23) as referring to the process of procreation as being analogical to the sowing of seed, but the attributives φθαρτῆς and ἀφθάρτου would seem to shift the meaning of σπορά to parentage. It is possible that this use of σπορά in [1PE 1:23](https://ref.ly/Jas1:23) represents a case of figurative usage rather than conventionalized figurative meaning.

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Peter 1:23


## σπόριμος (id: 004604000000000)

σπόριμος
========

σπόριμος (G4702) — σπόριμα

adjc. \| \-ον \| σπείρω

43\.7 · Agriculture

standing grain, grain fields (derivative of σπείρω ‘to sow,’ [43\.6](#43.6)) grain growing in a field In a number of languages there are distinct terms for various stages of growth of grain, and in view of the context of the account in [MRK 2:23](https://ref.ly/Matt2:23) and parallel passages, it is important to indicate that the grain was essentially ripe.

[MAT 12:1](https://ref.ly/Matt12:1) · [MRK 2:23](https://ref.ly/Matt2:23) · [LUK 6:1](https://ref.ly/Mark6:1)

## σπόρος (id: 004605000000000)

σπόρος
======

σπόρος (G4703)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| σπείρω

3\.35 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

seed the kernel part of fruit, usually grain A number of languages make distinctions between two quite different types of seed: (1\) those produced by grasses (that is to say, grains) and (2\) those produced by other types of plants, for example, beans, squash, apples, etc. In all passages employing the Greek terms in this subdomain (κόκκος, σπέρμα, σπόρος), it is best to use some expression referring to ‘grain.’  
See also [10\.23](#10.23) for σπορά ‘seed’ used figuratively of descendants.

[MRK 4:26](https://ref.ly/Matt4:26) · [MRK 4:27](https://ref.ly/Matt4:27) · [LUK 8:5](https://ref.ly/Mark8:5) · [LUK 8:11](https://ref.ly/Mark8:11) · [2CO 9:10](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:10) · [2CO 9:10](https://ref.ly/1Cor9:10)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 4:26; Mark 4:27; Luke 8:5; Luke 8:11; 2 Corinthians 9:10

25\.75 · Attitudes and Emotions · Be Eager, Be Earnest, In a Devoted Manner

to hasten to, to hurry to, to do quickly to do something hurriedly, with the implication of associated energy1

[ROM 12:8](https://ref.ly/Acts12:8) · [JUD 1:3](https://ref.ly/3John1:3)

[ROM 12:11](https://ref.ly/Acts12:11) · [2CO 7:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:11) · [2CO 7:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:12) · [2CO 8:7](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:7) · [2CO 8:8](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:8) · [2CO 8:16](https://ref.ly/1Cor8:16) · [HEB 6:11](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:11)

68\.64 · Aspect · Do Intensely or Extensively

**Collocation:** σπουδὴν πᾶσαν παρεισφέρω

to do one’s best, to make every effort to, to try as hard as possible (an idiom, literally: to bring every effort to) to do one’s very best in attempting to do something In some languages it may be almost impossible to speak of ‘adding goodness to faith’ ([2PE 1:5](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:5)). However, an appropriate equivalent of this expression may be ‘do your best to be good as well as to believe.’

[2PE 1:5](https://ref.ly/1Pet1:5)

1 The meanings in this series ([68\.79](#68.79)) may very well be classified under Domain 67 Time, implying either that the period of time before beginning the event is a brief one or that the event itself takes place in a brief period of time. There is, however, a factor of energy involved in these terms, and therefore it seems legitimate to consider this additional factor as justifying the classification of these meanings as aspectual.

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 6:25; Luke 1:39; Romans 12:8; Jude 1:3; Romans 12:11; 2 Corinthians 7:11; 2 Corinthians 7:12; 2 Corinthians 8:7; 2 Corinthians 8:8; 2 Corinthians 8:16; Hebrews 6:11; 2 Peter 1:5

## στάδιον (id: 004611000000000)

στάδιον
=======

στάδιον (G4712) — στάδιοι

noun, n. \| \-ου

7\.55 · Constructions · Open Constructions

arena, stadium an open, oval area (frequently including a racetrack) around which was built an enclosed series of tiers of seats for those who came to watch the spectacles In [1CO 9:24](https://ref.ly/Rom9:24) the important feature is not the stadium as a construction, but as a place where races were conducted. Accordingly, ‘all the runners in the stadium’ may very well be rendered as ‘all the runners who are racing.’ The focus here is upon the competition rather than upon the type of place in which the competition took place.

[1CO 9:24](https://ref.ly/Rom9:24)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Corinthians 9:24

## σταυρός (id: 004617000000000)

σταυρός
=======

σταυρός (G4716)

noun, m. \| \-οῦ \| σταυρόω

6\.27 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Punishment and Execution

cross a pole stuck into the ground in an upright position with a crosspiece attached to its upper part; used as a means of execution In [MAT 27:32](https://ref.ly/Matt27:32) (τοῦτον ἠγγάρευσαν ἵνα ἄρῃ τὸν σταυρὸν αὐτοῦ ‘they forced him to carry Jesus’ cross’) the reference is probably to the crosspiece of the cross, which normally would have been carried by a man condemned to die.  
Because of the symbolism associated with the cross, translations of the NT in all languages preserve some expression which will identify the cross, not only as a means of capital punishment, but as having a particular form, namely, an upright pole with a crossbeam. In some receptor languages the term for a cross means simply ‘crossbeam.’ In other instances it is composed of a phrase meaning ‘crossed poles.’ It is important, however, to avoid an expression which will suggest crossed sticks in the form of X rather than a cross consisting of an upright with a horizontal beam. If at all possible one should employ a term or phrase which may be used in an extended sense, since in so many contexts the term ‘cross’ refers not only to the instrument of Christ’s death, but to the event of execution. It also becomes a symbol of the message of forgiveness and of reconciliation. Because of these extended meanings, it is important to choose a form which can, if at all possible, support these additional meanings.

[MAT 10:38](https://ref.ly/Matt10:38) · [MAT 16:24](https://ref.ly/Matt16:24) · [MAT 27:32](https://ref.ly/Matt27:32) · [MAT 27:40](https://ref.ly/Matt27:40) · [MAT 27:42](https://ref.ly/Matt27:42) · [MRK 8:34](https://ref.ly/Matt8:34) · [MRK 15:21](https://ref.ly/Matt15:21) · [MRK 15:30](https://ref.ly/Matt15:30) · [MRK 15:32](https://ref.ly/Matt15:32) · [LUK 9:23](https://ref.ly/Mark9:23) · [LUK 14:27](https://ref.ly/Mark14:27) · [LUK 23:26](https://ref.ly/Mark23:26) · [JHN 19:17](https://ref.ly/Luke19:17) · [JHN 19:19](https://ref.ly/Luke19:19) · [JHN 19:25](https://ref.ly/Luke19:25) · [JHN 19:31](https://ref.ly/Luke19:31) · [1CO 1:17](https://ref.ly/Rom1:17) · [1CO 1:18](https://ref.ly/Rom1:18) · [GAL 5:11](https://ref.ly/2Cor5:11) · [GAL 6:12](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:12) · [GAL 6:14](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:14) · [EPH 2:16](https://ref.ly/Gal2:16) · [PHP 2:8](https://ref.ly/Eph2:8) · [PHP 3:18](https://ref.ly/Eph3:18) · [COL 1:20](https://ref.ly/Phil1:20) · [COL 2:14](https://ref.ly/Phil2:14) · [HEB 12:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm12:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 10:38; Matthew 16:24; Matthew 27:32; Matthew 27:40; Matthew 27:42; Mark 8:34; Mark 15:21; Mark 15:30; Mark 15:32; Luke 9:23; Luke 14:27; Luke 23:26; John 19:17; John 19:19; John 19:25; John 19:31; 1 Corinthians 1:17; 1 Corinthians 1:18; Galatians 5:11; Galatians 6:12; Galatians 6:14; Ephesians 2:16; Philippians 2:8; Philippians 3:18; Colossians 1:20; Colossians 2:14; Hebrews 12:2


## σταυρόω (id: 004618000000000)

σταυρόω
=======

σταυρόω (G4717)

verb \| ἀνασταυρόω · σταυρός · συσταυρόομαι

20\.76 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Kill

to crucify to execute someone by nailing that person to a cross It is rare that one can find in receptor languages a technical term or phrase meaning specifically ‘to crucify.’ In general, a phrase must be employed, since this type of execution is no longer practiced. One can, for example, use such expressions as ‘to nail to a cross bar’ or ‘to nail up on wood’ or even ‘to nail up high.’

## σταφυλή (id: 004619000000000)

σταφυλή
=======

σταφυλή (G4718)

noun, f. \| \-ῆς

3\.38 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

grape, bunch of grapes the small round fruit, sweet and juicy, of a creeping plant that develops a woody stem when it matures; Vitis vinifera; symbol of blessing, prosperity, and happiness Some scholars have contended that βότρυς means primarily a bunch of grapes, while σταφυλή designates individual grapes. In [REV 14:18](https://ref.ly/Jude14:18) this difference might seem plausible, but there is scarcely any evidence for such a distinction, since both words may signify grapes as well as bunches of grapes.  
In some languages it is necessary to borrow a term for ‘grapes’ from a dominant language and then employ some kind of classifier, for example, ‘fruit called grapes.’ In other languages grapes may be known as ‘wine fruit,’ since wine may be more widely known than a term for grapes.

[MAT 7:16](https://ref.ly/Matt7:16) · [LUK 6:44](https://ref.ly/Mark6:44) · [REV 14:18](https://ref.ly/Jude14:18)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 7:16; Luke 6:44; Revelation 14:18


## στάχυς (id: 004620000000000)

στάχυς
======

στάχυς (G4719)

noun, m. \| \-υος

3\.40 · Plants · Fruit Parts of Plants

ear of wheat, head of wheat the dense spiky cluster in which the seeds of grain such as wheat and barley grow (restricted in NT contexts to references to wheat) In some languages it is impossible to speak of ‘a head of wheat’ or ‘an ear of wheat,’ since terms referring to ‘head’ and ‘ear’ have no such figurative extensions of meaning. In certain instances the equivalent may be ‘the point of the wheat’ or ‘the brush of the wheat,’ referring to the spike\-like objects which extend from each grain.

[MAT 12:1](https://ref.ly/Matt12:1) · [MRK 2:23](https://ref.ly/Matt2:23) · [MRK 4:28](https://ref.ly/Matt4:28) · [MRK 4:28](https://ref.ly/Matt4:28) · [LUK 6:1](https://ref.ly/Mark6:1)

## στέγη (id: 004622000000000)

στέγη
=====

στέγη (G4721)

noun, f. \| \-ης \| στέγω

7\.50 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

housetop the area on the top of a flat\-roof house In general, the types of roofs referred to in the NT are flat\-top, made of pounded dirt, sometimes mixed with lime or stone, and supported by heavy beams. In view of the various types of activities described as taking place on the housetop, it may be important in some languages to indicate either in the text or in a marginal note the fact that such housetops were flat and that there was usually easy access to such roofs.

## στεναγμός (id: 004627000000000)

στεναγμός
=========

στεναγμός (G4726)

noun, m. \| \-οῦ \| στενάζω

25\.143 · Attitudes and Emotions · Laugh, Cry, Groan

groan, sigh groaning or sighing as the result of deep concern or stress To groan or to sigh may be the result of quite different circumstances, and in a number of languages a clear distinction must be made in any term for groaning or sighing, depending upon the reason or basis for such an expression of emotion. In [MRK 7:34](https://ref.ly/Matt7:34) the sigh or groan would seem to be an expression of sympathy for the deaf\-mute, but in [ACT 7:34](https://ref.ly/John7:34) the groans would be caused by severe misery and oppression.

[2TI 2:19](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:19) · [HEB 5:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:12) · [HEB 5:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:14)

to be firm, to be strong pertaining to being firm and steadfast in one’s attitudes or beliefs

[1PE 5:9](https://ref.ly/Jas5:9)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Timothy 2:19; Hebrews 5:12; Hebrews 5:14; 1 Peter 5:9


## στερεόω (id: 004633000000000)

στερεόω
=======

στερεόω (G4732) — στερεόομαι

verb \| στερεός · στερέωμα

79\.68 · Features of Objects · Strong, Weak

to make strong, to strengthen to make physically strong In a number of languages one cannot speak of a name doing anything or even the ‘power of a name’ accomplishing some goal. Since in Greek the use of ὄνομα ‘name’ is essentially a metonym for the person, it is often necessary to translate an expression such as is in [ACT 3:16](https://ref.ly/John3:16) as ‘Christ made him strong’ or ‘Jesus made him strong.’ Such an expression, however, should not imply that this was a miracle performed directly by Jesus, either before or immediately after the resurrection.

[ACT 3:16](https://ref.ly/John3:16)

74\.19 · Able, Capable

to strengthen, to make more firm to cause someone to become stronger in the sense of more firm and unchanging in attitude or belief

[ACT 16:5](https://ref.ly/John16:5)

79\.67 · (στερεόομαι) · Features of Objects · Strong, Weak

to be strong, to become strong to be physically strong and vigorous

[ACT 3:7](https://ref.ly/John3:7)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 3:16; Acts 16:5; Acts 3:7

## στέφανος (id: 004636000000000)

στέφανος
========

στέφανος (G4735)

noun, m. \| \-ου

6\.192 · Artifacts · Adornments

wreath, crown a wreath consisting either of foliage or of precious metals formed to resemble foliage and worn as a symbol of honor, victory, or as a badge of high office It may be important in some contexts to indicate clearly the significance of the wreath worn on the head, for example, ‘a wreath to show victory.’ To describe ‘a wreath’ merely as ‘a circle of leaves’ would hardly be sufficient to indicate its cultural significance. In order to do justice to the cultural relevance of such a wreath, it may be important to add some type of marginal note (compare διάδημα ‘diadem crown,’ [6\.196](#6.196)).

[MAT 27:29](https://ref.ly/Matt27:29) · [MRK 15:17](https://ref.ly/Matt15:17) · [JHN 19:2](https://ref.ly/Luke19:2) · [JHN 19:5](https://ref.ly/Luke19:5) · [1CO 9:25](https://ref.ly/Rom9:25) · [1TH 2:19](https://ref.ly/Col2:19) · [JAS 1:12](https://ref.ly/Heb1:12) · [1PE 5:4](https://ref.ly/Jas5:4) · [REV 4:4](https://ref.ly/Jude4:4) · [REV 4:10](https://ref.ly/Jude4:10) · [REV 6:2](https://ref.ly/Jude6:2) · [REV 9:7](https://ref.ly/Jude9:7) · [REV 12:1](https://ref.ly/Jude12:1) · [REV 14:14](https://ref.ly/Jude14:14)

57\.121 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Give

prize, reward a prize or reward given as the result of outstanding performance In [REV 2:10](https://ref.ly/Jude2:10) the relationship between τὸν στέφανον and τῆς ζωῆς is one of apposition, for the prize consists of life. Essentially the same relationship exists in the construction ἀπόκειταί μοι ὁ τῆς δικαιοσύνης στέφανος ‘the prize of righteousness awaits me’ [2TI 4:8](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:8). In this case the prize is ‘being declared righteous’ or ‘being put right with God.’

[1TH 2:19](https://ref.ly/Col2:19) · [2TI 4:8](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:8) · [JAS 1:12](https://ref.ly/Heb1:12) · [REV 2:10](https://ref.ly/Jude2:10) · [REV 3:11](https://ref.ly/Jude3:11)

42\.19 · Perform, Do · Do, Perform

crown, symbol of success, sign of accomplishment (a figurative extension of meaning of στέφανος\[a] ‘wreath, crown,’ [6\.192](#6.192)) a symbol of successful activity

[PHP 4:1](https://ref.ly/Eph4:1) · [1TH 2:19](https://ref.ly/Col2:19)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 27:29; Mark 15:17; John 19:2; John 19:5; 1 Corinthians 9:25; 1 Thessalonians 2:19; James 1:12; 1 Peter 5:4; Revelation 4:4; Revelation 4:10; Revelation 6:2; Revelation 9:7; Revelation 12:1; Revelation 14:14; 2 Timothy 4:8; Revelation 2:10; Revelation 3:11; Philippians 4:1

## στίγμα (id: 004644000000000)

στίγμα
======

στίγμα (G4742)

noun, n. \| \-τος \| στιγμή

8\.55 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

scar, brand a permanent mark or scar on the body, especially the type of brand used to mark ownership of slaves1 In [GAL 6:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:17) Paul is most likely alluding to scars resulting from wounds received in the service of Jesus, but στίγμα may also imply ownership and hence suggest that such scars served as brands (see [8\.56](#8.56)). For other interpretations of στίγμα in [GAL 6:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:17), see [33\.481](#33.481) and [90\.84](#90.84).

[GAL 6:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:17)

33\.481 · Communication · Non\-Verbal Communication

mark, scar something on the surface of an object, for example, line, spot, or scar, without special design but carrying significance2 A strictly literal translation of [GAL 6:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:17) might suggest that Paul had the same marks on his hands, feet, and side as Jesus had, but this is evidently not the meaning of the state ment in [GAL 6:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:17). It is possible, of course, that since Paul was whipped much the same way that Jesus was whipped, he (Paul) would bear such scars on his back, but a more satisfactory rendering of [GAL 6:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:17) would probably be ‘for I have on my body scars indicating that I belong to Jesus.’ For other interpretations of στίγμα in [GAL 6:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:17), see [8\.55](#8.55) and [90\.84](#90.84).

[GAL 6:17](https://ref.ly/2Cor6:17)

1 Properly speaking, στίγμα\[a] ([8\.55](#8.55)) and τύπος\[a] ([8\.56](#8.56)) are not body parts, but may refer to features of the body which may result from some external force or object and could accordingly be classified in Domain 19 Physical Impact. They are, however, included at this point because they may refer to types of scars, which become a permanent feature of the body. 2 στίγμα\[b] differs from στίγμα\[a] ([8\.55](#8.55)) in that the significance of the scar is not the physical object as such but the meaning which the scar carries.

* **Associated Passages:** Galatians 6:17

## στοά (id: 004647000000000)

στοά
====

στοά (G4745)

noun, f. \| \-ᾶς \| ἵστημι

7\.40 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

porch, portico a covered colonnade, open normally on one side, where people could stand, sit, or walk, protected from the weather and the heat of the sun Also see comments at [7\.58](#7.58).

## στοιχεῖον (id: 004650000000000)

στοιχεῖον
=========

στοιχεῖον (G4747) — στοιχεῖα

noun, n. \| \-ου \| στοιχέω

2\.1 · Natural Substances · Elements

elements, natural substances the materials of which the world and the universe are composed In many languages the closest equivalent of στοιχεῖα is ‘the things of which the world is made’ or ‘what the world is made of’ or ‘the substances of which the universe consists.’

[2PE 3:10](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:10) · [2PE 3:12](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:12)

12\.43 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Powers

the supernatural powers over this world the supernatural powers or forces regarded as having control over the events of this world In a number of languages there is no way of speaking of ‘supernatural powers’ or ‘supernatural forces.’ Reference can only be made to such powers in terms of kinds of spirit beings; therefore, one may render στοιχεῖα\[b] in [COL 2:20](https://ref.ly/Phil2:20) as ‘those spirits that have power’ or ‘those spirits which control.’

[COL 2:20](https://ref.ly/Phil2:20)

58\.19 · Nature, Class, Example · Basic Principles or Features Defining the Nature of Something

basic principles, elementary concepts basic principles which underlie the nature of something In some languages it may be extremely difficult to find the lexical equivalents of ‘the basic principles about the elementary aspects.’ In Greek this represents highly generic vocabulary, and in many languages the closest equivalent is ‘how to understand the simple truths.’ Therefore, this expression in [HEB 5:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:12) may be rendered as ‘again you have need for someone to teach you how to understand the simple truths about God’s message.’

[GAL 4:3](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:3) · [GAL 4:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:9) · [COL 2:8](https://ref.ly/Phil2:8) · [COL 2:20](https://ref.ly/Phil2:20) · [HEB 5:12](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:12)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Peter 3:10; 2 Peter 3:12; Colossians 2:20; Galatians 4:3; Galatians 4:9; Colossians 2:8; Hebrews 5:12

## στόμα (id: 004653000000000)

στόμα
=====

στόμα (G4750)

noun, n. \| \-τος \| ἀποστοματίζω · δίστομος · ἐπιστομίζω · στόμαχος

8\.19 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Parts of the Body

mouth In some languages a distinction is made between terms used for the mouth when it is open and when it is closed. In [ACT 23:2](https://ref.ly/John23:2) presumably the mouth was closed.  
The term στόμα also occurs in a number of phrases associated with speech, but while in some languages one can say ‘to speak with the mouth,’ it may be more appropriate to say ‘to speak with the lips’ or ‘to speak with the tongue.’ In a number of contexts, however, it may be better simply to say ‘to speak,’ since the addition of ‘with the lips’ or ‘with the tongue’ or ‘with the mouth’ may appear to be unnecessarily redundant.

[MAT 15:11](https://ref.ly/Matt15:11) · [MAT 15:11](https://ref.ly/Matt15:11) · [MAT 15:17](https://ref.ly/Matt15:17) · [MAT 15:18](https://ref.ly/Matt15:18) · [MAT 17:27](https://ref.ly/Matt17:27) · [LUK 6:45](https://ref.ly/Mark6:45) · [JHN 19:29](https://ref.ly/Luke19:29) · [ACT 11:8](https://ref.ly/John11:8) · [ACT 23:2](https://ref.ly/John23:2) · [2TH 2:8](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:8) · [2TI 4:17](https://ref.ly/1Tim4:17) · [HEB 11:33](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:33) · [JAS 3:3](https://ref.ly/Heb3:3) · [JAS 3:10](https://ref.ly/Heb3:10) · [REV 1:16](https://ref.ly/Jude1:16) · [REV 2:16](https://ref.ly/Jude2:16) · [REV 3:16](https://ref.ly/Jude3:16) · [REV 9:17](https://ref.ly/Jude9:17) · [REV 9:18](https://ref.ly/Jude9:18) · [REV 9:19](https://ref.ly/Jude9:19) · [REV 10:9](https://ref.ly/Jude10:9) · [REV 10:10](https://ref.ly/Jude10:10) · [REV 11:5](https://ref.ly/Jude11:5) · [REV 12:15](https://ref.ly/Jude12:15) · [REV 12:16](https://ref.ly/Jude12:16) · [REV 12:16](https://ref.ly/Jude12:16) · [REV 13:2](https://ref.ly/Jude13:2) · [REV 13:2](https://ref.ly/Jude13:2) · [REV 16:13](https://ref.ly/Jude16:13) · [REV 16:13](https://ref.ly/Jude16:13) · [REV 16:13](https://ref.ly/Jude16:13) · [REV 19:15](https://ref.ly/Jude19:15) · [REV 19:21](https://ref.ly/Jude19:21)

33\.74 · Communication · Speak, Talk

speech, to speak (figurative extension of meaning of στόμα\[a] ‘mouth,’ [8\.19](#8.19)) to communicate orally

## στρατεία (id: 004655000000000)

στρατεία
========

στρατεία (G4752)

noun, f. \| \-ας \| στρατεύομαι

55\.4 · Military Activities · To Fight

war, warfare act of engaging in war or battle as a soldier στρατεύω\[a] and στρατεία in [1TI 1:18](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:18) and [2CO 10:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:4) are used figuratively, and it may be essential to mark this figurative usage as a type of simile. For example, in [1TI 1:18](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:18) στρατεύομαι may be rendered as ‘you may, so to speak, wage the good battle’ or ‘it is like you are fighting.’ Similarly, in [2CO 10:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:4) στρατεία may be rendered as ‘in what is like a battle for us.’

[2CO 10:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:4) · [1TI 1:18](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:18)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 10:4; 1 Timothy 1:18

## στρατεύω (id: 004657000000000)

στρατεύω

55\.4 · (στρατεύομαι\[a]) · Military Activities · To Fight

## στρατιά (id: 004659000000000)

στρατιά
=======

στρατιά (G4756)

noun, f. \| \-ᾶς \| στρατεύομαι

12\.30 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Beings

**Collocation:** στρατιὰ οὐράνιος

throng of angels, ranks of angels (an idiom, literally: heavenly army) a large group or throng of angels There may be distinct objections to speaking of στρατιὰ οὐράνιος as being a ‘heavenly army,’ though undoubtedly in earlier times the thought of angels being God’s military force would have been quite appropriate. Therefore, in place of some expression which may refer to an army or military unit, it may be possible to translate στρατιὰ οὐράνιος as simply ‘many, many angels’ or ‘row after row of angels.’

[LUK 2:13](https://ref.ly/Mark2:13)

12\.45 · Supernatural Beings and Powers · Supernatural Powers

**Collocation:** στρατιὰ τοῦ οὐρανοῦ

the stars of heaven (an idiom, literally: army of heaven) the stars of heaven as symbols of various supernatural powers Since ‘the stars of heaven’ serve primarily as symbols of certain heavenly supernatural powers, it may be appropriate in some languages to speak of ‘the spirits of the stars in the sky.’ See also [1\.5](#1.5).

[ACT 7:42](https://ref.ly/John7:42)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 2:13; Acts 7:42


## στρατιώτης (id: 004660000000000)

στρατιώτης
==========

στρατιώτης (G4757)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| στρατεύομαι

55\.17 · Military Activities · Soldiers, Officers

soldier a person of ordinary rank in an army In some languages the normal equivalent of στρατιώτης would be ‘one who carries a gun,’ but such an expression would be completely anachronistic. Some translators have attempted to substitute a phrase such as ‘one who carries a sword,’ but this has failed in most cases since it suggests merely individual violence instead of organized warfare. It may therefore be important to use a phrase such as ‘one who fights under command’ or ‘one who is charged by the rulers to fight.’

[MAT 8:9](https://ref.ly/Matt8:9) · [MAT 27:27](https://ref.ly/Matt27:27) · [MAT 28:12](https://ref.ly/Matt28:12) · [MRK 15:16](https://ref.ly/Matt15:16) · [LUK 7:8](https://ref.ly/Mark7:8) · [LUK 23:36](https://ref.ly/Mark23:36) · [JHN 19:2](https://ref.ly/Luke19:2) · [JHN 19:23](https://ref.ly/Luke19:23) · [JHN 19:23](https://ref.ly/Luke19:23) · [JHN 19:24](https://ref.ly/Luke19:24) · [JHN 19:32](https://ref.ly/Luke19:32) · [JHN 19:34](https://ref.ly/Luke19:34) · [ACT 10:7](https://ref.ly/John10:7) · [ACT 12:4](https://ref.ly/John12:4) · [ACT 12:6](https://ref.ly/John12:6) · [ACT 12:18](https://ref.ly/John12:18) · [ACT 21:32](https://ref.ly/John21:32) · [ACT 21:32](https://ref.ly/John21:32) · [ACT 21:35](https://ref.ly/John21:35) · [ACT 23:23](https://ref.ly/John23:23) · [ACT 23:31](https://ref.ly/John23:31) · [ACT 27:31](https://ref.ly/John27:31) · [ACT 27:32](https://ref.ly/John27:32) · [ACT 27:42](https://ref.ly/John27:42) · [ACT 28:16](https://ref.ly/John28:16) · [2TI 2:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 8:9; Matthew 27:27; Matthew 28:12; Mark 15:16; Luke 7:8; Luke 23:36; John 19:2; John 19:23; John 19:24; John 19:32; John 19:34; Acts 10:7; Acts 12:4; Acts 12:6; Acts 12:18; Acts 21:32; Acts 21:35; Acts 23:23; Acts 23:31; Acts 27:31; Acts 27:32; Acts 27:42; Acts 28:16; 2 Timothy 2:3


## στρατολογέω (id: 004661000000000)

55\.19 · Military Activities · Soldiers, Officers

to enlist soldiers to cause someone to be a soldier In some languages it may be necessary to specify somewhat more clearly the relationship involved in ‘to enlist soldiers.’ For example, the last part of [2TI 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:4) may be rendered as ‘because he must please the one who caused him to be a soldier’ or ‘... who got him to be a soldier’ or ‘... who induced him to be a soldier for him.’ For another interpretation of στρατολογέω in [2TI 2:4](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:4), see [55\.20](#55.20).

16\.13 · (στρέφομαι\[a]) · Non\-Linear Movement

[MAT 9:22](https://ref.ly/Matt9:22) · [LUK 7:9](https://ref.ly/Mark7:9) · [LUK 7:44](https://ref.ly/Mark7:44) · [LUK 9:55](https://ref.ly/Mark9:55) · [LUK 10:23](https://ref.ly/Mark10:23) · [LUK 14:25](https://ref.ly/Mark14:25) · [LUK 22:61](https://ref.ly/Mark22:61) · [LUK 23:28](https://ref.ly/Mark23:28) · [JHN 20:14](https://ref.ly/Luke20:14) · [JHN 20:16](https://ref.ly/Luke20:16)

31\.60 · (στρέφομαι\[b]) · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Change an Opinion Concerning Truth

to turn to, to come to believe, to come to accept to change one’s belief, with focus upon that to which one turns In analyzing the meaning of στρέφω\[g], ἐπιστρέφω\[b], and ἐπιστροφή\[a] in such passages as [MAT 18:3](https://ref.ly/Matt18:3), [JHN 12:40](https://ref.ly/Luke12:40), and [ACT 7:39](https://ref.ly/John7:39), it is difficult to determine the extent to which belief or behavior is primarily in focus. In the case of [1PE 2:25](https://ref.ly/Jas2:25), one could certainly argue that the emphasis is upon the interpersonal relationship. It is therefore essential in rendering these terms not to narrow the meaning too much, for in this way one would certainly do violence to certain crucial semantic features.  
For another interpretation of στρέφομαι in [MAT 18:3](https://ref.ly/Matt18:3), see [41\.50](#41.50).

## στρουθίον (id: 004669000000000)

στρουθίον
=========

στρουθίον (G4765)

noun, n. \| \-ου

4\.46 · Animals · Birds

sparrow small bird; speckled brown in color; genus Passer; roosts and nests in groups; eats grass seeds and grain; associated with the poor The Greek term στρουθίον no doubt refers to the so\-called ‘house sparrow,’ which almost always builds its nests near human habitation. In the Orient a similar type of sparrow exists, and a term designating such a sparrow can be used in all contexts in which the Greek term στρουθίον is employed.

[MAT 10:29](https://ref.ly/Matt10:29) · [MAT 10:31](https://ref.ly/Matt10:31) · [LUK 12:6](https://ref.ly/Mark12:6) · [LUK 12:7](https://ref.ly/Mark12:7)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 10:29; Matthew 10:31; Luke 12:6; Luke 12:7


## στρωννύω (id: 004670000000000)

στρωννύω
========

verb \| καταστρώννυμι · λιθόστρωτον · ὑποστρωννύω

16\.22 · (στρώννυμι\[a]) · Non\-Linear Movement

to spread, to spread out to spread something out

[MAT 21:8](https://ref.ly/Matt21:8) · [MAT 21:8](https://ref.ly/Matt21:8) · [MRK 11:8](https://ref.ly/Matt11:8)

46\.9 · (στρώννυμι\[b]) · Household Activities

to furnish, to arrange to fit out or arrange a room in a suitable manner (that is, to provide it with necessary furniture)1

[MRK 14:15](https://ref.ly/Matt14:15) · [LUK 22:12](https://ref.ly/Mark22:12)

46\.10 · (στρώννυμι\[c]) · Household Activities

to make one’s bed to prepare a bed, either for sleeping or making it up after it has been used1

[ACT 9:34](https://ref.ly/John9:34)

1 It is possible to argue that στρώννυμι (and the corresponding form στρωννύω) has only the base meaning to spread something out (as in [MAT 21:8](https://ref.ly/Matt21:8); see [16\.22](#16.22)), but this term seems to be used in an absolute sense in rather highly diverse contexts, and therefore one is justified in setting up more than one distinct meaning.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 21:8; Mark 11:8; Mark 14:15; Luke 22:12; Acts 9:34


## στυγητός (id: 004671000000000)

στυγητός
========

στυγητός (G4767)

adjc. \| \-ή, \-όν \| στυγνάζω

88\.204 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Hate, Hateful

hated pertaining to being hated or regarded as worthy of being hated

[TIT 3:3](https://ref.ly/2Tim3:3)

* **Associated Passages:** Titus 3:3


## στυγνάζω (id: 004672000000000)

στυγνάζω
========

στυγνάζω (G4768)

verb \| στυγέω (hate) · ἀποστυγέω · θεοστυγής · στυγητός

14\.56 · Physical Events and States · Darkness

to become dark and gloomy to become both dark and gloomy, with the implication of threatening In order to combine the components of στυγνάζω, which involve not only darkness but also gloom and threatening, it may be possible to translate as ‘dark and threatening’ or ‘so dark as to cause one to be afraid.’

[MAT 16:3](https://ref.ly/Matt16:3)

25\.286 · Attitudes and Emotions · Sorrow, Regret

to be downcast, to look gloomy to experience an emotional state of both grief and discouragement, as evidenced in the appearance of one’s face It is also possible to understand στυγνάζω in [MRK 10:22](https://ref.ly/Matt10:22) as meaning ‘to be shocked, to be appalled’ (see [25\.222](#25.222)).

[MRK 10:22](https://ref.ly/Matt10:22)

25\.222 · Attitudes and Emotions · Surprise, Astonish

to be shocked, to be appalled to experience an emotional state of great surprise because of something which appears incredible and alarming For a different interpretation of στυγνάζω in [MRK 10:22](https://ref.ly/Matt10:22), see [25\.286](#25.286).

[MRK 10:22](https://ref.ly/Matt10:22)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 16:3; Mark 10:22


## στῦλος (id: 004673000000000)

στῦλος
======

στῦλος (G4769)

noun, m. \| \-ου

7\.45 · Constructions · Parts and Areas of Buildings

pillar, column an upright shaft or structure used as a building support στῦλος is also used in speaking of the leaders of the Jerusalem church ([GAL 2:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:9); see [36\.7](#36.7)). In [GAL 2:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:9) the focus is upon the important role of such persons in supporting and maintaining the church. In a number of languages such a figurative meaning may be expressed as ‘very important persons in the church.’  
In a number of languages pillars may be described as ‘those poles which support the house’ or ‘those logs which hold up the roof.’ Usually, however, there are rather specific terms to designate these important parts in the construction of houses or halls.

[1TI 3:15](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:15) · [REV 3:12](https://ref.ly/Jude3:12) · [REV 10:1](https://ref.ly/Jude10:1)

36\.7 · Guide, Discipline, Follow · Guide, Lead

leader (a figurative extension of meaning of στῦλος\[a] ‘pillar, column,’ [7\.45](#7.45)) one who is a leader of a group, with the implication of strategic responsibility

[GAL 2:9](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:9)

* **Associated Passages:** 1 Timothy 3:15; Revelation 3:12; Revelation 10:1; Galatians 2:9


## σύ (id: 004674000000000)

σύ
==

pprs. \| σοῦ (σου)‏, σοί (σοι), σέ · pl. ὑμεῖς, ὑμῶν, ὑμῖν, ὑμᾶς

92\.6 · ((sg)) · Discourse Referentials · Receptor, Receptors

92\.7 · ((pl)) · Discourse Referentials · Receptor, Receptors

**Collocation:** ὑμᾶς · ὑμεῖς · ὑμῖν · ὑμῶν

you, your a reference to the receptors of a message, whether oral or written (with an added feature of emphasis in the form ὑμεῖς)

11\.57 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

fellow countryman a person who is a member of the same πατριά\[b] or φυλή\[b] ‘nation’ ([11\.56](#11.56)) The term ἄνδρες is often added to ἀδελφοί\[d], constituting a lexical unit having essentially the same meaning as ἀδελφοί\[d], but with the connotation of greater formality: ἄνδρες ἀδελφοίἐξὸν εἰπεῖν μετὰ παρρησίας πρὸς ὑμᾶς ‘fellow countrymen, I can speak to you quite plainly’ [ACT 2:29](https://ref.ly/John2:29).  
συμφυλέτης\[d] may often be translated by a phrase, for example, ‘a person of the same country’ or ‘a man who belongs to the same nation’ or ‘one who is part of the same tribe.’

[ROM 9:3](https://ref.ly/Acts9:3) · [ROM 16:7](https://ref.ly/Acts16:7) · [ROM 16:11](https://ref.ly/Acts16:11) · [ROM 16:21](https://ref.ly/Acts16:21)

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 6:4; Luke 1:58; Luke 2:44; Luke 14:12; Luke 21:16; John 18:26; Acts 10:24; Romans 9:3; Romans 16:7; Romans 16:11; Romans 16:21

## συγκάθημαι (id: 004679000000000)

συγκάθημαι
==========

συγκάθημαι (G4775)

verb \| καθίζω

17\.13 · Stances and Events Related to Stances · Sit

to sit down with, to be seated with, sitting with to sit down with someone or to be seated with someone1

[MRK 14:54](https://ref.ly/Matt14:54) · [ACT 26:30](https://ref.ly/John26:30)

1 There are certain technical problems involved in treating the series καθέζομαι, κάθημαι\[a], καθίζω\[a] ([17\.12](#17.12)) and συγκάθημαι, συγκαθίζω\[a] ([17\.13](#17.13)), since there appears to be an alternation in meaning between (1\) being in a position and (2\) assuming such a position. It would be possible to set up two distinct meanings or to assume that the respective forms are essentially ambiguous. In general, however, the participial forms indicate a state of being, while the non\-participial forms imply assuming a particular position of being seated. However, there are certain subtle differences in the tenses of the participial forms, and hence one cannot determine precisely what are the referential distinctions.

* **Associated Passages:** Mark 14:54; Acts 26:30

## συγχράομαι (id: 004702000000000)

συγχράομαι
==========

συγχράομαι (G4798)

verb \| χράομαι

34\.1 · Association · Associate

to associate, to be in the company of, to be involved with, association to associate with one another, normally involving spacial proximity and/or joint activity, and usually implying some kind of reciprocal relation or involvement In translating terms referring to association, one may employ a number of different kinds of expressions, for example, ‘to have something to do with,’ ‘to keep company with,’ ‘to go around with,’ ‘to join in doing things together,’ or ‘to become a companion of.’ Sometimes association is spoken of in terms of the impression made upon others, for example, ‘to be seen often together,’ ‘to be regarded as close friends,’ and even idiomatically as ‘to be another person’s shadow.’  
Some scholars interpret συγχράομαι in [JHN 4:9](https://ref.ly/Luke4:9) as denoting the use of the same dishes or utensils, so that one may translate this expression in [JHN 4:9](https://ref.ly/Luke4:9) as ‘Jews do not use dishes together with Samaritans’ or ‘Jews and Samaritans do not use the same dishes.’ Such an interpretation, however, is based upon etymological arguments for which there seems to be no certain justification in general Greek usage.

[JHN 4:9](https://ref.ly/Luke4:9)

* **Associated Passages:** John 4:9

[ACT 19:29](https://ref.ly/John19:29)

## συζάω (id: 004704000000000)

συζάω

to live together with, to live with to live in association with or together with someone else In [2CO 7:3](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:3) it is important to note that συζάω should not be understood in the sense of inhabiting the same house with someone else. ## συζήτησις (id: 004707000000000)

συζήτησις
=========

συζήτησις

noun, f. \| \-εως \| ζητέω

33\.440 · Communication · Dispute, Debate

dispute expression of forceful differences of opinion without necessarily having a presumed goal of seeking a solution This word is found as a variant reading only: ἀπῆλθον οἱ Ἰουδαῖοιπολλὴν ἔχοντες ἐν ἑαυτοῖς συζήτησιν ‘the Jews departed, disputing strongly among themselves’ [ACT 28:29](https://ref.ly/John28:29) (apparatus).

## συζωοποιέω (id: 004710000000000)

συζωοποιέω
==========

συζωοποιέω (G4806)

verb \| ζάω \+ ποιέω

23\.95 · Physiological Processes and States · Live, Die

to raise to life together with to cause to live again together with others There are serious semantic difficulties involved in a literal translation of συνεγείρω or συζωοποιέω, for a literal rendering could either be interpreted as ‘to be raised to life at the same time with’ or ‘to be raised to life in the same way as,’ but the reference in [COL 3:1](https://ref.ly/Phil3:1) and [EPH 2:5](https://ref.ly/Gal2:5) is to a spiritual existence more than to a literal resurrection of the body. This means that both συνεγείρω and συζωοποιέω must be understood as highly figurative. Hence, in [COL 3:1](https://ref.ly/Phil3:1) it may be necessary to translate εἰ οὖν συνηγέρθητε τῷ Χριστῷ as ‘since you have been raised to life, so to speak, with Christ’ or ‘since, as it were, you have been raised to life with Christ.’ In this way one may point to the fact of a figurative element involved.

[EPH 2:5](https://ref.ly/Gal2:5) · [COL 2:13](https://ref.ly/Phil2:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Ephesians 2:5; Colossians 2:13


## συκάμινος (id: 004711000000000)

συκάμινος
=========

συκάμινος (G4807)

noun, f. \| \-ου

3\.6 · Plants · Trees

mulberry tree a deciduous fruit tree growing to about 6 m; produces black berries containing a sweet reddish juice For languages which have no specific term for ‘mulberry tree,’ one can often employ a generic expression followed by a type of classifier, for example, ‘the tree called mulberry’ (in which case the term ‘mulberry’ may be borrowed from a dominant language of the area) or ‘a tree producing berries’; but in [LUK 17:6](https://ref.ly/Mark17:6) the focus is upon the tree as a large object and not upon the type of fruit which it produced. One can, therefore, say simply ‘this tree.’

[LUK 17:6](https://ref.ly/Mark17:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 17:6


## συκῆ (id: 004712000000000)

συκῆ
====

συκῆ (G4808)

noun, f. \| \-ῆς \| σῦκον

3\.5 · Plants · Trees

fig tree fruit tree; grows 5–8 m high; round crown and very deep roots; Ficus carica; fruit is about the size of a hen’s egg and can be green, yellow, purple, or brown depending on the type, and is sweet and soft In Palestine the fig tree occurs in both wild and cultivated forms and the latter is greatly valued for its sweet, edible fruit. It normally produces two crops each year: early figs ripening in June (late spring) and late ones in August and September (early fall).  
For languages in which a term for ‘fig tree’ is not known, one can often employ a borrowed term with a so\-called ‘classifier,’ for example, ‘a tree called fig’ or ‘a fruit tree producing fruit called figs.’ In many tropical areas of the world there are forest trees belonging to the botanical family of fig trees, but such trees generally produce inedible fruit. It may, however, be possible for a translator to use the term for such a forest tree but with the added explanation as to the fruit\- bearing quality of the trees mentioned in the Bible.

[MAT 21:19](https://ref.ly/Matt21:19) · [MAT 21:19](https://ref.ly/Matt21:19) · [MAT 21:20](https://ref.ly/Matt21:20) · [MAT 21:21](https://ref.ly/Matt21:21) · [MAT 24:32](https://ref.ly/Matt24:32) · [MRK 11:13](https://ref.ly/Matt11:13) · [MRK 11:20](https://ref.ly/Matt11:20) · [MRK 11:21](https://ref.ly/Matt11:21) · [MRK 13:28](https://ref.ly/Matt13:28) · [LUK 13:6](https://ref.ly/Mark13:6) · [LUK 13:7](https://ref.ly/Mark13:7) · [LUK 21:29](https://ref.ly/Mark21:29) · [JHN 1:48](https://ref.ly/Luke1:48) · [JHN 1:50](https://ref.ly/Luke1:50) · [JAS 3:12](https://ref.ly/Heb3:12) · [REV 6:13](https://ref.ly/Jude6:13)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 21:19; Matthew 21:20; Matthew 21:21; Matthew 24:32; Mark 11:13; Mark 11:20; Mark 11:21; Mark 13:28; Luke 13:6; Luke 13:7; Luke 21:29; John 1:48; John 1:50; James 3:12; Revelation 6:13


## συκομορέα (id: 004713000000000)

συκομορέα
=========

συκομορέα (G4809)

noun, f. \| \-ας \| σῦκον \+ μορον

3\.7 · Plants · Trees

sycamore\-fig tree a broad, heavy tree reaching a height of some fifteen meters (about fifty feet), with large, strong branches growing out from the trunk low down on the tree; fruit has the appearance of a small fig but its taste is relatively unpleasant As in the case of other specific trees for which no local term in the receptor language is available, one can borrow a word such as ‘sycamore’ from a dominant language in the area and add a classifier, for example, ‘tree called sycamore,’ but in a number of languages it may be appropriate to render συκομορέα in [LUK 19:4](https://ref.ly/Mark19:4) simply as ‘a big tree’ or ‘a wild fig tree.’

[LUK 19:4](https://ref.ly/Mark19:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 19:4

## συλαγωγέω (id: 004716000000000)
