to control completely, to take control of, to make a captive of (a figurative extension of meaning of συλαγωγέω ‘to carry off as booty or as captive in war,’ not occurring in the NT) to take over complete control of a person as one would a captive In some languages it is possible to preserve the figurative meaning of συλαγωγέω in [COL 2:8](https://ref.ly/Phil2:8) by employing a simile, for example, ‘see that no one makes you a kind of captive by human wisdom’ or ‘see to it that no one uses human wisdom and by this means makes you, so to speak, a captive.’

συλλαμβάνω

verb \| fut. συλλήμψομαι · aor. συνέλαβον · inf. συλλαβεῖν · pf. συνείληφα · aor.pass.inf. συλλημφθῆναι \| λαμβάνω

37\.109 · Control, Rule · Seize, Take into Custody

to seize, to catch, to take, to arrest to seize and to take along with

[MAT 26:55](https://ref.ly/Matt26:55) · [MRK 14:48](https://ref.ly/Matt14:48) · [LUK 5:9](https://ref.ly/Mark5:9) · [LUK 22:54](https://ref.ly/Mark22:54) · [JHN 18:12](https://ref.ly/Luke18:12) · [ACT 1:16](https://ref.ly/John1:16) · [ACT 12:3](https://ref.ly/John12:3) · [ACT 23:27](https://ref.ly/John23:27) · [ACT 26:21](https://ref.ly/John26:21)

23\.49 · Physiological Processes and States · Birth, Procreation

to conceive, to become pregnant In many languages the process of becoming pregnant is expressed in different ways: ‘to begin to become large,’ ‘to receive sperm,’ ‘to let a child enter,’ or ‘to stop bleeding’ (a reference to the cessation of menstrual periods).  
The phrases ἐν γαστρί ([LUK 1:31](https://ref.ly/Mark1:31)) and ἐν τῇ κοιλίᾳ ([LUK 2:21](https://ref.ly/Mark2:21)), meaning ‘in the womb,’ may be added to συλλαμβάνω without significant alteration of its meaning.

[LUK 1:24](https://ref.ly/Mark1:24) · [LUK 1:31](https://ref.ly/Mark1:31) · [LUK 1:36](https://ref.ly/Mark1:36) · [LUK 2:21](https://ref.ly/Mark2:21) · [JAS 1:15](https://ref.ly/Heb1:15)

35\.5 · (συλλαμβάνομαι) · Help, Care For · Help

to join in helping to help by joining in an activity or effort In a number of instances it is not necessary to specify the joint effort or activity, since this is supplied by the context itself as, for example, in [LUK 5:7](https://ref.ly/Mark5:7) in which ‘coming to help’ indicates clearly the joint efforts. But in some languages it may be important to use a specific expression rather than a generic one. Accordingly, ‘to come and help them’ in [LUK 5:7](https://ref.ly/Mark5:7) may be rendered as ‘to come and work with them.’

[LUK 5:7](https://ref.ly/Mark5:7) · [PHP 4:3](https://ref.ly/Eph4:3)

## συμμαρτυρέω (id: 004732000000000)

συμμαρτυρέω
===========

συμμαρτυρέω (G4828)

verb \| μαρτυρέω

33\.266 · Communication · Witness, Testify

to support by testimony, to provide supporting evidence, to testify in support to provide confirming evidence by means of a testimony It may be necessary in some languages to translate this phrase in [ROM 2:15](https://ref.ly/Acts2:15) as ‘their consciences say to them that this is true.’

## συμπαραγίνομαι (id: 004740000000000)

συμπαραγίνομαι
==============

συμπαραγίνομαι (G4836)

verb \| aor.ptc. συμπαραγενόμενος \| γίνομαι

15\.123 · Linear Movement · Gather, Cause To Come Together

to gather together, to come together, to go together, to meet, to assemble the movement of two or more objects to the same location1 In a number of languages important distinctions are made in terms referring to gathering or assembling of animate beings. The distinctions are usually based upon the number of individuals, the distance which they have come, and whether or not the individuals in question constitute a membership group or whether they are merely a loose aggregation. In view of these types of distinctions, it is likely that quite different terms will be required for the various contexts listed for this set of related meanings.

[LUK 23:48](https://ref.ly/Mark23:48)

1 There are no doubt a number of subtle distinctions in meaning in this series of expressions meaning to gather together, but the precise distinctions in meaning cannot be determined from existing NT contexts. 2 NEW NOTE

## συμπίνω (id: 004747000000000)

συμπίνω
=======

verb \| aor. συνέπιον \| πίνω

23\.36 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

to drink together drink together with others In rendering [ACT 10:41](https://ref.ly/John10:41) it may be necessary to restructure somewhat the expression of joint activity, for example, ‘we and he drank together’ or ‘he was one with us in drinking together.’ In some languages it may seem strange to speak of ‘eating and drinking,’ since both of these activities are often subsumed under a term for ‘dining.’ It may therefore be preferable in some languages to translate ‘we dined together with him’ or ‘we had our meals together with him.’

## συμφωνία (id: 004763000000000)

90\.2 · Case · Agent, Personal or Nonpersonal, Causative or Immediate, Direct or Indirect

**Collocation:** σὺν χειρί

by, with the help of (followed by the genitive; an idiom, literally: with the hand of) a marker of an associated agent

[ACT 7:35](https://ref.ly/John7:35)

1 The semantic domains of σύν\[a] ([89\.107](#89.107)) and μετά\[a] ([89\.108](#89.108)) overlap considerably, for in a number of instances essentially the same referential relationship can be expressed either by σύν\[a] or by μετά\[a]. However, in contexts involving hostility and combat, opposing forces may be spoken of as fighting against one another with μετά\[a]. In this type of context the preposition σύν\[a] would not be appropriate, since it would suggest those fighting on the same side, not on opposite sides of the conflict.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 26:35; Matthew 27:38; Matthew 27:44; Mark 2:26; Mark 4:10; Mark 8:34; Mark 9:4; Mark 15:27; Mark 15:32; Luke 1:56; Luke 2:5; Luke 2:13; Luke 5:9; Luke 7:6; Luke 7:12; Luke 8:1; Luke 8:38; Luke 8:51; Luke 9:32; Luke 20:1; Luke 22:14; Luke 22:56; Luke 23:32; Luke 24:10; Luke 24:24; Luke 24:29; Luke 24:33; Luke 24:44; John 12:2; John 18:1; John 21:3; Acts 1:14; Acts 1:22; Acts 2:14; Acts 3:4; Acts 3:8; Acts 4:13; Acts 4:14; Acts 5:1; Acts 5:17; Acts 5:21; Acts 5:26; Acts 8:20; Acts 8:31; Acts 10:2; Acts 10:20; Acts 10:23; Acts 11:12; Acts 13:7; Acts 14:4; Acts 14:5; Acts 14:13; Acts 14:20; Acts 14:28; Acts 15:22; Acts 15:25; Acts 16:3; Acts 16:32; Acts 17:34; Acts 18:8; Acts 18:18; Acts 19:38; Acts 20:36; Acts 21:5; Acts 21:16; Acts 21:18; Acts 21:24; Acts 21:26; Acts 21:29; Acts 22:9; Acts 23:15; Acts 23:27; Acts 23:32; Acts 24:24; Acts 25:23; Acts 26:13; Acts 27:2; Acts 28:16; Romans 6:8; Romans 16:14; Romans 16:15; 1 Corinthians 1:2; 1 Corinthians 10:13; 1 Corinthians 11:32; 1 Corinthians 15:10; 1 Corinthians 16:4; 1 Corinthians 16:19; 2 Corinthians 1:1; 2 Corinthians 1:21; 2 Corinthians 4:14; 2 Corinthians 9:4; 2 Corinthians 13:4; Galatians 1:2; Galatians 2:3; Galatians 3:9; Ephesians 3:18; Philippians 1:23; Philippians 2:22; Philippians 4:21; Colossians 2:5; Colossians 2:20; Colossians 3:3; Colossians 3:4; Colossians 4:9; 1 Thessalonians 4:14; 1 Thessalonians 4:17; 1 Thessalonians 5:10; James 1:11; 2 Peter 1:18; Matthew 25:27; Luke 5:19; Luke 19:23; Luke 23:11; Luke 24:21; Acts 4:27; Romans 8:32; 1 Corinthians 5:4; 2 Corinthians 8:19; Galatians 5:24; Ephesians 4:31; Philippians 1:1; Colossians 2:13; Colossians 3:9; Acts 7:35


## συνάγω (id: 004768000000000)

συνάγω
======

15\.125 · Linear Movement · Gather, Cause To Come Together

to gather together, to call together to cause to come together, whether of animate or inanimate objects

[MAT 2:4](https://ref.ly/Matt2:4) · [MAT 3:12](https://ref.ly/Matt3:12) · [MAT 6:26](https://ref.ly/Matt6:26) · [MAT 12:30](https://ref.ly/Matt12:30) · [MAT 13:30](https://ref.ly/Matt13:30) · [MAT 13:47](https://ref.ly/Matt13:47) · [MAT 22:10](https://ref.ly/Matt22:10) · [MAT 25:24](https://ref.ly/Matt25:24) · [MAT 25:26](https://ref.ly/Matt25:26) · [MAT 25:32](https://ref.ly/Matt25:32) · [MAT 27:27](https://ref.ly/Matt27:27) · [LUK 3:17](https://ref.ly/Mark3:17) · [LUK 11:23](https://ref.ly/Mark11:23) · [JHN 4:36](https://ref.ly/Luke4:36) · [JHN 11:47](https://ref.ly/Luke11:47) · [JHN 11:52](https://ref.ly/Luke11:52) · [JHN 15:6](https://ref.ly/Luke15:6) · [ACT 14:27](https://ref.ly/John14:27) · [ACT 15:30](https://ref.ly/John15:30) · [REV 16:14](https://ref.ly/Jude16:14) · [REV 16:16](https://ref.ly/Jude16:16) · [REV 20:8](https://ref.ly/Jude20:8)

57\.144 · Possess, Transfer, Exchange · Exchange

[LUK 15:13](https://ref.ly/Mark15:13)

15\.123 · (συνάγομαι) · Linear Movement · Gather, Cause To Come Together

to gather together, to come together, to go together, to meet, to assemble the movement of two or more objects to the same location2 In a number of languages important distinctions are made in terms referring to gathering or assembling of animate beings. The distinctions are usually based upon the number of individuals, the distance which they have come, and whether or not the individuals in question constitute a membership group or whether they are merely a loose aggregation. In view of these types of distinctions, it is likely that quite different terms will be required for the various contexts listed for this set of related meanings.

[MAT 13:2](https://ref.ly/Matt13:2) · [MAT 18:20](https://ref.ly/Matt18:20) · [MAT 22:34](https://ref.ly/Matt22:34) · [MAT 22:41](https://ref.ly/Matt22:41) · [MAT 24:28](https://ref.ly/Matt24:28) · [MAT 25:35](https://ref.ly/Matt25:35) · [MAT 25:38](https://ref.ly/Matt25:38) · [MAT 25:43](https://ref.ly/Matt25:43) · [MAT 26:3](https://ref.ly/Matt26:3) · [MAT 26:57](https://ref.ly/Matt26:57) · [MAT 27:17](https://ref.ly/Matt27:17) · [MAT 27:62](https://ref.ly/Matt27:62) · [MAT 28:12](https://ref.ly/Matt28:12) · [MRK 2:2](https://ref.ly/Matt2:2) · [MRK 4:1](https://ref.ly/Matt4:1) · [MRK 5:21](https://ref.ly/Matt5:21) · [MRK 6:30](https://ref.ly/Matt6:30) · [MRK 7:1](https://ref.ly/Matt7:1) · [LUK 22:66](https://ref.ly/Mark22:66) · [JHN 18:2](https://ref.ly/Luke18:2) · [ACT 4:5](https://ref.ly/John4:5) · [ACT 4:26](https://ref.ly/John4:26) · [ACT 4:27](https://ref.ly/John4:27) · [ACT 4:31](https://ref.ly/John4:31) · [ACT 11:26](https://ref.ly/John11:26) · [ACT 13:44](https://ref.ly/John13:44) · [ACT 15:6](https://ref.ly/John15:6) · [ACT 20:7](https://ref.ly/John20:7) · [ACT 20:8](https://ref.ly/John20:8) · [1CO 5:4](https://ref.ly/Rom5:4) · [REV 19:17](https://ref.ly/Jude19:17) · [REV 19:19](https://ref.ly/Jude19:19)

1 LUK 12:17 συνάγω in [LUK 12:17](https://ref.ly/Mark12:17) is another instance of a complex semantic structure involving not only the gathering together of material but the proper provision for it in some location. In [LUK 12:17](https://ref.ly/Mark12:17) the focus seems to be upon the storage rather than the process of harvesting. 2 There are no doubt a number of subtle distinctions in meaning in this series of expressions meaning ‘to gather together,’ but the precise distinctions in meaning cannot be determined from existing NT contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 2:4; Matthew 3:12; Matthew 6:26; Matthew 12:30; Matthew 13:30; Matthew 13:47; Matthew 22:10; Matthew 25:24; Matthew 25:26; Matthew 25:32; Matthew 27:27; Luke 3:17; Luke 11:23; John 4:36; John 11:47; John 11:52; John 15:6; Acts 14:27; Acts 15:30; Revelation 16:14; Revelation 16:16; Revelation 20:8; Luke 12:17; Luke 12:18; John 6:12; John 6:13; Luke 15:13; Matthew 13:2; Matthew 18:20; Matthew 22:34; Matthew 22:41; Matthew 24:28; Matthew 25:35; Matthew 25:38; Matthew 25:43; Matthew 26:3; Matthew 26:57; Matthew 27:17; Matthew 27:62; Matthew 28:12; Mark 2:2; Mark 4:1; Mark 5:21; Mark 6:30; Mark 7:1; Luke 22:66; John 18:2; Acts 4:5; Acts 4:26; Acts 4:27; Acts 4:31; Acts 11:26; Acts 13:44; Acts 15:6; Acts 20:7; Acts 20:8; 1 Corinthians 5:4; Revelation 19:17; Revelation 19:19


## συναγωγή (id: 004769000000000)

συναγωγή
========

συναγωγή (G4864)

noun, f. \| \-ῆς \| ἄγω

11\.44 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Religious

assembly, congregation an assembled group of worshipers or members of such a group In [JAS 2:2](https://ref.ly/Heb2:2) συναγωγή may indicate the place of gathering, rather than the assembled group (see συναγωγή\[c], [7\.20](#7.20)).  
In translating [JAS 2:2](https://ref.ly/Heb2:2) it is possible to render the conditional clause as ‘if a person comes into your church’ or ‘... into your congregation.’

[ACT 13:43](https://ref.ly/John13:43) · [JAS 2:2](https://ref.ly/Heb2:2) · [REV 2:9](https://ref.ly/Jude2:9) · [REV 3:9](https://ref.ly/Jude3:9)

11\.45 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Religious

synagogue, congregation a congregation of Jews Since the borrowed term ‘synagogue’ in receptor languages so frequently refers only to a building rather than to a congregation, it may be necessary in [ACT 9:2](https://ref.ly/John9:2) to say ‘he asked for letters of introduction to leaders of the synagogues’ or ‘... leaders of the congregations of Jews.’

[ACT 6:9](https://ref.ly/John6:9) · [ACT 9:2](https://ref.ly/John9:2) · [ACT 15:21](https://ref.ly/John15:21)

7\.20 · Constructions · Buildings

synagogue or Christian assembly place a building of assembly, associated with religious activity (normally a building in which Jewish worship took place and in which the Law was taught, but in [JAS 2:2](https://ref.ly/Heb2:2) a Christian assembly place) It is also possible to interpret συναγωγή in [JAS 2:2](https://ref.ly/Heb2:2) as a reference to an assembly of believers rather than to a building (see [11\.44](#11.44)).  
It is important to distinguish clearly between συναγωγή\[c] and ναός\[a] ([7\.15](#7.15)) or ἱερός\[b] ([7\.16](#7.16)). There were many synagogues, but only one Temple in Jerusalem, and it is not enough to speak of synagogues merely as ‘small temples.’ It is better either to borrow a term for synagogue or employ a descriptive equivalent such as ‘places where Jewish people worshiped God’ or ‘buildings for worshiping God.’  
It is also important to distinguish in translating between a term for ‘synagogue’ and for ‘church,’ whether as a reference to the congregation or to the building.

[MAT 4:23](https://ref.ly/Matt4:23) · [MAT 6:2](https://ref.ly/Matt6:2) · [MAT 6:5](https://ref.ly/Matt6:5) · [MAT 9:35](https://ref.ly/Matt9:35) · [MAT 10:17](https://ref.ly/Matt10:17) · [MAT 12:9](https://ref.ly/Matt12:9) · [MAT 13:54](https://ref.ly/Matt13:54) · [MAT 23:6](https://ref.ly/Matt23:6) · [MAT 23:34](https://ref.ly/Matt23:34) · [MRK 1:21](https://ref.ly/Matt1:21) · [MRK 1:23](https://ref.ly/Matt1:23) · [MRK 1:29](https://ref.ly/Matt1:29) · [MRK 1:39](https://ref.ly/Matt1:39) · [MRK 3:1](https://ref.ly/Matt3:1) · [MRK 6:2](https://ref.ly/Matt6:2) · [MRK 12:39](https://ref.ly/Matt12:39) · [MRK 13:9](https://ref.ly/Matt13:9) · [LUK 4:15](https://ref.ly/Mark4:15) · [LUK 4:16](https://ref.ly/Mark4:16) · [LUK 4:20](https://ref.ly/Mark4:20) · [LUK 4:28](https://ref.ly/Mark4:28) · [LUK 4:33](https://ref.ly/Mark4:33) · [LUK 4:38](https://ref.ly/Mark4:38) · [LUK 4:44](https://ref.ly/Mark4:44) · [LUK 6:6](https://ref.ly/Mark6:6) · [LUK 7:5](https://ref.ly/Mark7:5) · [LUK 8:41](https://ref.ly/Mark8:41) · [LUK 11:43](https://ref.ly/Mark11:43) · [LUK 12:11](https://ref.ly/Mark12:11) · [LUK 13:10](https://ref.ly/Mark13:10) · [LUK 20:46](https://ref.ly/Mark20:46) · [LUK 21:12](https://ref.ly/Mark21:12) · [JHN 6:59](https://ref.ly/Luke6:59) · [JHN 18:20](https://ref.ly/Luke18:20) · [ACT 9:20](https://ref.ly/John9:20) · [ACT 13:5](https://ref.ly/John13:5) · [ACT 13:14](https://ref.ly/John13:14) · [ACT 14:1](https://ref.ly/John14:1) · [ACT 15:21](https://ref.ly/John15:21) · [ACT 17:1](https://ref.ly/John17:1) · [ACT 17:10](https://ref.ly/John17:10) · [ACT 17:17](https://ref.ly/John17:17) · [ACT 18:4](https://ref.ly/John18:4) · [ACT 18:7](https://ref.ly/John18:7) · [ACT 18:19](https://ref.ly/John18:19) · [ACT 18:26](https://ref.ly/John18:26) · [ACT 19:8](https://ref.ly/John19:8) · [ACT 22:19](https://ref.ly/John22:19) · [ACT 24:12](https://ref.ly/John24:12) · [ACT 26:11](https://ref.ly/John26:11) · [JAS 2:2](https://ref.ly/Heb2:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 13:43; James 2:2; Revelation 2:9; Revelation 3:9; Acts 6:9; Acts 9:2; Acts 15:21; Matthew 4:23; Matthew 6:2; Matthew 6:5; Matthew 9:35; Matthew 10:17; Matthew 12:9; Matthew 13:54; Matthew 23:6; Matthew 23:34; Mark 1:21; Mark 1:23; Mark 1:29; Mark 1:39; Mark 3:1; Mark 6:2; Mark 12:39; Mark 13:9; Luke 4:15; Luke 4:16; Luke 4:20; Luke 4:28; Luke 4:33; Luke 4:38; Luke 4:44; Luke 6:6; Luke 7:5; Luke 8:41; Luke 11:43; Luke 12:11; Luke 13:10; Luke 20:46; Luke 21:12; John 6:59; John 18:20; Acts 9:20; Acts 13:5; Acts 13:14; Acts 14:1; Acts 17:1; Acts 17:10; Acts 17:17; Acts 18:4; Acts 18:7; Acts 18:19; Acts 18:26; Acts 19:8; Acts 22:19; Acts 24:12; Acts 26:11

## συναιχμάλωτος (id: 004774000000000)

συναιχμάλωτος
=============

συναιχμάλωτος (G4869)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| αἰχμή \+ ἅλωσις

37\.118 · Control, Rule · Imprison

fellow prisoner one who has been arrested and imprisoned along with someone else A strictly literal rendering of συναιχμάλωτος in the sense of ‘fellow captive’ could be misleading, since it might imply that Paul himself had been a soldier or civilian captured in a war.

[ROM 16:7](https://ref.ly/Acts16:7) · [COL 4:10](https://ref.ly/Phil4:10) · [PHM 1:23](https://ref.ly/Titus1:23)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 16:7; Colossians 4:10; Philemon 1:23

## συναλίζομαι (id: 004776000000000)

συναλίζομαι
===========

συναλίζομαι (G4871)

verb \| ἁλίζω

23\.13 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

to eat with eating together, with emphasis upon fellowship during the process συναλίζομαι in [ACT 1:4](https://ref.ly/John1:4) is interpreted by some as being συναλίζομαι\[b] to stay with ([41\.37](#41.37)) on the assumption that the occurrence in [ACT 1:4](https://ref.ly/John1:4) is simply an alternative spelling for συναυλίζομαι to stay with. This latter reading is supported by some manuscripts.

[ACT 1:4](https://ref.ly/John1:4)

41\.37 · Behavior and Related States · Particular Patterns of Behavior

to live with, to be in fellowship with to live in fellowship with others (a meaning of συναλίζομαι in view of its being regarded as a variant of συναυλίζομαι ‘to be with, to stay with,’ not occurring in the NT) συναλίζομαι in the sense of ‘to be together in fellowship’ fits well in the context of [ACT 1:4](https://ref.ly/John1:4), but this meaning would seem to be somewhat alien to general Greek usage, and therefore συναλίζομαι is more frequently understood in the context of [ACT 1:4](https://ref.ly/John1:4) as meaning ‘to be eating with’ (see [23\.13](#23.13)).

[ACT 1:4](https://ref.ly/John1:4)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 1:4


## συναλλάσσω (id: 004777000000000)

συναλλάσσω
==========

συναλλάσσω (G4900a)

verb \| ἀλλάσσω

40\.1 · Reconciliation, Forgiveness · Reconciliation

to reconcile, to make things right with one another, reconciliation to reestablish proper friendly interpersonal relations after these have been disrupted or broken (the componential features of this series of meanings involve (1\) disruption of friendly relations because of (2\) presumed or real provocation (3\) overt behavior designed to remove hostility, and (4\) restoration of original friendly relations)1 Because of the variety and complexity of the components involved in reconciliation, it is often necessary to use an entire phrase in order to communicate satisfactorily the meanings of the terms in this subdomain. In some languages, however, reconciliation is often spoken of in idiomatic terms, for example, ‘to cause to become friends again,’ ‘to cause to snap fingers again’ (a symbol of friendly interpersonal relations in many parts of Africa), ‘to cause to be one again,’ or ‘to take away the separation.’ A particularly crucial element in terms for reconciliation is the assigning of responsibility for original guilt in causing the estrangement. Some terms, for example, imply that the individual who initiates reconciliation is by doing so admitting his guilt in causing the estrangement. This, of course, provides a completely untenable meaning for reconciliation in speaking of God reconciling people to himself through Christ.  
In a number of languages the contextual basis for an expression for reconciliation is often found in terms relating to the reconciliation of husbands and wives. Such expressions fit in well with many contexts in the Scriptures, especially in speaking of reconciliation of people to God, since God is frequently referred to as the husband and the believers as the wife.  
This is the only instance of συναλλάσσω in the NT, and it has εἰς εἰρήνην added to emphasize peace as the goal, although the feature of making peace between previously hostile individuals is already implicit in the act of reconciliation.

[ACT 7:26](https://ref.ly/John7:26)

1 It may be that there are certain subtle distinctions of meaning in the series in [40\.1](#40.1), but there appears to be no contextual indication to justify setting up completely separate meanings.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 7:26

## συνανάκειμαι (id: 004779000000000)

συνανάκειμαι
============

συνανάκειμαι (G4873)

verb \| κεῖμαι

34\.10 · Association · Associate

to eat together, to associate in a meal to be associated with others in eating

[MAT 9:10](https://ref.ly/Matt9:10)1 · [MAT 14:9](https://ref.ly/Matt14:9) · [MRK 2:15](https://ref.ly/Matt2:15) · [MRK 6:22](https://ref.ly/Matt6:22) · [LUK 7:49](https://ref.ly/Mark7:49) · [LUK 14:10](https://ref.ly/Mark14:10) · [LUK 14:15](https://ref.ly/Mark14:15)

1 MAT 9:10 It is possible, of course, to understand συνανάκειμαι in [MAT 9:10](https://ref.ly/Matt9:10) as denoting merely the fact of eating together. However, in NT contexts such as this, the meaning appears to involve more than the mere fact of eating together; it is the association symbolized by eating together which is crucial and therefore constitutes the focal component of meaning.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 9:10; Matthew 14:9; Mark 2:15; Mark 6:22; Luke 7:49; Luke 14:10; Luke 14:15


## συναναμίγνυμι (id: 004780000000000)

συναναμίγνυμι
=============

συναναμίγνυμι (G4874)

verb \| μίγνυμι

34\.1 · Association · Associate

to associate, to be in the company of, to be involved with, association to associate with one another, normally involving spacial proximity and/or joint activity, and usually implying some kind of reciprocal relation or involvement In translating terms referring to association, one may employ a number of different kinds of expressions, for example, ‘to have something to do with,’ ‘to keep company with,’ ‘to go around with,’ ‘to join in doing things together,’ or ‘to become a companion of.’ Sometimes association is spoken of in terms of the impression made upon others, for example, ‘to be seen often together,’ ‘to be regarded as close friends,’ and even idiomatically as ‘to be another person’s shadow.’

[1CO 5:9](https://ref.ly/Rom5:9) · [1CO 5:11](https://ref.ly/Rom5:11) · [2TH 3:14](https://ref.ly/1Thess3:14)

## συναντιλαμβάνομαι (id: 004783000000000)

συναντιλαμβάνομαι
=================

συναντιλαμβάνομαι (G4878)

verb \| aor.subj. συναντιλάβωμαι \| λαμβάνω

35\.5 · Help, Care For · Help

to join in helping to help by joining in an activity or effort In a number of instances it is not necessary to specify the joint effort or activity, since this is supplied by the context itself as, for example, in [LUK 5:7](https://ref.ly/Mark5:7) in which ‘coming to help’ indicates clearly the joint efforts. But in some languages it may be important to use a specific expression rather than a generic one. ## συναπάγω (id: 004784000000000)

συναπάγω
========

συναπάγω (G4879) — συναπάγομαι

verb \| ἄγω

31\.76 · Hold a View, Believe, Trust · Change an Opinion Concerning Truth

to cause to go astray together, to deceive in addition, to lead astray with to cause someone else in addition to change from belief in what is true to belief in what is false

[GAL 2:13](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:13) · [2PE 3:17](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:17)

34\.1 · Association · Associate

to associate, to be in the company of, to be involved with, association to associate with one another, normally involving spacial proximity and/or joint activity, and usually implying some kind of reciprocal relation or involvement In translating terms referring to association, one may employ a number of different kinds of expressions, for example, ‘to have something to do with,’ ‘to keep company with,’ ‘to go around with,’ ‘to join in doing things together,’ or ‘to become a companion of.’ Sometimes association is spoken of in terms of the impression made upon others, for example, ‘to be seen often together,’ ‘to be regarded as close friends,’ and even idiomatically as ‘to be another person’s shadow.’  
It is also possible to interpret the phrase τοῖς ταπεινοῖς συναπαγόμενοι in [ROM 12:16](https://ref.ly/Acts12:16) as meaning ‘share in doing what is humble’ (see [41\.22](#41.22)).

[ROM 12:16](https://ref.ly/Acts12:16)

41\.22 · Behavior and Related States · Behavior, Conduct

to share, to share in doing to share in engaging continuously in some activity συναπάγομαι in [ROM 12:16](https://ref.ly/Acts12:16) may also be understood as meaning ‘to involve oneself with,’ and hence one may translate ‘do not be proud, but become involved with humble people’ or ‘... make friends with humble people.’ For this interpretation, see [34\.1](#34.1).

[ROM 12:16](https://ref.ly/Acts12:16)

87\.81 · Status · Slave, Free

## συνεγείρω (id: 004796000000000)

συνεγείρω
=========

συνεγείρω (G4891)

verb \| aor.pass. συνηγέρθην \| ἐγείρω

23\.95 · Physiological Processes and States · Live, Die

to raise to life together with to cause to live again together with others There are serious semantic difficulties involved in a literal translation of συνεγείρω or συζωοποιέω, for a literal rendering could either be interpreted as ‘to be raised to life at the same time with’ or ‘to be raised to life in the same way as,’ but the reference in [COL 3:1](https://ref.ly/Phil3:1) and [EPH 2:5](https://ref.ly/Gal2:5) is to a spiritual existence more than to a literal resurrection of the body. This means that both συνεγείρω and συζωοποιέω must be understood as highly figurative. Hence, in [COL 3:1](https://ref.ly/Phil3:1) it may be necessary to translate εἰ οὖν συνηγέρθητε τῷ Χριστῷ as ‘since you have been raised to life, so to speak, with Christ’ or ‘since, as it were, you have been raised to life with Christ.’ In this way one may point to the fact of a figurative element involved.

[EPH 2:6](https://ref.ly/Gal2:6) · [COL 2:12](https://ref.ly/Phil2:12) · [COL 3:1](https://ref.ly/Phil3:1)

* **Associated Passages:** Ephesians 2:6; Colossians 2:12; Colossians 3:1


## συνέδριον (id: 004797000000000)

συνέδριον
=========

συνέδριον (G4892)

noun, n. \| \-ου \| ἑδραῖος

11\.79 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

city council, council of judges a socio\-political group acting as a judicial council There are certain problems involved in the rendering of συνέδριον\[a] as ‘city council,’ since in so many parts of the world a group which would be designated as a ‘city council’ would be primarily legislative rather than judicial in function. It is for that reason that συνέδριον\[a] may be better translated in a number of instances as ‘the council which will judge you‘ or ‘before a group of men who will decide whether you have done right or wrong.’

[MAT 10:17](https://ref.ly/Matt10:17) · [MRK 13:9](https://ref.ly/Matt13:9)

11\.80 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Political

Sanhedrin, the council of the Jews the highest Jewish council, exercising jurisdiction in civil and religious matters, but having no power over life and death or over military actions or taxation1 In a number of languages συνέδριον\[b] can be rendered by a descriptive phrase, for example, ‘the most important council of the Jews’ or ‘the council that made decisions for the Jewish people.’

[MAT 5:22](https://ref.ly/Matt5:22) · [MAT 26:59](https://ref.ly/Matt26:59) · [MRK 14:55](https://ref.ly/Matt14:55) · [MRK 15:1](https://ref.ly/Matt15:1) · [LUK 22:66](https://ref.ly/Mark22:66) · [JHN 11:47](https://ref.ly/Luke11:47) · [ACT 4:15](https://ref.ly/John4:15) · [ACT 5:21](https://ref.ly/John5:21) · [ACT 5:27](https://ref.ly/John5:27) · [ACT 5:34](https://ref.ly/John5:34) · [ACT 5:41](https://ref.ly/John5:41) · [ACT 6:12](https://ref.ly/John6:12) · [ACT 6:15](https://ref.ly/John6:15) · [ACT 22:30](https://ref.ly/John22:30) · [ACT 23:1](https://ref.ly/John23:1) · [ACT 23:6](https://ref.ly/John23:6) · [ACT 23:15](https://ref.ly/John23:15) · [ACT 23:20](https://ref.ly/John23:20) · [ACT 23:28](https://ref.ly/John23:28) · [ACT 24:20](https://ref.ly/John24:20)

1 Though γερουσία and πρεσβυτέριον\[a] refer to the same council of the Jews as the term συνέδριον\[b] ([11\.80](#11.80)), this does not mean that the three terms are completely identical in meaning. The focus upon maturity of age and judgment as well as presumed social standing are more significant factors in γερουσία and πρεσβυτέριον\[a] than in συνέδριον\[b].

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 10:17; Mark 13:9; Matthew 5:22; Matthew 26:59; Mark 14:55; Mark 15:1; Luke 22:66; John 11:47; Acts 4:15; Acts 5:21; Acts 5:27; Acts 5:34; Acts 5:41; Acts 6:12; Acts 6:15; Acts 22:30; Acts 23:1; Acts 23:6; Acts 23:15; Acts 23:20; Acts 23:28; Acts 24:20


## συνείδησις (id: 004798000000000)

συνείδησις
==========

συνείδησις (G4893)

noun, f. \| \-εως \| εἶδος

28\.4 · Know · Know

to know, to be conscious of, to be aware of to be aware of information about something

[HEB 10:2](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:2) · [1PE 2:19](https://ref.ly/Jas2:19)

26\.13 · Psychological Faculties

moral sensitivity, conscience (contrast συνείδησις\[a] ‘knowledge about something,’ [28\.4](#28.4)) the psychological faculty which can distinguish between right and wrong In some languages συνείδησις\[b] may be rendered as ‘the inner voice’ or ‘the voice in one’s heart’ or ‘how one knows right from wrong.’ In some instances συνείδησις\[b] may be equivalent to some organ of the body, for example, heart or liver, but generally some descriptive phrase proves to be the most satisfactory equivalent.

[ACT 23:1](https://ref.ly/John23:1) · [ACT 24:16](https://ref.ly/John24:16) · [ROM 2:15](https://ref.ly/Acts2:15) · [ROM 9:1](https://ref.ly/Acts9:1) · [ROM 13:5](https://ref.ly/Acts13:5) · [1CO 8:7](https://ref.ly/Rom8:7) · [1CO 8:10](https://ref.ly/Rom8:10) · [1CO 8:12](https://ref.ly/Rom8:12) · [1CO 10:25](https://ref.ly/Rom10:25) · [1CO 10:27](https://ref.ly/Rom10:27) · [1CO 10:28](https://ref.ly/Rom10:28) · [1CO 10:29](https://ref.ly/Rom10:29) · [1CO 10:29](https://ref.ly/Rom10:29) · [2CO 1:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:12) · [2CO 4:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:2) · [2CO 5:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:11) · [1TI 1:5](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:5) · [1TI 1:19](https://ref.ly/2Thess1:19) · [1TI 3:9](https://ref.ly/2Thess3:9) · [1TI 4:2](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:2) · [2TI 1:3](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:3) · [TIT 1:15](https://ref.ly/2Tim1:15) · [HEB 9:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:9) · [HEB 9:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:14) · [HEB 10:22](https://ref.ly/Phlm10:22) · [HEB 13:18](https://ref.ly/Phlm13:18) · [1PE 3:16](https://ref.ly/Jas3:16) · [1PE 3:21](https://ref.ly/Jas3:21)

27\.54 · Learn · Be Willing To Learn

**Collocation:** καυστηριάζομαι τὴν συνείδησιν

to refuse to listen to one’s conscience, to be completely insensitive to (an idiom, literally: to be seared in the conscience, or: to be seared as to one’s conscience) to be unwilling to learn from one’s conscience

[1TI 4:2](https://ref.ly/2Thess4:2)

## σύνειμι (id: 004799000000000)

σύνειμι
=======

σύνειμι (G4896)

verb

15\.123 · Linear Movement · Gather, Cause To Come Together

to gather together, to come together, to go together, to meet, to assemble the movement of two or more objects to the same location1 In a number of languages important distinctions are made in terms referring to gathering or assembling of animate beings. The distinctions are usually based upon the number of individuals, the distance which they have come, and whether or not the individuals in question constitute a membership group or whether they are merely a loose aggregation. In view of these types of distinctions, it is likely that quite different terms will be required for the various contexts listed for this set of related meanings.

[LUK 8:4](https://ref.ly/Mark8:4)

85\.2 · Existence in Space · Be in a Place

to be with to be together with someone

[LUK 9:18](https://ref.ly/Mark9:18) · [ACT 22:11](https://ref.ly/John22:11)

1 There are no doubt a number of subtle distinctions in meaning in this series of expressions meaning to gather together, but the precise distinctions in meaning cannot be determined from existing NT contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 8:4; Luke 9:18; Acts 22:11

15\.123 · Linear Movement · Gather, Cause To Come Together

to gather together, to come together, to go together, to meet, to assemble the movement of two or more objects to the same location1 In a number of languages important distinctions are made in terms referring to gathering or assembling of animate beings. 23\.61 · Physiological Processes and States · Sexual Relations

to have sexual intercourse with a figurative extension of meaning of συνέρχομαι\[a] ‘to come together,’ [15\.123](#15.123) In almost all languages there are euphemistic ways of speaking about sexual intercourse, and the use of γινώσκω\[f] and συνέρχομαι\[c] is illustrative of this in the Greek NT. It is possible to translate γινώσκω in [LUK 1:34](https://ref.ly/Mark1:34) as simply ‘for I am not married to a man,’ and likewise, συνέρχομαι in [MAT 1:18](https://ref.ly/Matt1:18) may be rendered as ‘before they were married.’ In some languages one may use such expressions as ‘before they were joined’ or ‘before they slept together’ or ‘before they discovered one another.’

[MAT 1:18](https://ref.ly/Matt1:18)

## συνεσθίω (id: 004809000000000)

συνεσθίω
========

συνεσθίω (G4906)

verb \| aor. συνέφαγον \| ἐσθίω

23\.12 · Physiological Processes and States · Eat, Drink

to eat together to eat together with others In a number of languages a term meaning ‘to eat together with others’ is completely distinct from an expression referring to eating by one person. Furthermore, a term meaning basically ‘to eat together’ may focus primarily on conviviality and feasting rather than merely on the process of eating. In [ACT 11:3](https://ref.ly/John11:3) there is no indication of ‘feasting.’

## συνέχω (id: 004815000000000)

συνέχω
======

συνέχω (G4912)

verb \| aor. συνέσχον \| ἔχω

37\.17 · Control, Rule · Control, Restrain

to control, to restrain to exercise continuous control over someone or something There is usually no difficulty in speaking of ‘control’ if it is performed by a person as in [1PE 2:13](https://ref.ly/Jas2:13). However, it may not be possible to speak of ‘death’ having control, unless the language in question can personify death. In some instances [ACT 2:24](https://ref.ly/John2:24) (see [37\.16](#37.16)) must be rendered as ‘it was impossible for him to continue to be dead,’ and in [2CO 5:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:14) ‘Christ’s love controls us’ may be rendered as ‘the fact that Christ loves us causes us to act as we do.’

[2CO 5:14](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:14)

37\.122 · Control, Rule · Guard, Watch Over

to guard, to keep watch, custody to continue to hold in custody The act of holding someone in custody or guarding an individual may be expressed as ‘standing guard to see that someone will not escape’ or ‘watching carefully so that one cannot run off’ or ‘tying someone up so that he cannot leave.’

[LUK 22:63](https://ref.ly/Mark22:63)

19\.45 · Physical Impact · Press

to press in, to crowd around to press in hard from all sides

[LUK 8:45](https://ref.ly/Mark8:45) · [LUK 19:43](https://ref.ly/Mark19:43) · [PHP 1:23](https://ref.ly/Eph1:23)

24\.70 · Sensory Events and States · Hear

**Collocation:** συνέχω τὰ ὦτα

to refuse to listen, to refuse to pay attention (an idiom, literally: to hold the ears closed) to refuse to listen to what is being said In some languages the refusal to hear may be expressed idiomatically as ‘they put their hands over their ears’ or ‘they closed their ears’ or ‘the words never entered their heads.’

[ACT 7:57](https://ref.ly/John7:57)

90\.65 · Case · Experiencer

to experience, to have to experience a state or condition, generally involving duration

[MAT 4:24](https://ref.ly/Matt4:24) · [LUK 4:38](https://ref.ly/Mark4:38) · [LUK 8:37](https://ref.ly/Mark8:37) · [LUK 12:50](https://ref.ly/Mark12:50) · [ACT 28:8](https://ref.ly/John28:8)

25\.241 · Attitudes and Emotions · Worry, Anxiety, Distress, Peace

to be distressed, to be troubled to experience great psychological pressure and anxiety

[LUK 12:50](https://ref.ly/Mark12:50)

68\.19 · Aspect · Continue

to continue to give oneself to, to continue to apply oneself to to continue with close attention and devotion

[ACT 18:5](https://ref.ly/John18:5)

30\.18 · Think · To Think, Thought

**Collocation:** συνέχομαι ἐκ

to be pulled in two directions, to be betwixt and between, to have conflicting thoughts (an idiom, literally: to be held together from) to be in a mental state between two alternatives In a number of languages the rendering of this statement in [PHP 1:23](https://ref.ly/Eph1:23) must be expressed idiomatically, for example, ‘my mind is pulling me in two directions’ or ‘my thoughts are going in two different directions’ or ‘my heart is speaking two different words to me.’

[PHP 1:23](https://ref.ly/Eph1:23)

* **Associated Passages:** 2 Corinthians 5:14; Luke 22:63; Luke 8:45; Luke 19:43; Philippians 1:23; Acts 7:57; Matthew 4:24; Luke 4:38; Luke 8:37; Luke 12:50; Acts 28:8; Acts 18:5


## συνήδομαι (id: 004816000000000)

συνήδομαι
=========

συνήδομαι (G4913)

verb \| ἡδονή

25\.127 · Attitudes and Emotions · Happy, Glad, Joyful

to rejoice in, to delight in to be happy as the result of the pleasure derived from some experience or state In a number of languages one may speak of ‘one’s inner being’ as ‘one’s liver’ or ‘one’s heart’ or ‘one’s abdomen’ (employing a reference to one of the organs of the body as a focal element of the personality). But in some languages a more figurative and idiomatic expression may be employed, for example, ‘one’s inner counterpart’ or ‘the little one who stands inside of a person.’ It is often this central or crucial aspect of the personality which must be referred to in contexts speaking of the type of pleasure or delight which one might have in the law of God.

[ROM 7:22](https://ref.ly/Acts7:22)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 7:22


## συνήθεια (id: 004817000000000)

συνήθεια
========

συνήθεια (G4914)

noun, f. \| \-ας \| ἐθίζω

41\.25 · Behavior and Related States · Custom, Tradition

custom, habit a pattern of behavior more or less fixed by tradition and generally sanctioned by the society In a number of languages there is no noun for ‘custom’ or ‘habit,’ but the same meaning is communicated by verbal aspects or adverbial phrases indicating habitual action. For example, in the case of [JHN 19:40](https://ref.ly/Luke19:40) one may translate in some languages ‘as is the way in which Jews always bury people,’ and for [1CO 11:16](https://ref.ly/Rom11:16) one may translate ‘this is not what we constantly do.’

[JHN 18:39](https://ref.ly/Luke18:39) · [1CO 8:7](https://ref.ly/Rom8:7) · [1CO 11:16](https://ref.ly/Rom11:16)

* **Associated Passages:** John 18:39; 1 Corinthians 8:7; 1 Corinthians 11:16

**Collocation:** συνθρύπτω τὴν καρδίαν

to make grieve, to break one’s heart (an idiom, literally: to break the heart) to cause great sorrow and grief It is rare that one can reproduce in a literal form the idiom συνθρύπτω τὴν καρδίαν. [MAT 13:13](https://ref.ly/Matt13:13) · [MAT 13:14](https://ref.ly/Matt13:14) · [MAT 13:15](https://ref.ly/Matt13:15) · [MAT 13:19](https://ref.ly/Matt13:19) · [MAT 13:23](https://ref.ly/Matt13:23) · [MAT 13:51](https://ref.ly/Matt13:51) · [MAT 15:10](https://ref.ly/Matt15:10) · [MAT 16:12](https://ref.ly/Matt16:12) · [MAT 17:13](https://ref.ly/Matt17:13) · [MRK 4:12](https://ref.ly/Matt4:12) · [MRK 6:52](https://ref.ly/Matt6:52) · [MRK 7:14](https://ref.ly/Matt7:14) · [MRK 8:17](https://ref.ly/Matt8:17) · [MRK 8:21](https://ref.ly/Matt8:21) · [LUK 2:50](https://ref.ly/Mark2:50) · [LUK 8:10](https://ref.ly/Mark8:10) · [LUK 18:34](https://ref.ly/Mark18:34) · [LUK 24:45](https://ref.ly/Mark24:45) · [ACT 7:25](https://ref.ly/John7:25) · [ACT 7:25](https://ref.ly/John7:25) · [ACT 28:26](https://ref.ly/John28:26) · [ACT 28:27](https://ref.ly/John28:27) · [ROM 15:21](https://ref.ly/Acts15:21) · [2CO 10:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:12) · [EPH 5:17](https://ref.ly/Gal5:17)

32\.26 · Understand · Capacity for Understanding

to be able to comprehend, to understand, to be intelligent, insight, intelligence to be able to understand and evaluate

[ROM 3:11](https://ref.ly/Acts3:11)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 13:13; Matthew 13:14; Matthew 13:15; Matthew 13:19; Matthew 13:23; Matthew 13:51; Matthew 15:10; Matthew 16:12; Matthew 17:13; Mark 4:12; Mark 6:52; Mark 7:14; Mark 8:17; Mark 8:21; Luke 2:50; Luke 8:10; Luke 18:34; Luke 24:45; Acts 7:25; Acts 28:26; Acts 28:27; Romans 15:21; 2 Corinthians 10:12; Ephesians 5:17; Romans 3:11


## συνίστημι (id: 004824000000000)

συνίστημι
=========

συνίστημι (G4921) — συνίσταμαι

verb \| aor. συνέστησα · pf. συνέστηκα · ptc. συνεστώς \| ἵστημι

33\.344 · Communication · Recommend, Propose

to recommend to indicate approval of a person or event, with the implication that others adopt the same attitude

[ROM 16:1](https://ref.ly/Acts16:1) · [2CO 3:1](https://ref.ly/1Cor3:1) · [2CO 4:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor4:2) · [2CO 5:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:12) · [2CO 10:12](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:12) · [2CO 10:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:18) · [2CO 10:18](https://ref.ly/1Cor10:18) · [2CO 12:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor12:11)

28\.49 · Know · Well Known, Clearly Shown, Revealed

to make known by action, to demonstrate, to show to cause something to be known by action In a number of languages the expression ‘to show oneself to be’ may best be rendered as ‘to cause people to know that one is,’ and therefore this expression in [2CO 6:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:4) may be rendered as ‘in everything causing people to know by what we do that we are servants of God.’

[ROM 3:5](https://ref.ly/Acts3:5) · [ROM 5:8](https://ref.ly/Acts5:8) · [2CO 6:4](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:4) · [2CO 7:11](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:11) · [GAL 2:18](https://ref.ly/2Cor2:18)

63\.6 · Whole, Unite, Part, Divide · Unite

to hold together to bring together or hold together something in its proper or appropriate place or relationship In [COL 1:17](https://ref.ly/Phil1:17) it may not be easy to indicate clearly the relationship of the phrase ‘in him’ to the rest of the expression, namely, ‘all things hold together.’ Some translations have expanded the expression ‘in him’ to ‘in union with him’ or ‘in view of the fact that we are joined together with him.’  
It is also possible to understand ἐν αὐτῷ as indicating agent, so that this expression in [COL 1:17](https://ref.ly/Phil1:17) may mean ‘by means of him all things hold together.’

[COL 1:17](https://ref.ly/Phil1:17)

17\.2 · (συνίσταμαι (and perfect active)) · Stances and Events Related to Stances · Stand

to stand with to stand together with someone It is, of course, essential to avoid the idiomatic meaning of ‘to stand with’ in a sense of ‘to support.’ In this context the emphasis is simply upon being present with.

[LUK 9:32](https://ref.ly/Mark9:32)

13\.82 · (συνίσταμαι (and perfect active)) · Be, Become, Exist, Happen · Exist

to come into existence, to be formed to come into existence, with the implication of acquiring form and substance

[2PE 3:5](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:5)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 16:1; 2 Corinthians 3:1; 2 Corinthians 4:2; 2 Corinthians 5:12; 2 Corinthians 10:12; 2 Corinthians 10:18; 2 Corinthians 12:11; Romans 3:5; Romans 5:8; 2 Corinthians 6:4; 2 Corinthians 7:11; Galatians 2:18; Colossians 1:17; Luke 9:32; 2 Peter 3:5

## συντελέω (id: 004836000000000)

συντελέω
========

verb \| τελέω

68\.22 · Aspect · Complete, Finish, Succeed

to complete, to finish, to end, to accomplish to bring an activity to a successful finish1 It is also possible to render this phrase in [ROM 9:28](https://ref.ly/Acts9:28) as ‘for he will settle the account,’ the implication being that he will accomplish what he has said he would do.

[HEB 8:8](https://ref.ly/Phlm8:8)

67\.67 · Time · A Point of Time with Reference to Duration of Time: Beginning, End

[ACT 21:27](https://ref.ly/John21:27)

1 There are no doubt certain subtle distinctions, particularly of emphasis, in the series τελέω, ἐκτελέω\[a], ἀποτελέω, ἐπιτελέω\[a], συντελέω\[a], and τελειόω\[c], but it is not possible to determine with precision the particular distinctions on the basis of existing contexts, though possibly ἐκτελέω and ἀποτελέω emphasize more finality, while ἐπιτελέω\[a] may focus upon the resulting purpose.

## σύντριμμα (id: 004843000000000)

=========

noun, n. \| \-τος \| τρίβω (rub) · τρίβος

20\.59 · Violence, Harm, Destroy, Kill · Destroy

ruin, destruction a state of destruction and ruin In some languages it is impossible to speak of ‘leaving ruin’ except in the sense of going off from ruin. ## σύντροφος (id: 004844000000000)

σύντροφος
=========

σύντροφος (G4939)

adjc. \| \-ου \| τρέφω

10\.51 · Kinship Terms · Kinship Relations of the Same Generation

foster brother or foster sister a person offered parental care and/or adoption along with the reference person, though not related by blood It is possible, however, that σύντροφος in [ACT 13:1](https://ref.ly/John13:1) has the meaning of ‘a close friend from childhood’ (see [34\.15](#34.15)).  
In some languages ‘a foster brother’ may be referred to as ‘a person who becomes a brother by being adopted’ or ‘a person who grows up just as though he were a brother.’

[ACT 13:1](https://ref.ly/John13:1)

34\.15 · Association · Associate

close friend, intimate friend, friend since childhood a close friend on the basis of having been brought up together Some scholars, however, understand σύντροφος in [ACT 13:1](https://ref.ly/John13:1) as being an instance of σύντροφος\[a] 'foster brother' (see [10\.51](#10.51)).

[ACT 13:1](https://ref.ly/John13:1)

## συνυπουργέω (id: 004848000000000)

συνυπουργέω
===========

συνυπουργέω (G4943)

verb \| ἐργάζομαι

35\.5 · Help, Care For · Help

to join in helping to help by joining in an activity or effort In a number of instances it is not necessary to specify the joint effort or activity, since this is supplied by the context itself as, for example, in [LUK 5:7](https://ref.ly/Mark5:7) in which ‘coming to help’ indicates clearly the joint efforts. But in some languages it may be important to use a specific expression rather than a generic one. Accordingly, ‘to come and help them’ in [LUK 5:7](https://ref.ly/Mark5:7) may be rendered as ‘to come and work with them.’

15\.212 · Linear Movement · Pull, Draw, Drag

to pull, to drag, to draw to pull or drag, requiring force because of the inertia of the object being dragged

[JHN 21:8](https://ref.ly/Luke21:8) · [ACT 14:19](https://ref.ly/John14:19) · [REV 12:4](https://ref.ly/Jude12:4)

15\.178 · Linear Movement · Lead, Bring, Take

to drag, to lead by force to drag or pull by physical force, often implying resistance

[ACT 8:3](https://ref.ly/John8:3) · [ACT 17:6](https://ref.ly/John17:6)

* **Associated Passages:** John 21:8; Acts 14:19; Revelation 12:4; Acts 8:3; Acts 17:6

11\.9 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · General

co\-member a person who is a member of a group, with emphasis upon his coordinate relation to other members of the group The concept of ‘being a co\-member’ may be expressed in some languages as ‘a person who is counted along with others,’ so that in [EPH 3:6](https://ref.ly/Gal3:6) one may translate ‘the Gentiles are counted along with the Jews in sharing in the promise’ or even ‘the Gentiles along with the Jews share in the promise.’

## συστενάζω (id: 004863000000000)

συστενάζω
=========

συστενάζω (G4959)

verb \| στενάζω

25\.145 · Attitudes and Emotions · Laugh, Cry, Groan

to groan together, to sigh together to groan or to sigh together with someone else In [ROM 8:22](https://ref.ly/Acts8:22) συστενάζω is used figuratively. It may be difficult to speak of ‘all of creation groans together,’ since the phrase ‘all of creation’ would seem to be a total unit. It may therefore be necessary to translate ‘all of creation groans together’ as ‘all parts of the creation groan together’ or ‘everything that has been created is groaning at the same time.’

[ROM 8:22](https://ref.ly/Acts8:22)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 8:22


## συστοιχέω (id: 004864000000000)

συστοιχέω
=========

συστοιχέω (G4960)

verb \| στοιχέω

58\.68 · Nature, Class, Example · Archetype, Corresponding Type \[Antitype]

to correspond to, to stand for, to be a figure of, to represent to correspond to something else in certain significant features In a number of languages συστοιχέω in a context such as [GAL 4:25](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:25) may be best rendered as ‘points to’ or ‘is really talking about,’ so that one may render this expression in [GAL 4:25](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:25) as ‘Mount Sinai ... really points to the present Jerusalem’ or ‘Hagar ... really points to the present Jerusalem.’ The full form of [GAL 4:25](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:25) may be rendered as ‘Hagar, who stands for Mount Sinai in Arabia, represents the present Jerusalem.’

[GAL 4:25](https://ref.ly/2Cor4:25)

* **Associated Passages:** Galatians 4:25


## συστρατιώτης (id: 004865000000000)

συστρατιώτης
============

συστρατιώτης (G4961)

noun, m. \| \-ου \| στρατεύομαι

34\.19 · Association · Associate

one who struggles along with, one who works arduously along with, fellow struggler (a figurative extension of meaning of συστρατιώτης ‘fellow soldier,’ not occurring in the NT) one who serves in arduous tasks or undergoes severe experiences together with someone else A strictly literal translation of συστρατιώτης in [PHM 1:2](https://ref.ly/Titus1:2) might imply that Paul himself was a soldier and therefore, in a sense, a secret agent of some military force. Accordingly, it may be necessary to employ a simile, for example, ‘who works like a fellow soldier’ or ‘one who experiences great hardships along with us.’

[PHP 2:25](https://ref.ly/Eph2:25) · [PHM 1:2](https://ref.ly/Titus1:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Philippians 2:25; Philemon 1:2


## συστρέφω (id: 004866000000000)

συστρέφω
========

συστρέφω (G4962) — συστρέφομαι

verb \| στρέφω

15\.125 · Linear Movement · Gather, Cause To Come Together

to gather together, to call together to cause to come together, whether of animate or inanimate objects

[ACT 28:3](https://ref.ly/John28:3)

15\.123 · (συστρέφομαι) · Linear Movement · Gather, Cause To Come Together

to gather together, to come together, to go together, to meet, to assemble the movement of two or more objects to the same location1 In a number of languages important distinctions are made in terms referring to gathering or assembling of animate beings. The distinctions are usually based upon the number of individuals, the distance which they have come, and whether or not the individuals in question constitute a membership group or whether they are merely a loose aggregation. In view of these types of distinctions, it is likely that quite different terms will be required for the various contexts listed for this set of related meanings.

[MAT 17:22](https://ref.ly/Matt17:22)

1 There are no doubt a number of subtle distinctions in meaning in this series of expressions meaning to gather together, but the precise distinctions in meaning cannot be determined from existing NT contexts.

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 28:3; Matthew 17:22

## σφραγίς (id: 004877000000000)

σφραγίς
=======

σφραγίς (G4973)

noun, f. \| \-ῖδος \| σφραγίζω

6\.54 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Marking and Writing

seal, signet an engraved object used to make a mark denoting ownership, approval, or closure of something (normally done by pressing into heated wax and usually attached to a document or letter) In some languages the closest equivalent to ‘seal’ or ‘signet’ is the mark made by the seal, for example, ‘the symbol of his name’ or ‘the mark of his ownership.’ In certain contexts one may employ a phrase such as ‘the instrument by which a mark is made.’

[REV 7:2](https://ref.ly/Jude7:2)

6\.62 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Marking and Writing

seal the substance which bears the imprint of a seal or signet (see σφραγίς\[a], [6\.54](#6.54)), used for sealing a document or for showing ownership or endorsement In [REV 5:2](https://ref.ly/Jude5:2) one may speak of ‘the wax that keeps the scroll closed,’ but in some languages it may be better to use a more general statement, for example, ‘the substance with which the scroll is sealed’ or ‘the substance that kept the scroll closed.’

33\.483 · Communication · Non\-Verbal Communication

mark, seal the impression of a signet ring or seal, primarily indicating ownership One may also translate this clause in [REV 9:4](https://ref.ly/Jude9:4) as ‘who do not have the mark on their foreheads which shows that they belong to God.’

[2TI 2:19](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:19) · [REV 9:4](https://ref.ly/Jude9:4)

33\.47 · Communication · Written Language

mark, inscription the mark or impression made by a seal or stamp

[2TI 2:19](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:19)

73\.9 · Genuine, Phony

certification, validation, proof, evidence of genuineness that which confirms or attests to the genuineness of something

[ROM 4:11](https://ref.ly/Acts4:11) · [1CO 9:2](https://ref.ly/Rom9:2)

* **Associated Passages:** Revelation 7:2; Revelation 5:1; Revelation 5:2; Revelation 5:5; Revelation 5:9; Revelation 6:1; Revelation 6:3; Revelation 6:5; Revelation 6:7; Revelation 6:9; Revelation 6:12; Revelation 8:1; 2 Timothy 2:19; Revelation 9:4; Romans 4:11; 1 Corinthians 9:2

## σχῆμα (id: 004880000000000)

σχῆμα
=====

σχῆμα (G4976)

noun, n. \| \-τος \| ἔχω

58\.7 · Nature, Class, Example · Nature, Character

form, nature, structure the form or nature of something, with special reference to its outer form or structure In [1CO 7:31](https://ref.ly/Rom7:31) σχῆμα does not refer to the physical form of the earth but to the way of life in the world. The reference is primarily to culture rather than to physical form. It is possible, therefore, to render this expression in [1CO 7:31](https://ref.ly/Rom7:31) as ‘the way of life in this world is passing away.’

[1CO 7:31](https://ref.ly/Rom7:31)

58\.17 · Nature, Class, Example · Appearance as an Outward Manifestation of Form

## σχίζω (id: 004881000000000)

=====

σχίζω (G4977)

verb \| σχίσμα

19\.27 · Physical Impact · Split, Tear

to split, to tear to split or to tear an object into at least two parts In some languages the meaning of σχίζω in [MRK 1:10](https://ref.ly/Matt1:10) may be best expressed as ‘the sky tore’ or ‘there was a slit in the sky’ or possibly ‘there was suddenly an opening in the sky.’ The adverb ‘suddenly’ may provide some of the implications of the splitting involved in the verb σχίζω.

[MRK 1:10](https://ref.ly/Matt1:10) · [MRK 15:38](https://ref.ly/Matt15:38) · [LUK 5:36](https://ref.ly/Mark5:36) · [LUK 5:36](https://ref.ly/Mark5:36) · [JHN 19:24](https://ref.ly/Luke19:24) · [JHN 21:11](https://ref.ly/Luke21:11)

to divide, to split, to tear in two to split or divide into two parts

## σχίσμα (id: 004882000000000)

σχίσμα
======

σχίσμα (G4978)

noun, n. \| \-τος \| σχίζω

19\.28 · Physical Impact · Split, Tear

tear (derivative of σχίζω\[a] ‘to split, to tear,’ [19\.27](#19.27)) the condition resulting from the splitting or tearing The separation indicated by σχίσμα\[a] may be quite different in some languages, depending upon the substance involved, for example, cloth, leather, paper, and clouds.

[MAT 9:16](https://ref.ly/Matt9:16) · [MRK 2:21](https://ref.ly/Matt2:21)

39\.13 · Hostility, Strife · Division

division, discord a division into opposing groups, generally two In some languages the equivalent of ‘causing division’ is literally ‘to cause two groups in place of one group,’ but more frequently the equivalent is expressed in terms of attitudes, for example, ‘to cause people to be angry at one another’ or ‘to cause people not to like one another’ or ‘to cause people to think of one another as enemies.’

[JHN 7:43](https://ref.ly/Luke7:43) · [JHN 9:16](https://ref.ly/Luke9:16) · [JHN 10:19](https://ref.ly/Luke10:19) · [1CO 1:10](https://ref.ly/Rom1:10) · [1CO 11:18](https://ref.ly/Rom11:18) · [1CO 12:25](https://ref.ly/Rom12:25)

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 9:16; Mark 2:21; John 7:43; John 9:16; John 10:19; 1 Corinthians 1:10; 1 Corinthians 11:18; 1 Corinthians 12:25


## σχοινίον (id: 004883000000000)

σχοινίον
========

σχοινίον (G4979)

noun, n. \| \-ου

6\.18 · Artifacts · Instruments Used in Binding and Fastening

cord, rope thick cord formed by twisting or braiding several strands together; made of a variety of materials, including palm fibers, linen, or reeds The ropes mentioned in [ACT 27:32](https://ref.ly/John27:32) would obviously have been rather thick, while in [JHN 2:15](https://ref.ly/Luke2:15) the whip which Jesus made in driving the animals and merchants out of the Temple would probably have consisted of strong cords.

[JHN 2:15](https://ref.ly/Luke2:15) · [ACT 27:32](https://ref.ly/John27:32)

* **Associated Passages:** John 2:15; Acts 27:32

## σχολή (id: 004885000000000)

σχολή
=====

σχολή (G4981)

noun, f. \| \-ῆς \| σχολάζω

7\.14 · Constructions · Buildings

lecture hall, school a building where teachers and students met for study and discussion In [ACT 19:9](https://ref.ly/John19:9) it is better to use a translation such as ‘lecture hall’ rather than ‘school,’ since one does not wish to give the impression of the typical classroom situation characteristic of present\-day schools. One may translate the relevant context of [ACT 19:9](https://ref.ly/John19:9) as ‘every day Paul discussed with people in the lecture hall which belonged to Tyrannus’ or ‘... in a hall where Tyrannus often taught’ or ‘... lectured.’

[ACT 19:9](https://ref.ly/John19:9)

* **Associated Passages:** Acts 19:9

23\.136 · Physiological Processes and States · Health, Vigor, Strength

to heal, to cure, to make well, healing to cause someone to become well again after having been sick2 In a number of languages there are different terms for ‘healing’ depending upon the type of sickness or illness which is involved.

[MAT 9:21](https://ref.ly/Matt9:21) · [MAT 9:22](https://ref.ly/Matt9:22) · [MAT 9:22](https://ref.ly/Matt9:22) · [MRK 5:23](https://ref.ly/Matt5:23) · [MRK 5:28](https://ref.ly/Matt5:28) · [MRK 5:34](https://ref.ly/Matt5:34) · [MRK 6:56](https://ref.ly/Matt6:56) · [MRK 10:52](https://ref.ly/Matt10:52) · [LUK 8:36](https://ref.ly/Mark8:36) · [LUK 8:48](https://ref.ly/Mark8:48) · [LUK 8:50](https://ref.ly/Mark8:50) · [LUK 17:19](https://ref.ly/Mark17:19) · [LUK 18:42](https://ref.ly/Mark18:42) · [JHN 11:12](https://ref.ly/Luke11:12) · [ACT 4:9](https://ref.ly/John4:9) · [ACT 14:9](https://ref.ly/John14:9) · [JAS 5:15](https://ref.ly/Heb5:15)

1 The meanings of σῴζω and σωτηρία in this subdomain differ from the meaning of ἐξαιρέομαι ([21\.17](#21.17)) in implying not only a rescue from danger but a restoration to a former state of safety and well being. It is this aspect of the terms σῴζω and σωτηρία which provides such an excellent basis for their use in denoting religious salvation. 2 It is possible that διασῴζω\[b] is somewhat more emphatic in meaning than σῴζω\[c]. It is also possible that in a number of contexts σῴζω and διασῴζω may have the added implication of having rescued such persons from a state of illness.

## σῶμα (id: 004887000000000)

σῶμα
====

σῶμα (G4983)

noun, n. \| \-τος \| σύσσωμος · σωματικός · σωματικῶς

8\.1 · Body, Body Parts, and Body Products · Body

body the physical body of persons, animals, or plants,1 either dead or alive In a number of languages a clear distinction must be made between the body of a living person and a dead body (or corpse). Other languages distinguish between the bodies of persons and the bodies of animals, and frequently the term for a body of a plant is distinct from those referring to persons or animals. Often a term for body consists of a phrase, for example, ‘flesh and bones,’ and in a number of languages a reference to the body is made primarily by referring to the person himself. For example, in [MAT 26:12](https://ref.ly/Matt26:12) (‘has poured this ointment on my body’) the appropriate equivalent may be ‘has poured this ointment on me.’ In certain instances ‘body’ may be rendered as something which is experienced. For example, in [1CO 6:20](https://ref.ly/Rom6:20) ‘glorify God through your body’ may be rendered as ‘glorify God through what you do’ or ‘... do in your body.’

9\.8 · People · Human Beings

11\.34 · Groups and Classes of Persons and Members of Such Groups and Classes · Socio\-Religious

congregation, Christian group, church (a figurative extension of meaning of σῶμα\[a] ‘body,’ [8\.1](#8.1)) believers in Christ who are joined together as a group, with the implication of each having a distinctive function within the group Though in some languages it may seem relatively strange to speak of an organization of persons as a ‘body,’ it is important to try to preserve in one way or another this figurative meaning of σῶμα, since it plays such an important role in various phases of Paul’s teaching. It is frequently necessary, however, to change the metaphor into a simile, as has already been suggested in the translation of [EPH 4:12](https://ref.ly/Gal4:12).

58\.66 · Nature, Class, Example · Archetype, Corresponding Type \[Antitype]

[COL 2:17](https://ref.ly/Phil2:17)

1\.26 · Geographical Objects and Features · Heavenly Bodies

**Collocation:** σῶμα ἐπουράνιον

heavenly body (an idiom, literally: heavenly body, occurring in the NT only in the plural3) the luminous objects in the sky: sun, moon, and other planets and stars See also [1\.8](#1.8).  
The phrase σῶμα ἐπουράνιον is a highly generic expression which in the plural is sometimes translatable as ‘lights in the sky,’ but more often than not it may be necessary to identify the various heavenly bodies as ‘sun, moon, and stars.’ In certain contexts one may also wish to identify the planets, often spoken of as ‘wandering stars’ or ‘moving stars’ (reflecting the etymology of the English word planet, which is derived from a Greek word meaning ‘wanderer’). These are, of course, not to be confused with shooting stars and comets in the sky.

[1CO 15:40](https://ref.ly/Rom15:40)

23\.111 · Physiological Processes and States · Live, Die

**Collocation:** ἐκδημέω ἐκ τοῦ σώματος

to die (an idiom, literally: to leave home from the body) euphemistic expressions for dying

[2CO 5:8](https://ref.ly/1Cor5:8)

1 The use of σῶμα\[a] in connection with plants is quite rare in extrabiblical Greek and perhaps only occurs in [1CO 15:37](https://ref.ly/Rom15:37) because of the analogy between plants and persons in treating the theme of the resurrection body. 2 σῶμα\[b] is very similar in meaning to σάρξ\[f] ([26\.7](#26.7)) in that both denote human nature. There are, however, certain connotative differences in meaning in that σάρξ\[f] seems to focus more upon the purely physical desires of human nature, with the possible implication of greater emphasis upon normal sexual impulses. 3 It is difficult to say whether the phrase σῶμα ἐπουράνιον should be treated as a fixed phrase with a shifted meaning for the head word σῶμα and thus a type of idiom, or whether it should be considered a semantically endocentric expression and thus not a so\-called lexical unit. The treatment of σῶμα ἐπουράνιον as semantically endocentric can certainly be justified by the highly generic meaning of σῶμα as body, object, but one may also argue that the restriction in reference to the sun, moon, planets, and stars provides a basis for regarding it as semantically exocentric.

* **Associated Passages:** Matthew 5:29; Matthew 5:30; Matthew 6:22; Matthew 6:23; Matthew 6:25; Matthew 10:28; Matthew 26:12; Matthew 26:26; Matthew 27:52; Matthew 27:58; Matthew 27:59; Mark 5:29; Mark 14:8; Mark 14:22; Mark 15:43; Luke 11:34; Luke 11:36; Luke 12:4; Luke 12:22; Luke 12:23; Luke 17:37; Luke 22:19; Luke 23:52; Luke 23:55; Luke 24:3; Luke 24:23; John 2:21; John 19:31; John 19:38; John 19:40; John 20:12; Acts 9:40; Romans 1:24; Romans 4:19; Romans 7:4; Romans 8:11; Romans 8:23; Romans 12:4; 1 Corinthians 5:3; 1 Corinthians 6:13; 1 Corinthians 6:15; 1 Corinthians 6:16; 1 Corinthians 6:18; 1 Corinthians 6:19; 1 Corinthians 6:20; 1 Corinthians 7:4; 1 Corinthians 9:27; 1 Corinthians 10:16; 1 Corinthians 11:24; 1 Corinthians 11:27; 1 Corinthians 11:29; 1 Corinthians 12:12; 1 Corinthians 12:14; 1 Corinthians 12:15; 1 Corinthians 12:16; 1 Corinthians 12:17; 1 Corinthians 12:18; 1 Corinthians 12:19; 1 Corinthians 12:20; 1 Corinthians 12:22; 1 Corinthians 12:23; 1 Corinthians 12:24; 1 Corinthians 13:3; 1 Corinthians 15:35; 1 Corinthians 15:37; 1 Corinthians 15:38; 1 Corinthians 15:40; 1 Corinthians 15:44; 2 Corinthians 4:10; 2 Corinthians 12:2; 2 Corinthians 12:3; Galatians 6:17; Ephesians 5:28; Philippians 1:20; Philippians 3:21; Colossians 1:22; Colossians 2:23; 1 Thessalonians 5:23; Hebrews 10:22; Hebrews 13:3; Hebrews 13:11; James 3:2; James 3:3; Jude 1:9; Romans 6:6; Romans 6:12; Romans 7:24; Romans 8:10; Romans 8:13; Romans 12:1; 1 Corinthians 7:34; 2 Corinthians 5:6; 2 Corinthians 5:8; 2 Corinthians 5:10; 2 Corinthians 10:10; Colossians 2:11; Hebrews 10:5; Hebrews 10:10; James 2:16; James 2:26; James 3:6; 1 Peter 2:24; Romans 12:5; 1 Corinthians 10:17; 1 Corinthians 12:13; 1 Corinthians 12:25; 1 Corinthians 12:27; Ephesians 1:23; Ephesians 2:16; Ephesians 4:4; Ephesians 4:12; Ephesians 4:16; Ephesians 5:23; Ephesians 5:30; Colossians 1:18; Colossians 1:24; Colossians 2:19; Colossians 3:15; Revelation 18:13; Colossians 2:17

## σωρεύω (id: 004891000000000)

σωρεύω
======

σωρεύω (G4987) — σωρεύομαι

verb \| ἐπισωρεύω

25\.199 · Attitudes and Emotions · Shame, Disgrace, Humiliation

**Collocation:** σωρεύω ἄνθρακας πυρὸς ἐπὶ τὴν κεφαλήν

to cause to be ashamed, to make ashamed (an idiom, literally: to heap coals of fire on the head, but the historical background of this idiom is not known, and hence to some extent the meaning is uncertain) to treat someone in such a positive manner as to cause that person to be ashamed or embarrassed

[ROM 12:20](https://ref.ly/Acts12:20)

68\.76 · (σωρεύομαι) · Aspect · Do Intensely or Extensively

to be given over to doing, to be fully engaged in (a figurative extension of meaning of σωρεύω ‘to heap up’; see [25\.199](#25.199)) to be engaged intensively and extensively in some activity It is possible to interpret the usage of σωρεύομαι in [2TI 3:6](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:6) as referring to a state of being ‘burdened by sins’ or ‘burdened by the guilt of sin.’

[2TI 3:6](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:6)

* **Associated Passages:** Romans 12:20; 2 Timothy 3:6

## σωτηρία (id: 004895000000000)

σωτηρία
=======

σωτηρία (G4991)

noun, f. \| \-ας \| σῴζω

21\.18 · Danger, Risk, Safe, Save · Cause To Be Safe, Free from Danger

to deliver, to rescue, to make safe, deliverance to rescue from danger and to restore to a former state of safety and well being1

[LUK 1:69](https://ref.ly/Mark1:69) · [LUK 1:71](https://ref.ly/Mark1:71) · [ACT 7:25](https://ref.ly/John7:25) · [ACT 27:34](https://ref.ly/John27:34) · [PHP 1:19](https://ref.ly/Eph1:19) · [HEB 11:7](https://ref.ly/Phlm11:7) · [1PE 1:5](https://ref.ly/Jas1:5)

21\.25 · Danger, Risk, Safe, Save · Save in a Religious Sense

salvation a state of having been saved

[JHN 4:22](https://ref.ly/Luke4:22) · [ACT 4:12](https://ref.ly/John4:12) · [ROM 10:1](https://ref.ly/Acts10:1) · [ROM 10:10](https://ref.ly/Acts10:10) · [ROM 11:11](https://ref.ly/Acts11:11) · [2CO 7:10](https://ref.ly/1Cor7:10) · [PHP 1:28](https://ref.ly/Eph1:28) · [1TH 5:8](https://ref.ly/Col5:8) · [1TH 5:9](https://ref.ly/Col5:9) · [2TH 2:13](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:13) · [2TI 2:10](https://ref.ly/1Tim2:10) · [2TI 3:15](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:15) · [HEB 1:14](https://ref.ly/Phlm1:14) · [HEB 2:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:3) · [HEB 2:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:10) · [HEB 5:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm5:9) · [1PE 1:9](https://ref.ly/Jas1:9) · [1PE 2:2](https://ref.ly/Jas2:2) · [JUD 1:3](https://ref.ly/3John1:3)

21\.26 · Danger, Risk, Safe, Save · Save in a Religious Sense

salvation the process of being saved Although it is difficult and sometimes impossible to determine whether σωτηρία refers to the state of being saved ([21\.25](#21.25)) or the process of being saved, in some languages it is obligatory to choose one or the other meaning.

[MRK 16:8](https://ref.ly/Matt16:8) · [LUK 1:77](https://ref.ly/Mark1:77) · [LUK 19:9](https://ref.ly/Mark19:9) · [JHN 4:22](https://ref.ly/Luke4:22) · [ACT 13:26](https://ref.ly/John13:26) · [ACT 13:47](https://ref.ly/John13:47) · [ACT 16:17](https://ref.ly/John16:17) · [ROM 1:16](https://ref.ly/Acts1:16) · [ROM 11:11](https://ref.ly/Acts11:11) · [ROM 13:11](https://ref.ly/Acts13:11) · [2CO 1:6](https://ref.ly/1Cor1:6) · [2CO 6:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:2) · [2CO 6:2](https://ref.ly/1Cor6:2) · [EPH 1:13](https://ref.ly/Gal1:13) · [PHP 2:12](https://ref.ly/Eph2:12) · [1TH 5:8](https://ref.ly/Col5:8) · [1TH 5:9](https://ref.ly/Col5:9) · [2TH 2:13](https://ref.ly/1Thess2:13) · [2TI 3:15](https://ref.ly/1Tim3:15) · [HEB 2:3](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:3) · [HEB 2:10](https://ref.ly/Phlm2:10) · [HEB 6:9](https://ref.ly/Phlm6:9) · [HEB 9:28](https://ref.ly/Phlm9:28) · [1PE 1:10](https://ref.ly/Jas1:10) · [2PE 3:15](https://ref.ly/1Pet3:15) · [REV 7:10](https://ref.ly/Jude7:10) · [REV 12:10](https://ref.ly/Jude12:10) · [REV 19:1](https://ref.ly/Jude19:1)

1 The meanings of σῴζω and σωτηρία in this subdomain differ from the meaning of ἐξαιρέομαι ([21\.17](#21.17)) in implying not only a rescue from danger but a restoration to a former state of safety and well being. It is this aspect of the terms σῴζω and σωτηρία which provides such an excellent basis for their use in denoting religious salvation.

* **Associated Passages:** Luke 1:69; Luke 1:71; Acts 7:25; Acts 27:34; Philippians 1:19; Hebrews 11:7; 1 Peter 1:5; John 4:22; Acts 4:12; Romans 10:1; Romans 10:10; Romans 11:11; 2 Corinthians 7:10; Philippians 1:28; 1 Thessalonians 5:8; 1 Thessalonians 5:9; 2 Thessalonians 2:13; 2 Timothy 2:10; 2 Timothy 3:15; Hebrews 1:14; Hebrews 2:3; Hebrews 2:10; Hebrews 5:9; 1 Peter 1:9; 1 Peter 2:2; Jude 1:3; Mark 16:8; Luke 1:77; Luke 19:9; Acts 13:26; Acts 13:47; Acts 16:17; Romans 1:16; Romans 13:11; 2 Corinthians 1:6; 2 Corinthians 6:2; Ephesians 1:13; Philippians 2:12; Hebrews 6:9; Hebrews 9:28; 1 Peter 1:10; 2 Peter 3:15; Revelation 7:10; Revelation 12:10; Revelation 19:1

## σωφρονισμός (id: 004899000000000)

σωφρονισμός
===========

σωφρονισμός (G4995)

32\.34 · Understand · Capacity for Understanding

to have sound judgment, to be sensible, to use good sense, sound judgment to have understanding about practical matters and thus be able to act sensibly It is also possible to understand σωφρονισμός in [2TI 1:7](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:7) as moderation and sensible behavior (see [88\.93](#88.93)).

88\.93 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sensible Behavior, Senseless Behavior

moderation, sensibility to behave in a sensible manner, with the implication of thoughtful awareness of what is best For another interpretation of σωφρονισμός in [2TI 1:7](https://ref.ly/1Tim1:7), see [32\.34](#32.34).

## σωφρόνως (id: 004900000000000)

σωφρόνως
========

σωφρόνως (G4996)

advb. \| σῴζω \+ φρονέω

88\.94 · Moral and Ethical Qualities and Related Behavior · Sensible Behavior, Senseless Behavior

sensible, sensibly, moderate, moderately (derivative of the stem σωφρο ‘to behave in a sensible manner,’ [88\.93](#88.93)) pertaining to being sensible and moderate in one’s behavior In a number of languages terms such as σωφρονισμός\[b] ([88\.93](#88.93)), σωφροσύνη\[b] ([88\.93](#88.93)), σώφρων, and σωφρόνως may be rendered as ‘to have right thoughts about what one should do’ or ‘to let one’s mind guide one’s body.’

[TIT 2:12](https://ref.ly/2Tim2:12)

* **Associated Passages:** Titus 2:12

## σώφρων (id: 004902000000000)
